And a Bedouin fell ill, and it was said to him, "You will die." He said, "Where will I be taken?" They said, "To Allah." He said, "Then why should I dislike going to One from whom no good is seen except from Him?" And Abu al-Mu'tamir ibn Sulayman said: My father, when death was present for him, said, "O Mu'tamir, relate to me the concessions (in religion), so that perhaps I will meet Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, while having good expectations of Him." And they recommended that the servant's good deeds be mentioned to him at his death so that he would have good expectations of his Lord.

(Explanation of the anguish upon meeting the Angel of Death, with narratives that express the state eloquently.)

Ash'ath ibn Aslam said: Ibrahim, peace be upon him, asked the Angel of Death—and his name is 'Azra'il, and he has two eyes, an eye in his face and an eye in the back of his head—and said, "O Angel of Death, what do you do when there is a soul in the east and a soul in the west, and a plague occurs in a land, and two armies meet in battle—how do you manage?" He said, "I call the souls by the permission of Allah, and they are between these two fingers of mine." And he said that the earth was flattened out for him so it became like a basin before him, from which he takes what he wills. He said this while giving him the glad tidings that he was the intimate friend of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic.

And Sulayman ibn Dawud, peace be upon them both, said to the Angel of Death, peace be upon him, "Why do I not see you being equitable among people? You take this one and leave that one." He said, "I am no more knowledgeable about that than you. They are merely scrolls or writings that are cast to me, containing the names."

And Wahb ibn Munabbih said: There was a king among kings who wanted to ride to a land. He called for garments to wear, but they did not please him, so he sought others until he wore what pleased him after several attempts. Likewise, he sought a mount, and one was brought to him, but it did not please him until mounts were brought, and he rode the finest of them. Then Iblis came and blew into his nostrils a breath that filled him with arrogance. Then he set out, and the horses went with him, and he did not look at the people out of arrogance.

A man of shabby appearance came to him, greeted him, but received no return of the greeting. So he seized the bridle of his mount. The man said, "Release the bridle, for I have undertaken a grave matter." He replied, "I have a need of you." The man said, "Wait until I dismount." He said, "No, now." So he compelled him by the bridle of his mount. The man said, "Shall I mention it?" He said, "It is a secret." So he drew his head near and whispered to him, saying, "I am the Angel of Death." The king's complexion changed and his tongue faltered. Then he said, "Let me return to my family, settle my affairs, and bid them farewell." He said, "No, by God, you shall never see your family and your burden again." So he seized his soul, and he fell as if he were a piece of wood. Then he departed.

He met a believing servant in that same state, greeted him, and the servant returned the greeting. He said, "I have a need of you; I shall mention it in your ear." He said, "Speak." So he whispered to him, saying, "I am the Angel of Death." He said, "Welcome and greetings to one whose absence has been long upon me. By God, there was no absent one on earth I longed to meet more than you." The Angel of Death said, "Fulfill the need for which you came out." He said, "I have no need greater to me, nor more beloved, than meeting God, the Exalted." He said, "Then choose in whatever state you wish for me to take your soul." He said, "Are you able to do that?" He said, "Yes, for I have been commanded to do so." He said, "Then let me perform ablution and pray, then take my soul while I am prostrating." So he took his soul while he was prostrating.

Abu Bakr ibn 'Abdullah al-Muzani said: A man from the Children of Israel gathered wealth. When he was on the verge of death, he said to his sons, "Show me the varieties of my wealth." So he was brought a great deal: horses, camels, slaves, and other things. When he looked at it, he wept in regret over it. The Angel of Death saw him weeping and said to him, "What makes you weep? By the One who bestowed it upon you, I shall not leave your house until I separate your soul from your body." He said, "Then a respite until I distribute it." He said, "Far be it! The respite has been cut off from you. If only you had done that before your appointed time arrived." So he seized his soul.

It is narrated that a man gathered wealth, amassing it, leaving no kind of wealth but that he acquired it. He built a palace and put upon it two sturdy doors, and gathered upon it guards from his servants. Then he gathered his family and prepared food for them, and sat upon his couch, raising one leg over the other while they were eating. When they finished, he said, "O my soul, enjoy yourself for years, for I have gathered for you what will suffice you." He had not finished his speech when the Angel of Death approached him in the form of a man wearing worn clothes, with a beggar's bag around his neck, resembling the poor. He knocked on the door with a mighty, alarming knock that startled him on his bed. The servants rushed to him and said, "What is your business?" He said, "Call me to your master." They said, "Should our master come out to the likes of you?" He said, "Yes." So they informed him of that. He said, "Why did you not do such and such to him?" He knocked on the door a knock stronger than the first. The guards rushed to him. He said, "Inform him that I am the Angel of Death." When they heard him, terror was cast upon them, and humility and awe fell upon their master. He said, "Speak to him gently, and say, 'Do you take anyone?'" He entered upon him and said, "Do with your wealth what you will do, for I shall not leave it until I take your soul." He ordered his wealth to be placed before him. When he saw it, he said, "May God curse you, O wealth! You distracted me from the worship of my Lord and prevented me from devoting myself to my Lord." God gave speech to the wealth, and it said, "Why do you curse me? You used to enter upon rulers through me, and the pious were turned away from their doors. You married luxurious women through me, sat in the gatherings of kings through me, and spent me in the path of evil, and I did not withhold from you. Had you spent me in the path of good, I would have benefited you. You were created, O son of Adam, from dust, so some are set free by righteousness and some by sin." Then the Angel of Death seized his soul, and he fell.

Wahb ibn Munabbih said: The Angel of Death seized the soul of a tyrant among tyrants, the like of whom was not on earth. Then he ascended to heaven. The angels said, "To whom were you more merciful than the one whose soul you just took?" He said, "I was commanded to take the soul of a woman in a wilderness on earth. I came to her and she had just given birth to a child. I had mercy on her for her isolation, and mercy on her child for its smallness and being in a wilderness with no one to care for it." The angels said, "The tyrant whose soul you just took is that very child upon whom you had mercy." The Angel of Death said, "Glory be to the Subtle One in what He wills."

'Atā' ibn Yasar said: When the night of the middle of Sha'ban comes, a scroll is given to the Angel of Death, and it is said, "Take in this year whoever is in this scroll." He said, "Verily, the servant may plant saplings, marry wives, and build buildings, while his name is in that scroll, and he does not know."

Al-Hasan said: There is no day except that the angel of the day inspects every house three times. Whoever he finds among them has received his provision fully and his term has ended, he takes his soul. When he takes his soul, his family comes forward with wailing and weeping. The Angel of Death takes hold of the doorposts and says, "By God, I did not consume his provision, nor did I exhaust his lifespan, nor did I diminish his term. And I shall return to you again and again until I leave none of you." Al-Hasan said, "By God, if they were to see his standing and hear his speech, they would be distracted from their dead and would weep for themselves." And Yazid said...

Al-Raqashi: While a tyrant among the tyrants of the Children of Israel was sitting in his home, secluded with some of his family, he saw a person enter through the door of his house. He sprang toward him in alarm and anger, saying, “Who are you, and who let you into my dwelling?” He replied, “As for the one who let me into the house, it is its Lord. As for me, I am the one who is not barred by any veil, nor do I seek permission from kings, nor do I fear the might of oppressors. No obstinate tyrant nor rebellious devil can keep me away.” The tyrant was struck dumb and trembled until he fell upon his face. Then he raised his head to him, pleading and humbling himself, and said, “Then you are the Angel of Death?” He said, “I am he.” He said, “Will you grant me respite so that I may make a will?” He said, “Far from it! Your term has ended, your breaths have been exhausted, and your hours have run out. There is no way to delay you.” He said, “Then where will you take me?” He said, “To the deeds you have sent ahead and to the home you have prepared.” He said, “But I have not sent ahead any righteous deeds, nor have I prepared a good home.” He said, “Then to the Blazing Fire that strips away the scalp!” Then he seized his soul, and he fell dead among his family, amid cries and weeping. Yazid al-Raqashi said: If they knew the evil of the destination, the wailing over that would be greater.

From al-A‘mash, from Khaythama, who said: The Angel of Death entered upon Solomon, son of David, peace be upon them, and he kept gazing at one of his companions, looking at him persistently. When he left, the man said, “Who is this?” He said, “This is the Angel of Death.” He said, “I saw him looking at me as if he wanted me.” He said, “What do you wish?” He said, “I wish that you would deliver me from him, so command the wind to carry me to the farthest part of India.” The wind did so. Then Solomon said to the Angel of Death after he came to him a second time, “I saw you gazing persistently at one of my companions.” He said, “Yes, I was amazed at him because I had been commanded to seize his soul in the farthest part of India at a near hour, and he was with you, so I was amazed at that.”

(The Fourth Chapter: On the Death of the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, and the Rightly Guided Caliphs after him – The Death of the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him)

Know that in the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, there is an excellent example, alive and deceased, in his actions, his words, and all his states—a lesson for the observers and an insight for the discerning. For no one was more honored by God than him, since he was the intimate friend of God, His beloved, His confidant, His chosen one, His Messenger, and His Prophet. So consider: was he granted any respite at the expiration of his term? Was he delayed for a moment after the arrival of his appointed time? No, rather the noble angels entrusted with seizing the souls of mankind were sent to him, and they hastened to take his pure, noble soul to transfer it. They struggled to remove it from his immaculate body to mercy, pleasure, and beautiful blessings—indeed, to a seat of truth in the proximity of the Merciful. Yet despite this, his anguish in the throes of death intensified, his groaning became apparent, his distress multiplied, his lament rose, his complexion changed, his brow sweated, and his left and right sides trembled with contraction and expansion, until those present wept for his passing and sobbed at the severity of his state. Have you seen the station of prophethood ward off from him what was decreed? Did the Angel show regard for him due to family or kin? Did he pardon him because he was a supporter of truth and a bearer of glad tidings and warnings to creation? Far from it! Rather, he complied with what he was commanded and followed what he found inscribed on the Preserved Tablet. This was his state, while he, with God, possesses the praiseworthy station and the pond to be drunk from, and he is the first for whom the earth will split open, and he is the possessor of intercession on the Day of Presentation. So it is astonishing that we do not take admonition from him, and we are not confident in what we will meet. Rather, we are captives of desires and companions of sins and misdeeds. Why do we not heed the demise of Muhammad, the master of the messengers, the leader of the God-fearing, the beloved of the Lord of the worlds? Perhaps we imagine that we are immortal, or we suppose that with our evil deeds we are honored by God! Far from it, far from it! Rather, we are certain that we will all enter the Fire, and none will be saved from it except the God-fearing. So we are certain of entering it, yet we imagine being saved from it. No, rather we have wronged ourselves if we, in such a state, are awaiting what is most likely. For by God, we are not among the God-fearing. And God, the Lord of the worlds, has said: “And there is none of you but will come to it. This is, with your Lord, a decree which must be accomplished. Then We will save those who feared God, and leave the wrongdoers therein, kneeling.” So let every servant look at his own soul: is he closer to the wrongdoers or to the God-fearing? Look at yourself after you have looked at the conduct of the righteous predecessors, for they, despite what they were granted, were among the fearful. Then look at the master of the messengers, for his affair was one of certainty, since he was the master of the prophets and the guide of the God-fearing. And reflect on how his anguish was at parting from the world and how severe his affair was when turning to the Garden of Abode! Ibn Mas‘ud, may God be pleased with him, said: We entered upon the Messenger of God, peace and blessings be upon him, in the house of our mother ‘A’ishah, may God be pleased with her, when the parting drew near. He looked at us, and his eyes, peace and blessings be upon him, filled with tears, then he said: “Welcome to you…”

May God grant you life, shelter you, and grant you victory. I enjoin upon you the fear of God, and God enjoins upon you concerning me. Verily, I am to you from Him a clear warner: that you do not exalt yourselves above God in His lands and over His servants. The appointed time has drawn near, and the return is to God, and to the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, and to the Garden of Refuge, and to the fullest cup. So convey upon yourselves, and upon those who enter your religion after me, peace from me and the mercy of God.

And it is narrated that he, peace be upon him, said to Gabriel, upon him be peace, at the time of his death: "Who will be for my community after me?" So God, Exalted is He, revealed to Gabriel: "Give glad tidings to My Beloved that I will not forsake him concerning his community. And give him glad tidings that he is the swiftest of people to emerge from the earth when they are resurrected, and their master when they are gathered, and that Paradise is forbidden to the nations until his community enters it." He said: "Now my eye is comforted."

And Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, commanded us to wash him with seven waterskins from seven wells. We did that, and he found relief. He went out and led the people in prayer, sought forgiveness for the people of Uhud and supplicated for them. And he enjoined concerning the Ansar, saying: 'Now then, O company of the Emigrants, you will increase, while the Ansar have become such that they will not increase beyond what they are today. Verily, the Ansar are my trusted shelter to which I resorted. So honor their honorable ones—meaning their doers of good—and overlook their wrongdoers.' Then he said: 'A servant was given the choice between this world and what is with God, and he chose what is with God.' Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, wept, thinking he meant himself. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Gently, O Abu Bakr. Block these streets leading to the mosque except the door of Abu Bakr, for I know of no one more excellent to me in companionship than Abu Bakr.'"

Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said: "He, peace be upon him, passed away in my house, on my day, between my chest and my throat, and God joined my saliva with his at the time of death. My brother Abd al-Rahman entered, and in his hand was a toothstick. He began to look at it, and I knew he desired it. I said to him: 'Shall I take it for you?' He indicated with his head, 'Yes.' I gave it to him, and he placed it in his mouth, but it was too hard for him. I said: 'Shall I soften it for you?' He indicated with his head, 'Yes.' So I softened it. There was a water vessel before him. He would dip his hand in it and say: 'There is no god but God. Indeed, death has its agonies.' Then he raised his hand, saying: 'The Highest Companion, the Highest Companion.' I said: 'Then, by God, he will not choose us.'"

And Sa'id ibn Abdullah narrated from his father, who said: "When the Ansar saw that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was growing increasingly weak, they gathered around the mosque. Al-Abbas, may God be pleased with him, entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and informed him of their presence and their concern. Then al-Fadl entered upon him and informed him of the same. Then Ali, may God be pleased with him, entered upon him and informed him likewise. He extended his hand and said: 'Here,' so they took hold of him. He said: 'What do you say?' They said: 'We say we fear you may die, and their women will wail due to the gathering of their men with the Prophet, peace be upon him.' The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, arose and went out, leaning on Ali and al-Fadl, with al-Abbas before him. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, had his head wrapped, dragging his feet until he sat on the lowest step of the pulpit. The people gathered to him. He praised God and extolled Him, then said: 'O people, it has reached me that you fear death, as if you find the death of your Prophet strange. What do you find strange about the death of your Prophet? Did I not convey to you, and were your own souls not conveyed to you? Did any prophet before me remain forever among the people to whom he was sent, so that I should remain forever among you? Verily, I am going to my Lord, and you are going to Him. I enjoin you to treat the first Emigrants well, and I enjoin the Emigrants concerning their relations among themselves, for God, Mighty and Majestic, has said: "By time, indeed mankind is in loss, except for those who have believed..." to its end. Matters proceed by God's permission, so let not the delay of a matter lead you to hasten it, for God, Mighty and Majestic, is not hastened by anyone's haste. Whoever contends with God, He will overcome him; whoever tries to deceive God, He will deceive him. "Then is it to be expected of you, if you turn away, that you will cause corruption on earth and sever your [ties of] kinship?" I enjoin you to treat the Ansar well, for they are the ones who settled the Home and [embraced] faith before you, that you be good to them. Did they not share their fruits with you? Did they not make room for you in their dwellings? Did they not prefer you over themselves, even while in need? Verily, whoever is appointed to judge between two men, let him accept from their doers of good and overlook their wrongdoers. Do not withhold from them. Verily, I am your forerunner, and you will come to me. Verily, your appointed place is the Pool—my Pool—wider than the distance between Busra in Syria and Sana'a in Yemen. The spout of al-Kawthar pours into it. Its water is whiter than milk, softer than foam, and sweeter than honey. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. Its pebbles are pearls, and its soil is musk. Whoever is deprived of it on the Day of Standing is deprived of all good. So whoever loves to meet me at it tomorrow, let him restrain his tongue and his hand from all but what is right.' Al-Abbas said: 'O Prophet of God, enjoin concerning Quraysh.' He said: 'I only enjoin this matter to Quraysh, and the people follow Quraysh: their righteous for their righteous, and their wicked for their wicked. So enjoin the family of Quraysh to treat the people well. O people, sins change blessings.'"

And the condition changes, so when people are righteous, their leaders are righteous, and when people are corrupt, their intellects are corrupted. God Almighty says: "Thus do We make the wrongdoers allies of one another for what they have earned." (6:129) And Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him, reported that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him: "Ask, O Abu Bakr." He said: "O Messenger of God, the appointed time has drawn near." He said: "Indeed, the appointed time has drawn near and is descending." He said: "May what is with God delight you, O Prophet of God! I wonder about our return." He said: "To God, and to the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, then to the Garden of Refuge and the Highest Paradise, and the fullest cup, and the Highest Companion, and the share and the pleasant life." He said: "O Prophet of God, who will wash you?" He said: "Men from my closest family, then the next closest." He said: "In what shall we shroud you?" He said: "In these garments of mine, and in a Yemeni garment, and in the white cloth of Egypt." He said: "How shall we pray over you, while we weep?" And he wept. Then he said: "Gently, may God forgive you and reward you well on behalf of your Prophet. When you have washed me and shrouded me, place me on my bed in this house of mine, at the edge of my grave. Then withdraw from me for a while, for the first to pray over me will be God, Mighty and Majestic, 'It is He who confers blessing upon you, and His angels.' (33:43) Then He will grant the angels permission to pray over me. So the first of God's creation to enter upon me and pray over me will be Gabriel, then Michael, then Israfil, then the Angel of Death with many troops, then all the angels together, may God's blessings be upon them all. Then you, enter upon me in groups and pray over me in groups, company by company, and give salutations of peace, and do not harm me with loud praise, or outcry, or wailing. Let the Imam and my closest family, then the next closest, begin among you, then groups of women, then groups of children." He said: "Who will place you in the grave?" He said: "A company from my closest family, then the next closest, along with many angels whom you will not see, but they will see you. Rise and convey from me to those after me."

And Abdullah ibn Zam'ah said: "Bilal came at the beginning of the month of Rabi' al-Awwal and gave the call to prayer. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' I went out and saw no one at the door except Umar among men, and Abu Bakr was not among them. I said: 'Stand, O Umar, and lead the people in prayer.' Umar stood, and when he said the takbir—and he was a man with a loud voice—the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, heard his voice with the takbir and said: 'Where is Abu Bakr? God refuses that, and so do the Muslims.' He said it three times: 'Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said: 'O Messenger of God, Abu Bakr is a man of tender heart; when he stands in your place, weeping overcomes him.' He said: 'You are like the companions of Joseph. Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' He said: So Abu Bakr led the prayer after the prayer that Umar had led. And Umar would later say to Abdullah ibn Zam'ah: 'Woe to you, what have you done to me? By God, had I not thought that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, commanded you, I would not have done it.' And Abdullah would say: 'I saw no one more deserving of that than you.' Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said: 'I did not say that, nor divert it from Abu Bakr, except out of desire for him to turn away from this world, and because of the peril and destruction in leadership except for whom God protects. I also feared that people might not love a man who led prayer in the place of the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was still alive, unless God wills, and they would envy him, bear malice against him, and consider him an ill omen. So indeed, the command is God's command, and the decree is His decree, and God protected him from everything I feared for him in matters of this world and religion.'"

And Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said: "When the day came on which the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, died, they saw lightness in him at the beginning of the day, so the men dispersed to their homes and their needs, rejoicing, and they left the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, with the women. While we were in that state—not in our usual state of hope and joy before that—the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Let everyone leave me; this angel seeks permission to enter upon me.' Everyone in the house left except me, and his head was in my lap. He sat up, and I withdrew to a corner of the house. The angel conversed with him at length. Then he called me and placed his head back in my lap and said to the women: 'Enter.' I said: 'This is not the presence of Gabriel, peace be upon him.' The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Yes, O Aisha, this is the Angel of Death. He came to me and said: "Indeed, God, Mighty and Majestic, has sent me and commanded me not to enter upon you except with your permission. If you do not permit me, I will return, and if you permit me, I will enter. And He commanded me not to take your soul until you command me." So what do you command?' I said: 'Hold back from me until Gabriel, peace be upon him, comes to me, for this is the hour of Gabriel.'" Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said: "We were faced with a matter for which we had no answer or opinion, and we were stunned, as if struck by a deafening blow; we could not think of anything, and no one in the household spoke out of reverence for that matter and an awe that filled our hearts." She said: "Gabriel came at his hour and gave salutations. I recognized his presence, and the household left. He entered and said: 'Indeed, God, Mighty and Majestic, conveys His greetings to you and says: "How do you find yourself?"—and He knows best what you are experiencing—but He wished to increase you in honor and nobility.'"

And that your honor and nobility over creation be perfected, and that it become a sunnah for your community. He said, "I feel pain." He said, "Rejoice, for Allah the Exalted intends to grant you what He has prepared for you." He said, "O Gabriel, the Angel of Death has sought permission to enter upon me," and he informed him of the matter. Gabriel said, "O Muhammad, your Lord longs for you. Did He not inform you of what He intends for you? No, by Allah the Exalted, the Angel of Death has never sought permission to enter upon anyone, nor will he ever seek permission, except that your Lord is perfecting your nobility and He longs for you." He said, "Then do not leave until he comes." And he gave permission for the women. He said, "O Fatimah, come near." So she leaned over him, and he whispered to her. She raised her head, her eyes weeping, unable to speak. Then he said, "Bring your head near to me." So she leaned over him, and he whispered to her. She raised her head, laughing, unable to speak. What we saw from her was astonishing. I asked her about it afterward, and she said, "He informed me and said, 'I will die today,' so I wept. Then he said, 'I supplicated to Allah to join you with me as the first of my family and to place you with me,' so I laughed." And she brought her two sons near to him, and he smelled them. She said, "And the Angel of Death came and sought permission, and permission was granted to him. The angel said, 'What do you command us, O Muhammad?' He said, 'Join me with my Lord now.' He said, 'Yes, from this day of yours. Indeed, your Lord longs for you. He has not hesitated over anyone as He hesitated over you, nor has He forbidden me from entering upon anyone without permission except you. But your hour is before you.' And he left." She said, "And Gabriel came and said, 'Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah. This is the last of what is revealed to me on earth forever. Revelation is rolled up, and the world is rolled up. I have no need on earth except you, and I have no need therein except your presence, then adhering to my station.' No, by the One who sent Muhammad with the truth, there was no one in the house able to utter a word to him in that, nor could anyone be sent to any of his men due to the greatness of what they heard from his speech and what we found and our apprehension." She said, "I went to the Prophet (peace be upon him) until I placed his head between my breasts and held his chest. He began to lose consciousness until it overcame him, and his forehead exuded a sweat I have never seen from any human. I began to wipe that sweat, and I never found the scent of anything more pleasant than it. I would say to him when he regained consciousness, 'May my father and mother, my soul and my family be sacrificed for you, what is this sweat on your forehead?' He said, 'O Aisha, the soul of the believer exits with sweat, and the soul of the disbeliever exits from his jaws like the braying of a donkey.' At that, we were alarmed and sent for our families. The first man to come to us, and my brother did not witness it, he sent to my father. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died before anyone came. Indeed, Allah only kept them away from him because He entrusted him to Gabriel and Michael." And when he would lose consciousness, he would say, "Rather, the Highest Companion," as if the choice were presented to him. And when he was able to speak, he said, "The prayer, the prayer. You will remain united as long as you pray together. The prayer, the prayer." He kept enjoining it until he died, saying, "The prayer, the prayer." Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said, "The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died between the rising of the forenoon and midday on Monday." Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with her) said, "What I have encountered from Monday! By Allah, the community will continue to be afflicted in it by a great calamity." And Umm Kulthum said on the day Ali (may Allah honor his face) was struck in Kufa, like her, "What I have encountered from Monday! The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died on it, and on it Ali (may Allah honor him) was killed, and on it my father was killed. What I have encountered from Monday!" And Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said, "When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) died, the people rushed in when the wailing rose, and the angels shrouded the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with a garment. They differed: some denied his death, some were struck dumb and did not speak except after a long time, others were confused and mixed speech without clarity, and others remained with their intellects intact, and others sat down. Umar ibn al-Khattab was among those who denied his death, Ali was among those who sat down, and Uthman was among those struck dumb. Umar went out to the people and said, 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has not died. Allah Almighty will return him, and He will cut off the hands and feet of men among the hypocrites who wish death for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Allah Almighty only promised him as He promised Moses, and He is coming to you.'" In another narration, he said, "O people, restrain your tongues regarding the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), for he has not died. By Allah, I will not hear anyone mention that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has died except that I strike him with this sword of mine." As for Ali, he sat down and did not leave the house. As for Uthman, he began not to speak to anyone; he would be taken by the hand, brought and taken away. And no one among the Muslims was in a state like Abu Bakr and al-Abbas, for Allah Almighty supported them with success and correctness. And the people did not come to their senses except by the words of Abu Bakr, until al-Abbas came and said, "By Allah, besides whom there is no god, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) has indeed tasted death, and he said while among you, 'Indeed, you are to die, and indeed they are to die. Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, before your Lord, will dispute.'" And the news reached Abu Bakr while he was with the Banu al-Harith ibn al-Khazraj, so he came and entered upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).

He looked upon him, then leaned over and kissed him, saying, "May my father and mother be your ransom, O Messenger of God! God Almighty would not make you taste death twice. By God, the Messenger of God has indeed passed away." Then he went out to the people and said, "O people! Whoever worshipped Muhammad, Muhammad has died. But whoever worships the Lord of Muhammad, He is Ever-Living and does not die." God Almighty says: "Muhammad is but a messenger; messengers have passed away before him. If he were to die or be killed, would you turn back on your heels?" It was as if the people had never heard this verse until that day.

In another narration: When Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, received the news, he entered the house of the Messenger of God while he was laid out, and his eyes overflowed, his sobs rising like the bubbling of a water-skin. Yet in that state, he was firm in action and speech. He leaned over him, uncovered his face, kissed his forehead and cheeks, wiped his face, and wept, saying, "May my father and mother, my soul, and my family be your ransom! You were pure in life and in death. What was severed by your death was not severed by the death of any other prophet. Prophethood is too immense to be described, too majestic for weeping. You were singled out until you became a consolation, and made universal until we became equal in you. Had your death not been by your own choice, we would have expended our very souls in grief for you. Had you not forbidden weeping, we would have poured forth our tears upon you. As for what we cannot dispel from ourselves—sorrow and remembrance are two companions that do not depart. O God, convey to him from us: Remember us, O Muhammad, before your Lord, and keep us in your thoughts. Were it not for the tranquility you left behind, no one could have endured the desolation you left. O God, convey to Your Prophet from us, and preserve him among us."

From Ibn 'Umar: When Abu Bakr entered the house, prayed, and praised, the household wailed loudly, a lament heard by those in the prayer area. Whenever he mentioned something, they increased in weeping. Their wailing did not cease until a man at the door, with a strong, clear voice, gave salutations, saying, "Peace be upon you, O people of the house. 'Every soul will taste death.' In God is a successor to everyone, a fulfillment for every desire, and salvation from every fear. So place your hope in God Almighty, trust in Him, listen to Him, and reject this, and cease weeping." When the weeping stopped, his voice faded. One of them looked out but saw no one. Then they returned to weeping. Another caller, whose voice they did not recognize, called to them, "O people of the house, remember God Almighty and praise Him in every state, that you may be among the sincere. In God is solace for every affliction and compensation for every loss. So obey God and act by His command." Abu Bakr said, "This was Al-Khidr and Al-Yasa', peace be upon them, attending the Prophet."

Al-Qa'qa' ibn 'Amr fully recounted the account of Abu Bakr's sermon: Abu Bakr stood to address the people after they had spent their tears in a sermon that was largely prayers upon the Prophet. He praised God and extolled Him in every circumstance, saying, "I bear witness that there is no god but God alone. He fulfilled His promise, aided His servant, and alone defeated the confederates. Praise belongs to God alone. And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, the seal of His prophets. I bear witness that the Book is as He legislated, the religion as He established, the narration as he related, and the word as he spoke, and that God is the Manifest Truth. O God, send blessings upon Muhammad, Your servant, Messenger, Prophet, beloved, trusted one, chosen one, and elect, with the best blessings You have sent upon any of Your creation. O God, make Your blessings, Your pardon, and Your mercy upon the master of messengers, the seal of prophets, the imam of the God-fearing, Muhammad, the leader of good, the imam of good, the messenger of mercy. O God, bring near his intercession, magnify his proof, honor his station, and resurrect him to a praiseworthy station envied by the first and the last. Benefit us by his praiseworthy station on the Day of Resurrection, and appoint him as our successor in this world and the next. Grant him the highest rank and the means of nearness in Paradise. O God, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, and bestow favor upon Muhammad and the family of Muhammad, as You blessed and bestowed favor upon Abraham. Indeed, You are Praiseworthy, Glorious.

O people, whoever worshipped Muhammad, Muhammad has died. But whoever worships God, God is Ever-Living and does not die. God has presented to you His decree, so do not abandon it in panic. For God Almighty chose for His Prophet what is with Him over what is with you, and took him to His reward, leaving among you His Book and the Sunnah of His Prophet. Whoever takes hold of them will know, and whoever separates between them will be led astray. 'O you who believe, be upholders of justice.' Let not Satan distract you with the death of your Prophet, nor tempt you away from your religion. Confront Satan with good and you will overcome him; do not grant him respite, lest he overtake you and tempt you."

Ibn 'Abbas said: When Abu Bakr finished his sermon, he said, "O 'Umar, I was told that you said, 'The Prophet of God has not died.' Do you not see that the Prophet of God said on such-and-such day such-and-such, and on such-and-such day such-and-such? And God says in His Book: 'Indeed, you are to die, and indeed, they are to die.'" He replied, "By God, it is as if I had never heard it in the Book of God until now, when this befell us. I bear witness that..."

The Book as it was revealed, and the Hadith as it was narrated, and that God is Ever-Living, He does not die. "Indeed, to God we belong and to Him we shall return." And may the blessings of God be upon His Messenger, and with God we place our trust in His Messenger. Then he sat with Abu Bakr.

And 'A'isha, may God be pleased with her, said: When they gathered to wash him, they said, "By God, we do not know how to wash the Messenger of God. Should we remove his garments as we do with our dead, or wash him in his garments?" She said: Then God sent sleep upon them until there remained not a man among them except that his chin was upon his chest, sleeping. Then a speaker, whom none knew, said, "Wash the Messenger of God in his garments." They awoke and did so, washing the Messenger of God in his shirt. When they finished washing him, they shrouded him. And 'Ali, may God honor his face, said, "We intended to remove his shirt, but we were called to, 'Do not remove the garments from the Messenger of God.' So we left it and washed him in his shirt as we wash our dead, lying on his back. We did not wish to turn any limb of his for us except that it was turned for us without any force until we finished with him. And indeed, with us in the house was a rustling like a gentle wind, and a voice called to us, 'Be gentle with the Messenger of God, for you will soon shroud him.'" Thus was the passing of the Messenger of God, and he left neither a coarse mat nor a felt mat except that it was buried with him. Abu Ja'far said: His grave was spread with his bedding and his woolen blanket, and his garments which he wore while awake were spread upon the woolen blanket and bedding. Then he was placed upon them in his shrouds. He left behind no wealth after his passing, nor did he, during his life, build brick upon brick or place reed upon reed. In his passing is a complete lesson, and for the Muslims in him is an excellent example.

(On the passing of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may God be pleased with him)
When Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, was nearing death, 'A'isha, may God be pleased with her, came and recited this verse:
"By your life, wealth does not avail a young man, when the death rattle comes one day and the chest is constricted by it."
He uncovered his face and said, "Not like that, but say: 'And the stupor of death comes with the truth; that is what you were avoiding.' Look at these two garments of mine; wash them and shroud me in them, for the living have more need of new garments than the dead." And 'A'isha, may God be pleased with her, said at the time of his death:
"And a fair-faced one by whose countenance the clouds are besought for rain, the springtime of orphans, a protection for widows."
Abu Bakr said, "That is the Messenger of God." They entered upon him and said, "Shall we not call a physician to examine you?" He said, "He has already examined me, my Physician, and said, 'Indeed, I do what I will.'" And Salman al-Farsi, may God be pleased with him, entered upon him to visit him and said, "O Abu Bakr, counsel us." He said, "Indeed, God is opening the world to you, so take from it only what suffices you. And know that whoever prays the dawn prayer is under the protection of God, so do not betray God in His protection, lest He cast you into the Fire on your face." And when Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, became gravely ill and the people wanted him to appoint a successor, he appointed 'Umar, may God be pleased with him. The people said to him, "You have appointed over us a harsh and severe man. What will you say to your Lord?" He said, "I will say, 'I appointed the best of Your creation over Your creation.'" Then he sent for 'Umar, may God be pleased with him, and he came. He said, "I counsel you with a counsel. Know that God has a right in the daytime which He does not accept in the night, and a right in the night which He does not accept in the daytime, and He does not accept supererogatory acts until the obligatory acts are fulfilled. Indeed, the scales of those whose scales are heavy on the Day of Resurrection are heavy only because they followed the truth in the world and it was heavy upon them. And it is fitting for a scale in which nothing but the truth is placed to be heavy. Indeed, the scales of those whose scales are light on the Day of Resurrection are light only because they followed falsehood and it was light upon them. And it is fitting for a scale in which nothing but falsehood is placed to be light. And God mentions the people of Paradise by their best deeds and overlooks their evil deeds. So a person will say, 'I am less than these, and I do not reach the station of the righteous deeds they performed.' And another will say, 'I am better than these.' And God mentions the verse of mercy and the verse of punishment so that the believer may be desirous and fearful, and not cast himself with his own hands into destruction, nor wish upon God other than the truth. If you preserve this counsel of mine, then let no absent thing be more beloved to you than death, for you must meet it. And if you neglect my counsel, then let no absent thing be more hateful to you than death, for you must meet it, and you cannot escape it."

And Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib said: When Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, was nearing death, a group of the Companions came to him and said, "O Successor of the Messenger of God, provide us provision, for we see what is with you." Abu Bakr said, "Whoever says these words and then dies, God will place his soul in the Clear Horizon." They said, "And what is the Clear Horizon?" He said, "A plain before the Throne, in which are the gardens, rivers, and trees of God, visited every day by a hundred mercies. So whoever says this statement, God will place his soul in this place: 'O God, You originated creation without any need of them from You. Then You made them two parties: a party for bliss and a party for the Blaze. So make me...'"

For bliss, and do not make me for the Blaze. O Allah, You created creation in divisions and distinguished them before You created them, making among them the wretched and the fortunate, the misguided and the rightly guided, so do not make me wretched through disobedience to You. O Allah, You knew what every soul would earn before You created it, and there is no escape for it from what You foreknew, so make me among those whom You employ in Your obedience. O Allah, none wills until You will, so make Your will that I will what brings me nearer to You. O Allah, You have decreed the movements of Your servants, and nothing moves except by Your leave, so make my movements in reverence of You. O Allah, You created good and evil and appointed for each a worker to perform it, so make me from the better of the two divisions. O Allah, You created Paradise and the Fire and appointed for each its inhabitants, so make me among the dwellers of Your Paradise. O Allah, You willed misguidance for a people and constricted their hearts with it, so expand my heart for faith and adorn it within my heart. O Allah, You manage all affairs and have made their final end to You, so grant me life after death a goodly life and draw me near to You in closeness. O Allah, whoever begins his morning and evening with his trust and hope in other than You—You are my trust and my hope, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah. Abu Bakr said: All of this is in the Book of Allah, the Mighty, the Majestic.

(The Passing of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him)
'Amr ibn Maymun said: I was standing on the morning 'Umar was struck, with none between him and me except 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas. When he would pass between the rows, he would stand between them, and if he saw a gap he would say, "Straighten the rows," until he saw no gap. Then he would not proceed forward until he said the Takbir. He said: Sometimes he would recite Surah Yusuf or Surah an-Nahl or the like in the first Rak'ah until the people gathered. It was only when he said the Takbir that I heard him say, "The dog has killed me—or eaten me," when Abu Lu'lu'ah stabbed him. The non-Arab man dashed with a double-edged dagger, stabbing anyone to his right or left until he had stabbed thirteen men, of whom nine died—in one narration, seven. When a Muslim man saw this, he threw a cloak over him. When the non-Arab man thought he was captured, he slit his own throat. 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, took hold of 'Abdur-Rahman ibn 'Awf and placed him forward. As for those near 'Umar, they saw what I saw, but those in other parts of the mosque did not know what had happened; they only missed 'Umar's voice and were saying, "Subhanallah, Subhanallah." 'Abdur-Rahman led them in a brief prayer. When they finished, he said, "O Ibn 'Abbas, see who has struck me." He went away for a while and then returned and said, "The slave of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah." 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, said, "May Allah fight him! I had indeed enjoined good treatment upon him." Then he said, "Praise be to Allah who did not make my death at the hand of a man who professes Islam. You and your father used to desire that non-Arabs increase in al-Madinah, and al-'Abbas had the most slaves among them." Ibn 'Abbas said, "If you wish, I will do it," meaning, "If you wish, I will kill them." He said, "After they have spoken your language, prayed toward your Qiblah, and performed your Hajj?" He was carried to his house, and we went with him. He said: It was as if the people had not been struck by a calamity before that day. Some were saying, "I fear for him," and others saying, "It is nothing." He was brought some Nabidh (a drink) and drank it, but it came out from his wound. Then he was brought milk and drank it, and it came out from his wound, so they knew he would die. He said: We entered upon him, and people came praising him. A young man came and said, "Receive glad tidings, O Commander of the Faithful, of good news from Allah, the Mighty, the Majestic. You had companionship with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and precedence in Islam as is known. Then you assumed leadership and were just. Then, martyrdom." He said, "I wish that would be just sufficient, neither against me nor for me." When the man turned to leave, his lower garment was touching the ground. He said, "Bring the young man back to me." He said, "O my nephew, raise your garment, for it is cleaner for your garment and more pious toward your Lord." Then he said, "O 'Abdullah, see what debt is upon me." They calculated it and found it to be about eighty-six thousand. He said, "If the wealth of the family of 'Umar suffices, then repay it from their wealth. If not, then ask among Banu 'Adi ibn Ka'b. If their wealth does not suffice, then ask among Quraysh, and do not go beyond them. Repay this debt on my behalf. Go to the Mother of the Believers, 'Aishah, and say, ''Umar sends you greetings of peace,' and do not say 'the Commander of the Faithful,' for I am not today the commander of the believers. Say, 'He asks permission for 'Umar ibn al-Khattab to be buried with his two companions.'" 'Abdullah went, gave greetings, sought permission, and entered upon her. He found her sitting and weeping. He said, "'Umar ibn al-Khattab sends you greetings of peace and asks permission to be buried with his two companions." She said, "I had desired it for myself, but I would prefer him over myself today." When he returned, it was said, "Here is 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar coming." He said, "Lift me up." A man supported him against himself. He said, "What news do you have?" He said, "What you love, O Commander of the Faithful. She has given permission." He said, "Praise be to Allah. Nothing was more important to me than that. When I am taken, carry me, then give greetings and say, ''Umar seeks permission.' If she permits me, then enter me. If she turns me back, then return me to the graveyard of the Muslims." And Umm al-Mu'minin Hafṣah came...

The women were covering her, and when we saw her, we rose, and she entered upon him. She remained with him for a while, then the men sought permission and entered inside. We heard her weeping from within, and they said, "Offer your testament, O Commander of the Faithful, and appoint a successor." He said, "I do not see anyone more deserving of this matter than these men, with whom the Messenger of God ﷺ was pleased at the time of his passing." He named Ali, Uthman, al-Zubayr, Talha, Sa'd, and Abd al-Rahman, and said, "Let Abdullah ibn Umar bear witness among you, though he has no share in the command, as a form of consolation for him. If leadership falls to Sa'd, then so be it; otherwise, let whichever of you is appointed seek his aid, for I have not exempted him due to incapacity or betrayal." And he said, "I enjoin the Caliph after me to treat the early Emigrants well, to acknowledge their merit and preserve their sanctity. I enjoin him to treat the Ansar well—those who settled the abode and faith before them—to accept from their doers of good and pardon their wrongdoers. I enjoin him to treat the people of the garrison towns well, for they are the support of Islam, the collectors of wealth, and the vexation of the enemy, and that he take from them only their surplus willingly. I enjoin him to treat the Bedouins well, for they are the root of the Arabs and the substance of Islam, and that he take from the fringes of their wealth and return it to their poor. I enjoin him by the covenant of God Almighty and the covenant of His Messenger ﷺ to fulfill their pact, to fight on their behalf from behind them, and not to burden them beyond their capacity." He said: When he passed away, we carried him out and proceeded walking. Abdullah ibn Umar gave salutations and sought permission for Umar ibn al-Khattab. She said, "Admit him," and he was admitted to a place there with his two companions.

The Hadith: From the Prophet ﷺ, he said: "Gabriel, peace be upon him, said to me: 'Let Islam weep for the death of Umar.'" And from Ibn Abbas, he said: Umar was placed on his bed, and people surrounded him supplicating and praying before he was raised, and I was among them. Suddenly, I felt a man take me by my shoulder, and I turned to find Ali ibn Abi Talib, may God be pleased with him. He invoked mercy upon Umar and said, "I have left no one whose deeds I would more love to meet God with than yours. By God, I indeed used to think that God would place you with your two companions, for I often heard the Prophet ﷺ say: 'I and Abu Bakr and Umar went; I and Abu Bakr and Umar went out; I and Abu Bakr and Umar entered.' Thus, I hoped—indeed, I thought—that God would place you with them."

(The Passing of Uthman, may God be pleased with him)
The Hadith concerning his killing is well-known. Abdullah ibn Salam said: I came to my brother Uthman to greet him while he was under siege. I entered upon him, and he said, "Welcome, my brother. I saw the Messenger of God ﷺ tonight at this small window—a window in the house." He said, "O Uthman, have they besieged you?" I said, "Yes." He said, "Have they made you thirsty?" I said, "Yes." Then he lowered to me a bucket containing water, and I drank until I was quenched, to the point that I still feel its coolness between my chest and my shoulders. And he said to me, "If you wish, I will grant you victory over them, and if you wish, you may break your fast with us." I chose to break my fast with him, and he was killed that day, may God be pleased with him. And Abdullah ibn Salam said to those present while Uthman was struggling in death when wounded, "What did Uthman say as he struggled?" They said, "We heard him say: 'O God, unite the community of Muhammad ﷺ' three times." He said, "By the One in whose hand is my soul, had he prayed to God that they never unite, they would not have united until the Day of Resurrection." And from Thamama ibn Hazn al-Qushayri, he said: I witnessed the house when Uthman, may God be pleased with him, appeared to them and said, "Bring me your two companions who incited you." He said: They were brought as if they were two lambs or two donkeys. Uthman, may God be pleased with him, appeared to them and said, "I adjure you by God and Islam, do you not know that when the Messenger of God ﷺ arrived in Medina, there was no sweet water to drink except the well of Rumah? He said, 'Whoever buys Rumah and places his bucket with the buckets of the Muslims will have better than it in Paradise,' so I bought it with my own wealth. And today you prevent me from drinking from it, even from the water of the sea?" They said, "O God, yes." He said, "I adjure you by God and Islam, do you not know that I equipped the army of hardship from my wealth?" They said, "Yes." He said, "I adjure you by God and Islam, do you not know that the mosque became too narrow for its people, and the Messenger of God ﷺ said, 'Whoever buys the plot of so-and-so to add it to the mosque will have better than it in Paradise,' so I bought it with my own wealth. And today you prevent me from praying two rak'ahs in it?" They said, "O God, yes." He said, "I adjure you by God and Islam, do you not know that the Messenger of God ﷺ was upon Thabir in Mecca, with Abu Bakr, Umar, and I, and the mountain shook until its stones fell into the valley? He struck it with his foot and said, 'Be still, O Thabir, for upon you are only a Prophet, a truthful one, and two martyrs.'" They said, "O God, yes." He said, "God is greatest! They have borne witness for me, and by the Lord of the Kaaba, I am a martyr." And it is narrated from a shaykh of the tribe of Dabba that when Uthman was struck and blood flowed upon his beard, he kept saying, "There is no god but You, glory be to You, indeed I have been among the wrongdoers. O God, I seek Your aid against them, and I seek Your help in all my affairs, and I ask You for patience with what You have tested me."

(The Passing of Ali, may God honor his countenance)
Al-Asbagh al-Hanzali said: On the night in which Ali, may God honor his countenance, was struck down, Ibn al-Tiyyah came to him at the break of dawn to call him to prayer. He found him lying down, sluggish. He returned a second time and found him the same. Then he returned a third time, and Ali rose, walking while saying:
      "Gird your loins for death, for death shall come to you.
      And do not be dismayed by death when it descends upon your valley."
When he reached the small door, Ibn Muljam assailed him and struck him. Umm Kulthum, the daughter of Ali, may God be pleased with him and her, came out and began to say, "What is the dawn prayer to me now? The dawn prayer has killed my husband, the Commander of the Faithful! The dawn prayer has killed my father!" And from a shaykh of Quraysh: When Ali, may God honor his countenance, was struck by Ibn Muljam, he said, "I have succeeded, by the Lord of the Ka'ba!" And from Muhammad ibn Ali: When he was struck, he instructed his sons, then spoke nothing but 'There is no god but God' until he passed away. And when al-Hasan ibn Ali, may God be pleased with them both, grew gravely ill, al-Husayn, may God be pleased with him, entered upon him and said, "O my brother, why are you dismayed? You are going forward to meet the Messenger of God ﷺ and Ali ibn Abi Talib, and they are your two fathers; and to Khadijah bint Khuwaylid and Fatimah bint Muhammad, and they are your two mothers; and to Hamzah and Ja'far, and they are your two uncles." He said, "O my brother, I am going forward to a matter the like of which I have never gone forward to before." And from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, may God be pleased with them both, who said: When the people descended upon al-Husayn, may God be pleased with him, and he became certain they would kill him, he stood among his companions and delivered a sermon. He praised God and extolled Him, then said, "That which you see has now come to pass. The world has changed and become alien, its good has turned its back and shriveled away until nothing remains of it but like the dregs in a vessel. Is not an existence like blighted pasture enough for me? Do you not see that right is not acted upon and wrong is not refrained from? So let the believer yearn for the meeting with God, the Exalted. I see death as nothing but felicity, and life with the wrongdoers as nothing but sin."

       (Chapter Five: On the Words of the Dying among the Caliphs, Commanders, and the Righteous)
When the death of Mu'awiyah ibn Abi Sufyan approached, he said, "Sit me up." They sat him up, and he began to glorify God, the Exalted, and remember Him. Then he wept and said, "Remember your Lord, O Mu'awiyah, after old age and decline? Would that this were so, and the branch of youth fresh and succulent!" And he wept until his weeping grew loud, and said, "O Lord, have mercy on the sinful old man with the hard heart. O God, pardon the stumble, forgive the slip, and treat with Your forbearance one who hopes in none but You and trusts in no one besides You." It is narrated from a shaykh of Quraysh that he entered upon him with a group during his illness, and they saw wrinkles upon his skin. He praised God and extolled Him, then said, "As for what follows: Is the entire world anything but what we have experienced and seen? By God, we faced its bloom with our earnestness and our delight in our living, but the world did not tarry long before it stripped that from us, state after state, bond after bond, until the world rose having betrayed us, failed us, and become hostile to us. Fie upon the world as an abode! Then fie upon it as an abode!" And it is narrated that the last sermon Mu'awiyah delivered, he said: "O people, I am from a crop that has fully ripened. I have governed you, and none shall govern you after me except one worse than me, just as those before me were better than me. And O Yazid, when my term is fulfilled, appoint a discerning man to wash me, for the discerning one is held in a place by God. So let him wash me thoroughly and raise his voice with the takbir. Then proceed to a kerchief in the chest containing a garment from the garments of the Prophet ﷺ and a clipping from his hair and nails. Place the clipping in my nose, my mouth, my ears, and my eyes, and place the garment upon my skin beneath my shrouds. And O Yazid, keep God's injunction regarding parents. When you enfold me in my new cloth and place me in my grave, leave Mu'awiyah to the Most Merciful of the merciful." And Muhammad ibn 'Uqbah said: When death descended upon Mu'awiyah, he said, "Would that I were a man from Quraysh in Dhu Tawa, and that I had never been involved in this affair at all."
When the death of 'Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan approached, he looked at a washerman beside Damascus wringing a garment with his hand and then striking it against the washing stone. 'Abd al-Malik said, "Would that I were a washerman, eating from the labor of my hands day by day, and had never been involved in the affairs of the world at all." This reached Abu Hazim, who said, "Praise be to God, who makes them, when death approaches them, wish for what we are in; and when death approaches us, we do not wish for what they are in." 'Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan was asked during the illness from which he died, "How do you find yourself, O Commander of the Faithful?" He said, "I find myself as God, the Exalted, has said: 'And you have certainly come to Us alone as We created you the first time, and you have left what We bestowed upon you behind your backs...' (Quran 6:94)" and he died. And Fatimah bint 'Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan, the wife of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, said: I used to hear 'Umar during the illness from which he died saying, "O God, make my death easy for them, even for an hour of the day." On the day he was taken, I left his presence and sat down.

In another chamber between us with a door, he being in his dome, I heard him say: "That abode of the Hereafter We assign to those who seek not exaltation in the earth nor corruption, and the outcome is for the righteous." Then he fell silent. I ceased to hear any movement or speech, so I said to his attendant, "See if he is asleep." When he entered, he cried out, and I rushed in to find him deceased. It was said to him as death approached, "Leave a testament, O Commander of the Faithful." He said, "I warn you against a demise like this one, for it is inevitable for you." It is related that when 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz became gravely ill, a physician was summoned for him. When the physician examined him, he said, "I see the man has been given poison, and I fear death for him." 'Umar raised his gaze and said, "And do you not also fear death for one who has not been given poison?" The physician said, "Did you sense this, O Commander of the Faithful?" He said, "Yes, I knew it when it entered my belly." He said, "Then seek treatment, O Commander of the Faithful, for I fear your soul will depart." He said, "My Lord is the best destination. By God, if I knew my cure lay in the lobe of my ear, I would not raise my hand to my ear to take it. O God, choose for 'Umar in meeting You." He lingered but a few days until he died. It was said that when his death approached, he wept. He was asked, "What makes you weep, O Commander of the Faithful? Rejoice, for God has revived through you traditions and manifested through you justice." He wept and then said, "Will I not be made to stand and questioned concerning the affairs of this creation? By God, even if I were just among them, I would fear for my soul that it would not fulfill its argument before God, unless God prompts its argument. So what of the many things we have neglected?" His eyes overflowed, and he lingered but a short while until he died. When the time of his death drew near, he said, "Sit me up." They sat him up, and he said, "I am the one You commanded, yet I fell short; You forbade me, yet I disobeyed," three times. Then he said, "But there is no god but God." Then he raised his head, fixing his gaze intently. He was asked about that, and he said, "Verily, I see a verdant green; they are neither human nor jinn." Then he passed away, may God have mercy on him. It is recounted of Harun al-Rashid that he selected his shrouds with his own hand at death and would look at them and say, "His wealth availed him not, nor his authority; it has perished from him." Al-Ma'mun spread ashes and lay upon them, saying, "O You whose dominion does not vanish, have mercy on one whose dominion has vanished." Al-Mu'tasim would say at his death, "Had I known my life was this short, I would not have done [what I did]." Al-Muntasir would writhe upon himself at his death, and it was said to him, "There is no harm upon you, O Commander of the Faithful." He said, "It is only this: the world has gone, and the Hereafter has come." 'Amr ibn al-'As said at death, looking at chests belonging to his sons, "Who will take them with their contents? Would that it were dung." Al-Hajjaj said at his death, "O God, forgive me, for the people say You will not forgive me." 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz admired this statement of his and envied him for it. When this was recounted to al-Hasan, he said, "Did he say it?" It was said, "Yes." He said, "Perhaps."

(Exposition of the sayings of a group from among the elect righteous from the Companions, the Successors, and those after them from the people of Sufism, may God be pleased with them all.)

When death approached Mu'adh, may God be pleased with him, he said, "O God, I used to fear You, and today I hope in You. O God, You know I did not love the world and long abiding in it for the flowing of rivers nor the planting of trees, but for the thirst of the midday heat, the striving through the hours, and jostling with the scholars in the company at the circles of remembrance." When his death throes intensified—throes like none had experienced—every time he emerged from the swoon, he would open his eyes and say, "My Lord, how You suffocate me with Your suffocation! By Your might, You know my heart loves You." (When death approached Salman, he wept. He was asked, "What makes you weep?" He said, "I weep not in anguish for the world, but the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, enjoined upon us that the provision of any of us from the world should be like the provision of a traveler.") When Salman died, they looked at all he left, and its value was a few dirhams. When death approached Bilal, his wife said, "O our grief!" He said, "Nay, O our joy! Tomorrow we meet the beloved ones, Muhammad and his party." It is said that 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak opened his eyes at death and smiled, saying, "For the like of this let the workers work." When death approached Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, he wept. He was asked, "What makes you weep?" He said, "I await a messenger from God to give me glad tidings of Paradise or of the Fire." When death approached Ibn al-Munkadir, he wept. He was asked, "What makes you weep?" He said, "By God, I weep not for a sin I know I committed, but I fear I committed something I deemed trivial while it is great with God." When death approached 'Amir ibn 'Abd al-Qays, he wept. He was asked, "What makes you weep?" He said, "I weep not in dread of death nor in craving for the world, but I weep for what I will miss of the thirst of the midday heat and for standing in prayer at night in winter." When death approached Fudayl, he lost consciousness, then opened his eyes and said, "O how distant his journey, and how scant his provision!" When death approached Ibn al-Mubarak, he said to Nasr...

His master said, "Place my head upon the earth," and he wept. Nusayr asked him, "What makes you weep?" He replied, "I remembered the bliss I was in, and here you are dying poor and estranged." He said, "Be silent, for I asked God Almighty to grant me the life of the wealthy and the death of the poor." Then he said to him, "Meet me, and do not return to me unless I speak a second word."

‘Ata ibn Yasar said: Iblis appeared to a man at the time of death and said to him, "You are saved." He replied, "What security do you have after this?" And one of them wept at the time of death, so it was said to him, "What makes you weep?" He said, "A verse in the Book of God Almighty, His Mighty and Majestic saying: 'God only accepts from the righteous.'"

Al-Hasan, may God be pleased with him, entered upon a man whose soul was departing and said, "A matter whose beginning is such is truly worthy that its end be feared, and a matter whose end is such is truly worthy that its beginning be renounced."

Al-Jurayri said: I was with al-Junayd during his final moments, and it was Friday and the day of Nayruz. He was reciting the Qur’an and completed it. I said to him in that state, "O Abu al-Qasim." He replied, "And who is more deserving of that than I? Behold, my scroll is being rolled up."

Ruwaym said: I attended the passing of Abu Sa‘id al-Kharraz, and he was saying:
"The yearning of the hearts of the knowers for remembrance,
And their recollection at the time of intimate communion with the Secret.
Cups of deaths were passed around to them,
So they became heedless of the world like the heedlessness of the grateful.
Their concerns roam in a camp
Where the people of God’s affection are like shining stars.
Their bodies on earth are slain by His love,
And their spirits in the veils soar toward the heights.
They have not camped except near their Beloved,
Nor have they alighted from any touch of misery or harm."

It was said to al-Junayd, "Abu Sa‘id al-Khazzaz used to be greatly overcome with spiritual emotion at death." He said, "It is not surprising that his spirit would fly away out of longing." And it was said to Dhu al-Nun at his death, "What do you desire?" He said, "That I know Him a moment before my death." And it was said to one of them while in the throes of death, "Say 'Allah'." He replied, "How long will you say 'Allah' while I am burning with Allah?"

One of them said: I was with Mumsad al-Dinawari when a poor man approached and said, "Peace be upon you. Is there here a clean place where a person can die?" He said: They pointed him to a place, and there was a spring of water there. The poor man renewed his ablution, prayed as much as God willed, then went to that place, stretched out his legs, and died.

Abu ‘Abbas al-Dinawari was speaking in his gathering when a woman cried out in spiritual emotion. He said to her, "Die." The woman stood up, and when she reached the house, she turned to him and said, "I have died," and fell down dead.

It is related from Fatimah, the sister of Abu ‘Ali al-Rudhbari, that she said: When the term of Abu ‘Ali al-Rudhbari drew near, and his head was in my lap, he opened his eyes and said, "These are the gates of heaven, they have opened; these are the gardens, they have been adorned; and this is a caller saying, 'O Abu ‘Ali, we have brought you to the highest rank, even if you did not desire it.'" Then he began to say:
"By Your right, I have not looked to other than You
With an eye of affection, until
I see You—You see my torment with a languid glance
And with the rosy cheek from Your life."

It was said to al-Junayd, "Say 'There is no god but God'." He replied, "I have not forgotten it that you should remind me of it." Ja‘far ibn Nasir asked Bakran, the servant of al-Dinawari who attended al-Shibli, "What did you see from him?" He said, "He said, 'There is a single dirham of injustice against me, and I have given thousands in charity on behalf of its owner, yet there is no concern upon my heart greater than it.' Then he said, 'Make ablution for me for prayer.' I did so, but I forgot to comb his beard, and he had seized his tongue. So he grasped my hand and inserted it into his beard, then he died." Ja‘far wept and said, "What do you say about a man who, at the end of his life, did not neglect a single etiquette of the Sacred Law?"

It was said to Bishr ibn al-Harith when he was on his deathbed—and it was as if life was dear to him—so he said, "The arrival before God is severe." And it was said to Salih ibn Mismar, "Will you not leave a will for your son and your family?" He said, "I am too shy before God to entrust them to other than Him."

When Abu Sulayman al-Darani was on his deathbed, his companions came to him and said, "Receive glad tidings, for you are proceeding to a Lord Forgiving and Merciful." He said to them, "Will you not say, 'Beware, for you are proceeding to a Lord who will call you to account for the small and punish you for the great'?"

When Abu Bakr al-Wasiti was on his deathbed, it was said to him, "Counsel us." He said, "Preserve the desire of the Truth concerning you."

One of them was on his deathbed, and his wife wept. He said to her, "What makes you weep?" She said, "I weep for you." He said, "If you must weep, then weep for yourself, for I have wept for this day for forty years."

Al-Junayd said: I entered upon Sari al-Saqati to visit him in his fatal illness and said, "How do you find yourself?" He began to say:
"How can I complain to my Physician of what ails me,
When what ails me has come to me from my Physician?"
I took a fan to fan him, and he said, "How can the breeze of the fan reach one whose innards are burning?" Then he began to say:
"The heart is burning, the tears are racing,
The distress is gathered, and patience is scattered.
How can there be settlement for one who has no settlement
From what passion, longing, and anxiety have incurred?
O Lord, if there is any relief for me in anything,
Bestow it upon me as long as I have a breath."

It is related that a group of al-Shibli’s companions entered upon him while he was dying and said to him, "Say 'There is no god but God'." He began to say:

A house you inhabit needs no lamp, for your hoped-for countenance is our argument on the day people come with their proofs. May God not grant me relief on the day I call upon you for deliverance.

It is related that Abu al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Ata’ entered upon Junayd at the moment of his passing. He greeted him, but Junayd did not answer. Then he answered after an hour and said, “Excuse me, for I was in my litany.” Then he turned his face toward the *qiblah*, uttered the *takbir*, and died.

It was said to al-Kinani when death approached him, “What was your practice?” He said, “Had my term not drawn near, I would not have told you. I stood at the door of my heart for forty years, and whenever anything other than God passed through it, I barred it from him.”

It is related from al-Mu‘tamir, who said: I was among those present with al-Hakam ibn ‘Abd al-Malik when the Truth came to him. I said, “O God, make the agonies of death easy for him, for he was such and such,” and I mentioned his good qualities. He regained consciousness and said, “Who is speaking?” I said, “I am.” He said, “Indeed, the Angel of Death, peace be upon him, says to me, ‘I am gentle with every generous person.’” Then he was extinguished.

And when the death of Yusuf ibn Asbat approached, Hudhayfah attended him and found him anxious. He said, “O Abu Muhammad, this is the time for anxiety and dismay?” He said, “O Abu ‘Abd Allah, how can I not be anxious and dismayed, for I do not know that I have been truthful to God in any of my works?” Hudhayfah said, “How astonishing! This righteous man leaves at his death claiming he does not know he was truthful to God in any of his works.”

And from al-Mughazili, who said: I entered upon a shaykh of mine from the people of this quality while he was ill, and he was saying, “You are able to do what you wish, so be gentle with me.”

And one of the shaykhs entered upon Mumsad al-Dinawari at the time of his death and said to him, “May God Almighty act and do,” from the door of supplication. He laughed and then said, “For thirty years Paradise has been presented to me with all that is in it, and I have not cast a glance at it.”

And it was said to Ruwaym at death, “Say, ‘There is no god but God.’” He said, “I know nothing else.”

And when the death of al-Thawri approached, it was said to him, “Say, ‘There is no god but God.’” He said, “Is there not then a command?”

And al-Muzani entered upon al-Shafi‘i, mercy of God upon them both, during the illness in which he died and said to him, “How are you this morning, O Abu ‘Abd Allah?” He said, “I have become one departing from the world, parting from the brethren, meeting my evil deeds, drinking from the cup of death, and arriving before God Almighty. And I do not know whether my soul will go to Paradise, so that I may congratulate it, or to the Fire, so that I may console it.” Then he began to recite:

> When my heart hardened and my paths narrowed, I made my hope toward Your pardon a ladder.
> My sin seemed immense to me, but when I compared it to Your pardon, my Lord, Your pardon was greater.
> You have not ceased to be One who pardons sin, constantly bestowing and pardoning out of grace and generosity.
> Were it not for You, no worshipper would have been led astray by Iblis, so how, when he led astray Your intimate Adam?

And when the death of Ahmad ibn Khadruwayh approached, he was asked about a question. His eyes welled with tears and he said, “O my son, a door I have been knocking upon for ninety-five years—behold, it is opened for me this very hour. I do not know whether it opens with felicity or wretchedness. Now is the time for the answer.”

These are their sayings, and they differed only according to the difference of their states. Fear dominated some, hope others, and yearning and love others. Each of them spoke according to the requirement of his state, and all are sound relative to their states.

*(The Sixth Chapter: On the Sayings of the Knowers Concerning Funerals and Graves, and the Ruling on Visiting Graves)*

Know that funerals are a lesson for the insightful and contain an admonition and reminder for the heedless. However, they only increase them in hardness, for they think they are always looking at the funeral of another and do not consider that they will inevitably be carried upon biers—or they do consider it, but they do not have the capacity for nearness, nor do they reflect that those carried upon biers also thought thus, but their thinking proved false and their time expired in nearness. Let no servant look upon a funeral without imagining himself carried upon it, for he will be carried upon it in nearness—as if it has already happened, and perhaps tomorrow or the day after.

It is related from Abu Hurayrah that when he saw a funeral, he would say, “Proceed, for we are upon the trace.”

And Makhul al-Dimashqi, when he saw a funeral, would say, “Go forth, for we are going.” A powerful admonition and a swift heedlessness—the first and the last pass away, he who has no intellect.

And Usayd ibn Hudayr said, “I never witnessed a funeral without my soul telling me of nothing except what is being done to him and what he is proceeding to.”
