Abu Huraira reported: The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "When a servant dies, two black, blue-eyed angels come to him, one called Munkar and the other Nakir. They say, 'What did you used to say about this Prophet?' If he was a believer, he says, 'He is the servant of God and His Messenger; I bear witness that there is no god but God and that Muhammad is the Messenger of God.' They say, 'We knew you would say that.' Then his grave is expanded for him seventy cubits by seventy cubits, and his grave is illuminated for him. Then it is said to him, 'Sleep.' He says, 'Let me return to my family to inform them.' It is said to him, 'Sleep,' and he sleeps like the sleep of a bridegroom whom none awakens except the most beloved of his family to him, until God raises him from that resting place. If he was a hypocrite, he says, 'I do not know; I used to hear people saying something and I would say it.' They say, 'We knew you would say that.' Then it is said to the earth, 'Close in upon him,' and it closes in upon him until his ribs interlace, and he remains tormented until God raises him from that resting place."

From 'Ata' ibn Yasar, he said: The Messenger of God said to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may God be pleased with him: "O 'Umar, how will you be when you die and your people take you, measure for you three cubits by a cubit and a span, then return to you, wash you, shroud you, embalm you, then carry you until they place you in it, then heap the earth upon you and bury you? When they depart from you, the tempters of the grave, Munkar and Nakir, come to you—their voices like crashing thunder and their sight like flashing lightning, dragging their hair and digging the grave with their fangs, tearing you and tossing you—how will you be then, O 'Umar?" 'Umar said, "Will I have my intellect like now?" He said, "Yes." He said, "Then I will suffice against them."

This is an explicit text that the intellect does not change with death; rather, the body and limbs change. Thus, the deceased is rational, perceiving, aware of pains and pleasures as he was, with nothing of his intellect changed. The perceiving intellect is not these limbs; rather, it is an inner thing having no length nor width. Indeed, that which is indivisible in itself is what perceives things. Even if all the limbs of a person were scattered and nothing remained except the perceiving part that is indivisible and does not split, the rational person in his completeness would remain established and existing. And so it is after death, for that part is not dissolved by death nor does non-existence befall it.

Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir said: It reached me that the disbeliever is given mastery over in his grave by a blind, deaf creature, in its hand an iron whip with a head like a camel's bucket, with which it strikes him until the Day of Resurrection. He does not see it to guard against it, nor does he hear its voice so that it might have mercy on him.

Abu Huraira said: When the deceased is placed in his grave, there come...

His righteous deeds surrounded him. If it came from the direction of his head, his recitation of the Qur’an came forth. If it came from the direction of his feet, his standing in prayer came forth. If it came from the direction of his hands, the hands said, “By God, he used to extend me for charity and supplication; you have no way to him.” If it came from his mouth, his remembrance and his fasting came forth. Likewise, the prayer and patience stood aside and said, “Indeed, if I had seen any shortcoming, I would have been its companion.” Sufyan said: His righteous deeds fended for him as a man fends for his brother, his family, and his children. Then it is said to him at that time, “May God bless you in your resting place. How excellent are your companions, and how excellent are your friends.”

From Hudhayfah, who said: We were with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, at a funeral. He sat at the head of the grave, then began looking into it and said, “The believer is pressed in this [grave] with a pressure that makes his ribs converge.”

‘A’ishah, may God be pleased with her, said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, “The grave has a pressure; if anyone were to be safe or saved from it, Sa‘d ibn Mu‘adh would have been saved.”

From Anas, who said: Zaynab, the daughter of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, died. She was a woman who was often ill. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, followed her, and his condition saddened us. When we reached the grave and he entered it, his face turned pale yellow. When he came out, his face brightened. We said, “O Messenger of God, we saw something from you; what was that?” He said, “I remembered the pressure upon my daughter and the severity of the grave’s punishment. I came and was informed that God had lightened it for her, yet she was pressed with a pressure whose sound was heard between the two horizons.”

(Chapter Eight: What is Known of the States of the Dead Through Spiritual Disclosure in Dreams)

Know that the lights of insight gained from the Book of God Almighty and the Sunnah of His Messenger, peace be upon him, and from the paths of reflection, acquaint us with the states of the dead in general and their division into the blissful and the wretched. However, the specific state of Zayd or ‘Amr is not disclosed at all. For if we rely on the faith of Zayd and ‘Amr, we do not know upon what he died or how his end was sealed. If we rely on his outward righteousness, the place of God-consciousness is the heart, and it is obscure, hidden even from the possessor of God-consciousness, let alone others. Therefore, outward righteousness without inward God-consciousness holds no judgment. God Almighty said: “God only accepts from the God-conscious.” Thus, the judgment of Zayd or ‘Amr cannot be known except by witnessing him and what befalls him. When he dies, he has transferred from the world of dominion and testimony to the world of the unseen and the sovereign realm. He is not seen with the outward eye, but is seen with another eye created in the heart of every person. However, a dense veil from his desires and worldly preoccupations has been placed upon it, so he does not see with it, nor can he imagine seeing anything from the sovereign realm unless that veil is lifted from the eye of his heart. Since the veil was lifted from the eyes of the prophets, upon them be peace, they undoubtedly looked upon the sovereign realm and witnessed its wonders, and the dead are in the sovereign realm, so they saw them and informed [others]. For this reason, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, saw the pressure of the grave in the case of Sa‘d ibn Mu‘adh and in the case of his daughter Zaynab. Likewise was the state of Abu Jabar when he was martyred, as he informed him that God seated him before Him with no veil between them. Such witnessing is not attainable except for the prophets and the saints whose rank is close to theirs. What is possible for the likes of us is another, weaker form of witnessing, yet it is also a prophetic witnessing: I mean witnessing in dreams, which is from the lights of prophethood. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: “The good dream is one part of forty-six parts of prophethood.” This too is a disclosure that occurs only by the lifting of the veil from the heart. Therefore, it is only trusted from the dream of a righteous, truthful man. Whoever lies frequently, his dream is not truthful. Whoever is excessive in corruption and disobedience, his heart becomes darkened, and what he sees is confused dreams. For this reason, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, commanded purity when sleeping, so that one may sleep in a state of purity—an allusion to inward purity as well, for it is the foundation, while outward purity is like its completion and perfection. Whenever the inward becomes clear, what will occur in the future is disclosed in the pupil of the heart, just as the entry into Makkah was disclosed to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, in sleep, until the verse was revealed: “God has truly fulfilled His Messenger’s vision in truth.” Rarely is a person without dreams that indicate matters which are later found to be true. The dream and knowledge of the unseen in sleep are among the wonders of God Almighty’s creation and the marvels of human nature. It is among the clearest proofs of the sovereign realm, yet people are heedless of it, as they are heedless of the other wonders of the heart and the wonders of the world. Speaking on the reality of the dream is from the subtleties of the sciences of spiritual disclosure; it cannot be mentioned in addition to the science of spiritual conduct. But the amount that can be mentioned here is an example to make you understand the intended meaning: which is to know that the heart is like a mirror in which images and the realities of matters are reflected, and that everything God Almighty has decreed from the beginning of creation...

The world and all that follows is inscribed and established in the creation that God, Exalted is He, brought into being. It is expressed at times as the Preserved Tablet, at times as the Clear Book, and at times as a Manifest Imam, as has come in the Qur’an. Thus, all that has occurred in the world and all that will occur is written therein and engraved upon it with an engraving not beheld by this eye. Do not imagine that this Tablet is of wood, iron, or bone, nor that the Book is of paper or parchment. Rather, you must understand definitively that the Tablet of God does not resemble the tablet of creation, and the Book of God does not resemble the book of creation, just as His Essence and Attributes do not resemble the essence and attributes of creation. If you seek an analogy to bring it closer to your understanding, then know that the establishment of the decrees upon the Tablet parallels the establishment of the words and letters of the Qur’an in the mind and heart of one who has memorized it. For it is inscribed therein, such that when he recites it, it is as if he is looking upon it. Yet if you were to examine his brain part by part, you would not perceive a single letter of that script, even though there is no visible script or observable letter there. From this pattern, you should understand the nature of the Tablet being engraved with all that God, Exalted is He, has decreed and ordained.

In the analogy, the Tablet is like a mirror in which images appear. If another mirror were placed opposite it, the image from that mirror would be reflected in this one, unless there is a veil between them. The heart is a mirror that receives the impressions of knowledge, and the Tablet is a mirror in which all the impressions of knowledge are present. The heart’s preoccupation with its desires and the demands of the senses is a veil cast between it and the contemplation of the Tablet, which is from the realm of the Unseen. If a wind blows, moving and lifting this veil, something from the realm of the Unseen flashes in the mirror of the heart like fleeting lightning. It may become established and endure, or it may not endure—and this is the more common case. As long as one is awake, the heart is occupied with what the senses bring to it from the realm of dominion and the visible world, and this is a veil from the realm of the Unseen. The meaning of sleep is that the senses are subdued and do not bring their impressions to the heart. When it is freed from them and from imagination, and is pure in its essence, the veil between it and the Preserved Tablet is lifted. Then something from what is on the Tablet falls into the heart, just as an image falls from one mirror to another when the veil between them is removed. However, sleep prevents all the senses from functioning, but it does not prevent imagination from its work and its movement. Thus, what falls into the heart is immediately seized by the imagination, which imitates it with a resembling form. Imaginative forms are more firmly retained in memory than others, so the imagination remains in memory. When one awakens, only the imagination is remembered, and the interpreter must look at this imagined form to discern which meaning among meanings it is a depiction of, returning to the meanings through the connection between the imagined form and the meanings. Examples of this are evident to one who has studied the science of dream interpretation. One example should suffice you: A man said to Ibn Sirin, "I saw as if I had a ring in my hand with which I was sealing the mouths of men and the private parts of women." He said, "You are a caller to prayer who gives the call before dawn in Ramadan." The man said, "You have spoken the truth." Consider that the spirit of sealing is prevention, and for this reason sealing is intended. What is unveiled to the heart from the Preserved Tablet is the actual state of the person as it truly is—namely, that he is one who prevents people from eating and drinking. But the imagination is accustomed to associating prevention with sealing by a ring, so it depicted it with the imaginative form that contains the spirit of the meaning. What remains in memory is only the imaginative form. This is a brief glimpse from the ocean of the knowledge of dreams, whose wonders are boundless. And how could it not be, for it is the brother of death? Indeed, death is a wonder among wonders, and this is because it resembles it in one weak aspect: its effect in lifting the veil from the unseen realm, to the point that the sleeper comes to know what will be in the future. So what do we suppose of death, which tears the veil and removes the covering entirely, so that a person, at the moment the soul is severed, sees without delay—either surrounded by punishments, disgrace, and shame (we seek refuge in God from that), or enveloped in everlasting bliss and a great, endless dominion? At this point, it is said to the wretched, when the covering has been removed: "You were certainly in unmindfulness of this, and We have removed from you your covering, so your sight today is sharp." And it is said: "Is this magic, or do you not see? Enter it and be patient, or do not be patient—it is all the same to you. You are only being recompensed for what you used to do." And to them is the allusion in His saying, Exalted is He: "And there will appear to them from God that which they had never anticipated." Thus, the most knowledgeable of scholars and the wisest of sages, upon death, will have unveiled to him wonders and signs that never once crossed his mind or stirred within his conscience. If a rational person had no concern or grief other than contemplating the gravity of that state—what the veil is lifted from, and what the covering is removed from, whether it be inherent misery or permanent felicity—that alone would suffice to consume an entire lifetime. A wonder indeed is our heedlessness, with these immense matters before us. And more wondrous still is our rejoicing in our wealth and our families.

And through our means and our progeny, nay, through our limbs and our hearing and sight, even though we know with certainty that we shall part from all of that. But where is he who breathes the Spirit of Holiness into awe, uttering what was said to the Master of the Prophets: "Love whom you will, for you shall part from them; live as you will, for you shall die; and do as you will, for you shall be recompensed for it." Thus, inevitably, since that was unveiled to him with the eye of certainty, he was in the world like a wayfarer who laid not brick upon brick, nor reed upon reed, and left behind neither dinar nor dirham, nor took a beloved or an intimate friend. Indeed, he said: "If I were to take an intimate friend, I would have taken Abu Bakr as an intimate friend, but your companion is the intimate friend of the All-Merciful." Thus, he clarified that the intimate friendship of the All-Merciful permeated the innermost of his heart and that His love took hold of the core of his heart, leaving no room therein for an intimate or a beloved. And he said to his community: "If you love Allah, then follow me; Allah will love you." For his community is only those who follow him, and none follow him except those who turn away from this world and turn towards the Hereafter, for he called only to Allah and the Last Day, and diverted only from the world and immediate gains. Thus, to the extent you turn away from the world and turn towards the Hereafter, you have trodden his path which he trod; and to the extent you tread his path, you have followed him; and to the extent you follow him, you have become of his community; and to the extent you incline towards the world, you have deviated from his path, desired other than following him, and joined those about whom Allah, the Exalted, said: "But as for he who transgressed and preferred the life of this world, then indeed, Hellfire will be his refuge." So if you were to emerge from the abode of delusion and be just to yourself, O man—and all of us are that man—you would know that from morning until evening you strive only for immediate gains, and you move and rest only for the immediate world, then you hope to be tomorrow among his community and followers. How distant is your assumption, and how cold your hope! "Then will We treat the Muslims like the criminals? What is [wrong] with you? How do you judge?" Let us return to what we were upon and concerning, for the reins of speech have extended beyond its intended aim. And let us now mention from the dreams that reveal the states of the deceased what greatly benefits, since prophethood has gone and only glad tidings remain, and that is nothing but dreams.

(Explanation of dreams that reveal the states of the deceased and deeds beneficial in the Hereafter)

Among these is the vision of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and he said, peace be upon him: "Whoever sees me in a dream has indeed seen me truly, for Satan cannot take my form." And 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, said: "I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in a dream, and I saw him not looking at me. I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what is my affair?' He turned to me and said: 'Are you not the one who kisses while you are fasting?' By the One in whose hand is my soul, I will never kiss a woman while I am fasting, ever." And al-'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: "I was fond of 'Umar and wished to see him in a dream, but I did not see him until near the turn of the year. I saw him wiping sweat from his forehead, saying: 'This is the time of my relief. Were it not that I met Him as Compassionate, Merciful, my throne would indeed be shaken.'" And al-Hasan ibn 'Ali said: "'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, said to me: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, appeared to me tonight in a dream. I said: "O Messenger of Allah, what have you encountered from your community?" He said: "Supplicate against them." So I said: "O Allah, replace them for me with those better for me than them, and replace me for them with one worse for them than me." Then he went out and Ibn Muljam struck him.'" And some of the shaykhs said: "I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, seek forgiveness for me.' But he turned away from me. I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah narrated to us from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah that you never refused when asked for anything.' He said: 'No.' Then he turned to me and said: 'May Allah forgive you.'" And it is narrated from al-'Abbas ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib, who said: "I was a close companion to Abu Lahab, keeping company with him. When he died and Allah informed about him what He informed, I grieved for him and his matter concerned me. I asked Allah, the Exalted, for a year to show him to me in a dream." He said: "I saw him aflame with fire. I asked him about his condition, and he said: 'I have entered the Fire in torment; it is not lightened for me nor is there relief except on Monday night among all the days and nights.' I said: 'How is that?' He said: 'Muhammad, peace be upon him, was born on that night. Umm Ayman came to me and gave me the glad tidings of his birth from Aminah, so I rejoiced at him and freed a slave girl of mine out of joy for him. Thus, Allah rewarded me for that by lifting the torment from me every Monday night.'" And 'Abd al-Wahid ibn Zaid said: "I went out for Hajj, and a man accompanied me who would not stand, sit, move, or rest without sending blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him. I asked him about that, and he said: 'I will tell you about that. The first time I went out to Mecca, my father was with me. When we turned back, I slept at one of the stopping places. While I was asleep, a visitor came to me and said: "Get up, for Allah has caused your father to die and blackened his face." I got up in alarm and lifted the cloth from his face, and he was dead with a blackened face. Terror entered me because of that. While I was in that grief, my eyes overcame me and I slept."

Then, at my father's head stood four black men holding iron rods, when a man of handsome countenance, clad in two green garments, approached and said to them, "Step aside." He wiped his face with his hand, then came to me and said, "Rise, for God has whitened your father's face." I asked, "Who are you, may my father and mother be your ransom?" He replied, "I am Muhammad." I rose and uncovered the cloth from my father's face, and behold, it was white. Never after that did I neglect to send blessings upon the Messenger of God ﷺ. And from 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, he said: I saw the Messenger of God ﷺ with Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may God be pleased with them, sitting beside him. I gave greetings and sat down. While I was seated, 'Ali and Mu'awiyah were brought and led into a house, the door closed upon them as I watched. No sooner had they entered than 'Ali, may God be pleased with him, emerged saying, "By the Lord of the Ka'bah, judgment has been passed in my favor!" And no sooner had he emerged than Mu'awiyah followed, saying, "By the Lord of the Ka'bah, I have been forgiven!" And Ibn 'Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, once awoke from sleep exclaiming in grief, "By God, al-Husayn has been killed!"—this before his actual slaying. His companions expressed disbelief, so he said, "I saw the Messenger of God ﷺ holding a vial of blood, and he said, 'Do you not know what my community has done after me? They have killed the son of al-Husayn, and this is his blood and the blood of his companions, which I raise to God Almighty.'" The news of his killing came twenty-four days later, on the very day he had seen it. And al-Siddiq, may God be pleased with him, was seen in a vision and asked, "You used to constantly say on your tongue, 'This will lead me to the watering places'—so what has God done with you?" He replied, "I said with it, 'There is no god but God,' and He led me to Paradise."

(Explanation of the Dreams of the Masters, may God's mercy be upon them all.)

One of the masters said: I saw Muttamim al-Dawraqi in a dream and asked, "O my master, what has God done with you?" He replied, "He settled me in the Gardens." It was said to him, "O Muttamim, did you find anything pleasing therein?" He said, "No, O my master." He responded, "Had you found anything pleasing therein, I would have entrusted you to it and not brought you to me." And Yusuf ibn al-Husayn was seen in a dream and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He forgave me." Asked, "By what means?" He replied, "I never mixed seriousness with levity." And from Mansur ibn Isma'il, he said: I saw 'Abdullah ibn al-Bazzar in a dream and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He stood me before Him and forgave me every sin I confessed, except one, for I was too ashamed to confess it. So He kept me standing in sweat until the flesh of my face fell away." I asked, "What was that sin?" He said, "I looked at a handsome youth and admired him, and I was ashamed before God to mention it." And Abu Ja'far al-Saydalani said: I saw the Messenger of God ﷺ in a dream, surrounded by a group of the poor. While we were thus, the sky split open and two angels descended, one holding a basin and the other a ewer. They placed the basin before the Messenger of God ﷺ, and he washed his hands, then commanded until all had washed. Then they placed the basin before me, and one said to the other, "Do not pour over his hand, for he is not of them." I said, "O Messenger of God, is it not reported from you that you said, 'A person is with those he loves'?" He said, "Yes." I said, "O Messenger of God, I love you and I love these poor ones." He ﷺ said, "Pour over his hand, for he is of them." And al-Junayd said: I saw in a dream as if I were speaking to people when an angel stood by and asked, "What is the closest means by which seekers draw near to God Almighty?" I said, "A hidden deed weighed in the balance." As I spoke, the angel said, "A successful word, by God!" And Mujammi' was seen in a dream and asked, "How did you find the matter?" He replied, "I saw that those who renounce the world have taken the best of this world and the Hereafter." And a man from Syria said to al-'Ala' ibn Ziyad, "I saw you in a dream as if you were in Paradise." He rose from his seat, turned to him, and said, "Perhaps Satan intended something, but I was protected from it," and he sent a man to kill me. And Muhammad ibn Was'i said, "A dream gladdens the believer but does not deceive him." And Salih ibn Bashir said: I saw 'Ata' al-Sulami in a dream and said, "May God have mercy on you, you were long in sorrow in the world." He said, "By God, that has brought me lasting comfort and perpetual joy." I asked, "In which ranks are you?" He replied, "With those upon whom God has bestowed favor: the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous—and excellent are those as companions." And Zurarah ibn Abi Awfa was asked in a dream, "Which deeds are most excellent in your view?" He said, "Contentment and short hopes." And Yazid ibn Madh'ur said: I saw al-Awza'i in a dream and asked, "O Abu 'Amr, guide me to a deed by which I may draw near to God Almighty." He said, "I have not seen there any rank higher than the rank of the scholars, then the rank of the grief-stricken." Yazid was a great elder, and he wept until his eyes grew dark. And Ibn 'Uyaynah said: I saw my brother in a dream and asked, "O my brother, what has God done with you?" He said, "Every sin I sought forgiveness for was forgiven me, and what I did not seek forgiveness for was not forgiven." And 'Ali al-Talhi said: I saw in a dream a woman unlike the women of this world and asked, "Who are you?" She said, "A houri." I said, "Give yourself to me in marriage." She said...

"Seek my hand in marriage from my Master, and set my dowry." I asked, "And what is your dowry?" She replied, "To restrain your soul from its afflictions." Ibrahim ibn Ishaq al-Harbi said, "I saw Zubaydah in a dream and asked, 'What has God done with you?' She answered, 'He forgave me.' I asked her, 'For what you spent on the road to Mecca?' She said, 'As for the expenditures I made, their rewards returned to their owners, but I was forgiven for my daughter.'"

When Sufyan al-Thawri died, he was seen in a dream and asked, "What has been done with you?" He said, "My first foot was placed on the Bridge, and the second in Paradise." Ahmad ibn Abi al-Hawari said, "I saw in a dream a maiden, the most beautiful I had ever seen, and her face shone with light. I asked her, 'From what is the radiance of your face?' She said, 'From remembering that night you wept.' I said, 'Yes.' She said, 'I took your tear and wiped my face with it, and hence the radiance you see.'"

Al-Kattani said, "I saw al-Junayd in a dream and asked him, 'What has God done with you?' He said, 'Those allusions vanished and those expressions departed, and we gained nothing but two rak'ahs we used to pray at night.' Zubaydah was seen in a dream and asked, 'What has God done with you?' She said, 'He forgave me for these four words: "There is no god but God"—I spent my life with it; "There is no god but God"—I enter my grave with it; "There is no god but God"—I am alone with it; "There is no god but God"—I meet my Lord, Mighty and Majestic, with it.'"

And it was said, "O Bishr, are you not ashamed before Me? You used to fear Me with all that fear." Abu Sulayman was seen in a dream and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He showed me mercy." Bishr was seen in a dream and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He showed me mercy, and nothing was more harmful to me than the allusions of the people to me." Abu Bakr al-Kattani said, "I saw in a dream a youth, the most beautiful I had ever seen. I asked him, 'Who are you?' He said, 'Piety.' I said, 'Where do you dwell?' He said, 'In every sorrowful heart.' Then I turned and saw a black woman. I asked, 'Who are you?' She said, 'I am Sickness.' I said, 'Where do you dwell?' She said, 'In every joyful, merry heart.' I awoke and vowed not to laugh except if overcome."

Abu Sa'id al-Kharraz said, "I saw in a dream as if Iblis leapt upon me, and I took a stick to strike him, but he was not alarmed by it. A caller cried out to me, 'This one does not fear this; he only fears a light that is in the heart.'" Al-Masuhi said, "I saw Iblis in a dream walking naked. I said, 'Are you not ashamed before people?' He said, 'By God, these are people? If they were from people, I would not toy with them all day as children toy with a ball. Rather, people are a folk other than these; they have sickened my body'—and he pointed with his hand to our Sufi companions."

Abu Sa'id al-Kharraz said, "I was in Damascus and saw in a dream as if the Prophet, peace be upon him, came to me leaning on Abu Bakr and Umar, may God be pleased with them. He came and stood over me while I was uttering some sounds and beating my chest. He said, 'The evil of this is greater than its good.'" From Ibn 'Uyaynah, he said, "I saw Sufyan al-Thawri in a dream as if he were in Paradise, flying from tree to tree, saying, 'For the like of this let the workers work.' I said to him, 'Advise me.' He said, 'Minimize acquaintance with people.'"

Abu Hatim al-Razi narrated from Qabishah ibn 'Uqbah, who said, "I saw Sufyan al-Thawri and asked, 'What has God done with you?' He said:
      I beheld my Lord face to face, and He said to me,
      'Rejoice in My pleasure with you, O son of Sa'id.
      You were one who stood in prayer when darkness fell,
      With a tear of longing and a heart devoted.
      So choose for yourself any palace you desire,
      And visit Me, for I am not far from you.'"

Al-Shibli was seen after his death by three days and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He called me to account until I despaired, and when He saw my despair, He enveloped me in His mercy." Bani 'Amir was seen after his death in a dream and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He forgave me and made me a proof against the lovers." Al-Thawri was seen in a dream and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He showed me mercy." It was said, "What is the state of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak?" He said, "He is among those who enter upon his Lord twice every day."

Some of them were seen and asked about his state. He said, "They called us to account, scrutinized strictly, then bestowed and set free." Malik ibn Anas was seen and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He forgave me for a word that Uthman ibn 'Affan, may God be pleased with him, used to say upon seeing a funeral: 'Glory be to the Ever-Living who does not die.'" In the night al-Hasan al-Basri died, it was seen as if the gates of heaven were open and a caller called out, 'Behold, al-Hasan al-Basri has come to God, and He is pleased with him.'"

Al-Jahiz was seen and asked, "What has God done with you?" He said:
      "Write not with your hand except what will please you to see on the Day of Resurrection."

Al-Junayd saw Iblis in a dream naked and said, "Are you not ashamed before people?" He said, "And these are people? People are a folk in the mosque of al-Shuniziyyah who have worn out my body and burned my liver." Al-Junayd said, "When I awoke, I went to the mosque and saw a group who had placed their heads on their knees, contemplating. When they saw me, they said, 'Let not the talk of the wicked deceive you.'" Al-Nasr Abadhi was seen in Mecca after his death in a dream.

It was said to him, "What has God done with you?" He replied, "I was reproached with the reproach of the noble, then I was called, 'O Abu al-Qasim, after connection comes separation.' So I said, 'No, O Possessor of Majesty!' I had not been placed in the grave before I joined my Lord."

'Utbah the youth saw a houri in a dream, in a beautiful form. She said, "O 'Utbah, I am in love with you. So beware, do not perform any deed that would cause a barrier between me and you." 'Utbah said, "I have divorced the world thrice; there is no return for me to it until I meet you."

It was said that Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani saw the funeral procession of 'Asim, so he entered a passageway so as not to pray over him. Then someone saw the deceased in a dream and it was said to him, "What has God done with you?" He said, "He forgave me," and said, "Tell Ayyub: 'Say, [O Muhammad], "If you possessed the treasuries of the mercy of my Lord, then you would withhold out of fear of spending."'"

Some said, "I saw on the night Dawud al-Ta'i died a light, angels descending and angels ascending. I said, 'What night is this?' They said, 'The night Dawud al-Ta'i died. Paradise has been adorned for the arrival of his spirit.'"

Abu Sa'id al-Shahham said, "I saw Sahl al-Sa'luki in a dream. I said, 'O Elder.' He said, 'Leave off calling me elder.' I said, 'Those spiritual states you witnessed?' He said, 'They availed us nothing.' I said, 'What has God done with you?' He said, 'He forgave me due to questions concerning incapacity that were asked.'"

Abu Bakr al-Rashidi said, "I saw Muhammad al-Tusi the teacher in a dream. He said to me, 'Tell Abu Sa'id al-Saffar the tutor:
    "We were resolved not to turn from passion,
    But by the life of love, you have turned, and we have not."'
I awoke and mentioned that to him. He said, 'I used to visit his grave every Friday, but I did not visit it this Friday.'"

Ibn Rashid said, "I saw Ibn al-Mubarak in a dream after his death. I said, 'Have you not died?' He said, 'Yes.' I said, 'What has God done with you?' He said, 'He forgave me with a forgiveness that encompassed every sin.' I said, 'And Sufyan al-Thawri?' He said, 'Ah, ah! That one is "from those upon whom God has bestowed favor, of the prophets and the truthful..."'"

Al-Rabi' ibn Sulayman said, "I saw al-Shafi'i, mercy of God upon him, after his death in a dream. I said, 'O Abu 'Abdillah, what has God done with you?' He said, 'He seated me upon a chair of gold and scattered moist pearls over me.'"

A man from the companions of al-Hasan al-Basri saw, on the night al-Hasan died, as if a caller was calling out: 'Indeed, God chose Adam and Noah and the family of Abraham and the family of 'Imran over the worlds,' and chose al-Hasan al-Basri over the people of his time."

Abu Ya'qub al-Qari al-Daqiqi said, "I saw in my dream a tall, dark-skinned man, and people were following him. I said, 'Who is this?' They said, 'Uways al-Qarani.' I went to him and said, 'Counsel me, may God have mercy on you.' He frowned at me. I said, 'I am seeking guidance, so guide me, may God guide you.' He turned to me and said, 'Follow the mercy of your Lord at the time of His love, and beware His wrath at the time of your disobedience, and do not cut off your hope in Him amidst all that.' Then he turned away and left me."

Abu Bakr ibn Abi Maryam said, "I saw Warqa' ibn Bishr al-Hadrami. I said, 'What have you done, O Warqa'?' He said, 'Weeping from the fear of God.'"

Yazid ibn Na'amah said, "A young woman perished in the sweeping plague. Her father saw her in a dream and said to her, 'O my daughter, inform me about the Hereafter.' She said, 'O my father, we have arrived at a tremendous matter. We know but do not act, and you act but do not know. By God, a glorification or two glorifications, or a rak'ah or two rak'ahs performed in a moment of leisure, is more beloved to me than the world and all it contains.'"

One of the companions of 'Utbah the youth said, "I saw 'Utbah in a dream. I said, 'What has God done with you?' He said, 'I entered Paradise by that supplication written in your house.' When I awoke, I came to my house and found the handwriting of 'Utbah the youth on the wall of the house: 'O Guide of the misguided, O Merciful to the sinners, O Accepter of the stumbles of the stumblers, have mercy on Your servant of great peril and upon all the Muslims collectively, and place us with the living, the provided-for, those upon whom You have bestowed favor from among the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous. Amen, O Lord of the worlds.'"

Musa ibn Hammad said, "I saw Sufyan al-Thawri in Paradise, flying from one palm tree to another and from one tree to another. I said, 'O Abu 'Abdillah, by what did you attain this?' He said, 'By scrupulous piety.' I said, 'What about 'Ali ibn 'Asim?' He said, 'That one is scarcely seen except as a star is seen.'"

A man from the Followers saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, in a dream and said, "O Messenger of God, admonish me." He said, "Yes. Whoever does not take stock of his deficiency is in deficiency, and whoever is in deficiency, death is better for him."

Al-Shafi'i, mercy of God upon him, said, "An affair overcame me in these days that distressed and pained me, and none but God, the Mighty and Majestic, was aware of it. Last night, a visitor came to me in my dream and said to me, 'O Muhammad ibn Idris, say: O God, I possess for myself neither benefit nor harm, nor death, nor life, nor resurrection. I cannot take except what You have given me, nor guard against except what You have protected me from. O God, so grant me success in what You love and are pleased with of speech and action, in well-being.'"

I have now prepared that. When the day had advanced, God Almighty granted me my request and facilitated my deliverance from what I was in. So, adhere to these supplications; do not neglect them. This is a collection of spiritual unveilings that indicate the states of the deceased and the deeds that draw one nearer to God. After this, we shall mention what lies before the deceased, from the initial blast of the Trumpet to the final abode, whether in Paradise or in the Fire. And praise be to God, the praise of the thankful.

[The second part of the book: The Remembrance of Death, concerning the states of the deceased from the time of the Trumpet's blast to the final settlement in Paradise or the Fire, and a detailing of the terrors and perils that lie before him.] In it is an explanation of the Trumpet's blast, the description of the land of the Gathering and its people, the description of the length of the Day of Resurrection, the description of the Day of Resurrection and its calamities and its names, the description of the questioning about sins, the description of the Scales, the description of the disputants and the restitution of wrongs, the description of the Bridge, the description of Intercession, the description of the Pool, the description of Hell and its terrors, its shackles, its serpents, and its scorpions, the description of Paradise and the varieties of its bliss, the number of its gardens, its gates, its chambers, its walls, its rivers, its trees, the clothing of its people, their furnishings and their couches, the description of their food, the description of the wide-eyed maidens and the immortal youths, the description of gazing upon the Countenance of God Almighty, and a chapter on the vastness of His mercy, Almighty is He, with which the book is concluded, God willing.

(Description of the Trumpet's Blast)
You have come to know in what preceded the states of the deceased in the agonies of death and his peril in the fear of the outcome, then his suffering the darkness of the grave and its worms, then [his encounter with] Munkar and Nakir and their questioning, then the torment of the grave and its peril if he is one upon whom wrath has fallen. Greater than all of that are the perils that lie before him: the blowing of the Trumpet, the resurrection on the Day of Rising, the presentation before the Compeller, the questioning about the little and the much, the setting up of the Scales to ascertain the measures, then the crossing of the Bridge despite its fineness and sharpness, then awaiting the call at the decree of judgment, either to felicity or to wretchedness. These are states and terrors which you must necessarily know, then believe in with certainty and affirmation, then prolong reflection upon, so that from your heart may arise the motives to prepare for them. Most people have not had faith in the Last Day enter the core of their hearts, nor has it taken firm root in the innermost recesses of their breasts. Indicative of this is their intense exertion and preparation for the heat of summer and the cold of winter, and their heedlessness regarding the heat of Hell and its bitter cold, along with the difficulties and terrors that encompass it. Rather, if they are asked about the Last Day, their tongues utter it, then their hearts become heedless of it. Whoever is informed that the food before him is poisoned, and says to his companion who saw it, "You have spoken the truth," then stretches forth his hands to take it, has affirmed with his tongue but belied with his action, and the denial of action is more severe than the denial of the tongue. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: (God Almighty said: The son of Adam has reviled Me, though it is not fitting for him to revile Me, and he has belied Me, though it is not fitting for him to belie Me. As for his reviling Me, it is his saying, 'I have a child.' As for his belying Me, it is his saying, 'He will not restore me as He originated me.') The weakness of the inner selves regarding the strength of certainty and affirmation of the resurrection and rising is only due to the lack of understanding in this world of such matters. If a person did not witness the procreation of animals and it was said to him that a maker creates from a drop of fluid a being like this fashioned, rational, speaking, and capable human, his inner self would strongly recoil from affirming it. Therefore, God Almighty said: "Does man not see that We created him from a drop? Then, behold, he is a clear adversary." And He said: "Does man think that he will be left neglected? Was he not a drop of emitted semen? Then he became a clinging clot; then He created and proportioned and made from him the two sexes, male and female." In the creation of the human, with the multitude of its wonders and the differing composition of its limbs, are wonders that exceed the wonders in his resurrection and restoration. So how can one who witnesses that in His creation and power deny that from the power and wisdom of God Almighty? If there is weakness in your faith, then strengthen faith by contemplating the first creation, for the second is like it and easier than it. If you are strong in faith regarding it, then make your heart feel those fears and perils, and increase in reflection and taking lesson therein, so that ease and tranquility may be stripped from your heart, and you may busy yourself with preparing for the presentation before the Compeller. First, reflect on what strikes the hearing of the inhabitants of the graves from the intensity of the Trumpet's blast, for it is a single cry by which the graves are split open over the heads of the deceased, and they rise up all at once. Imagine yourself having sprung forth, your face altered, your body dust-covered from your head to your feet from the dust of your grave, stunned by the severity of the shock, your eyes fixed towards the call, while creation has risen up in a single uprising from the graves in which their tribulation was long, and alarm and terror have roused them, added to what was with them of sorrows, griefs, and the intensity of awaiting the outcome of the matter, as He said...

He, the Exalted, said: "And the Trumpet will be blown, and all who are in the heavens and all who are on earth will fall dead, except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown again, and at once they will be standing, looking on." And He, the Exalted, said: "Then when the Trumpet is blown with a single blast, that Day will be a difficult day for the disbelievers, not easy." And He, the Exalted, said: "And they say, 'When is this promise, if you should be truthful?' They await not but one blast which will seize them while they are disputing. And they will not be able to make a testament, nor to their families will they return. And the Trumpet will be blown, and at once from the graves to their Lord they will hasten. They will say, 'O woe to us! Who has raised us from our sleeping place?' [The reply will be], 'This is what the Most Merciful had promised, and the messengers told the truth.'"

If there were nothing before the dead except the terror of that blast, it would be sufficient to inspire fear. For it is a blast and a shout by which all who are in the heavens and the earth are struck dead—meaning they die by it—except whom Allah wills, and that is some of the angels. For this reason, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "How can I be at ease when the bearer of the Trumpet has placed the horn to his mouth, lowered his forehead, and inclined his ear, awaiting when he will be commanded to blow?" Muqatil said: The Trumpet is the horn. Israfil, upon him be peace, places his mouth upon the horn like a trumpet, and the circumference of the horn's head is like the breadth of the heavens and the earth. He is gazing intently towards the Throne, waiting for when he will be commanded to blow the first blast. When he blows, all who are in the heavens and the earth are struck dead—meaning every living creature dies from the intensity of the terror—except whom Allah wills, and they are Gabriel, Michael, Israfil, and the Angel of Death. Then the Angel of Death is commanded to take the soul of Gabriel, then the soul of Michael, then the soul of Israfil. Then the Angel of Death is commanded, and he dies. Then the creation remains after the first blast in the Barzakh for forty years. Then Allah, the Exalted, revives Israfil and commands him to blow the second blast. That is His saying, the Exalted: "Then it will be blown again, and at once they will be standing, looking on." They will be standing on their feet, looking at the Resurrection. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "When I was sent as a prophet, I was sent to the bearer of the Trumpet. He brought it to his mouth, placed one foot forward and the other back, waiting for when he would be commanded to blow. So fear the blast."

Reflect upon the creation, their humiliation, their brokenness, and their submission at the time of being raised, in fear of this death-stroke and in anticipation of what is decreed for them of happiness or wretchedness. And you are among them, broken as they are broken, bewildered as they are bewildered. Rather, if you were among the affluent and the wealthy enjoying luxury in this world, the kings of the earth on that Day are the most humbled people of the gathering place, the smallest and most insignificant of them. They will be trodden underfoot like ants. At that time, the wild beasts from the deserts and the mountains will come forward, their heads lowered, mingled with the creation after their wildness, humbled for the Day of Resurrection, not due to any sin they have been defiled by, but their gathering is due to the intensity of the death-stroke and the terror of the blast, and that preoccupies them from fleeing from the creation and being wild among them. That is His saying, the Exalted: "And when the wild beasts are gathered." Then the rebellious devils, after their rebellion and insolence, will come forward, submitting humbly from the awe of the presentation before Allah, the Exalted, confirming His saying, the Exalted: "So by your Lord, We will surely gather them and the devils; then We will bring them around Hell on their knees." So reflect upon your state and the state of your heart there.

(Description of the Gathering Ground and Its People)

Then observe how they are driven after the resurrection and being raised, barefoot, naked, uncircumcised, to the Gathering Ground—a white land, a level plain. You see in it no crookedness nor elevation. You see upon it no hill behind which a person can hide, nor a depression lowering from sight. Rather, it is a single, smooth, level ground with no variation. They are driven to it in groups. So glory be to the One who gathers the creation despite the differences in their kinds from the corners of the earth when He drives them with the Shaker, followed by the Follower. The Shaker is the first blast, and the Follower is the second blast. It is truly fitting for those hearts to be trembling on that Day and for those eyes to be humbled. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "The people will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection on a white, reddish-white earth like a pure loaf of bread, with no landmark for anyone." The narrator said: Al-'Afrah is a whiteness that is not brilliant, and an-Naqee is the pure flour free from bran and husk. 'No landmark' means there is no structure to provide cover, nor variation to divert the gaze. Do not think that land is like the earth of this world. Rather, they are equal only in name. He, the Exalted, said: "On the Day the earth will be replaced by another earth, and the heavens [as well]." Ibn 'Abbas said: It increases and decreases, and its trees, mountains, valleys, and what is in it vanish. It is stretched out like the stretching of the hide of the 'Ukaz market—a white land like silver, upon which no blood has been spilled and upon which no sin has been committed. The heavens lose their sun, moon, and stars. So look, O wretched one, at the terror and severity of that Day. For when the creation is gathered on this level ground, the stars of the sky will scatter above them, the sun and moon will be extinguished, and the earth will darken as its lamp is quenched.

While they were in that state, the heavens above their heads began to revolve and split apart, despite their immense thickness and solidity of five hundred years, with angels standing upon their edges and corners. Imagine the terror of the sound of their splitting in your hearing, and the awe of the day when the sky will split apart despite its firmness and strength, then collapse and flow like molten silver, tinged with a yellowness until it becomes like red oil. The sky will become like molten brass, the mountains like carded wool, and people will be scattered like moths, walking barefoot and naked. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "People will be resurrected barefoot, naked, and uncircumcised, with sweat overwhelming them, reaching up to their earlobes." Sawdah, the wife of the Prophet and narrator of the hadith, said: "I exclaimed, 'O Messenger of God, how terrible! Will we see each other?' He replied, 'The people will be too preoccupied with their own affairs: "Every man that Day will have concern enough to make him heedless."'" So reflect greatly on the day when private parts will be exposed, and yet looking and turning will be safe. How much more so when some will be walking on their bellies and faces, unable to turn to look at others. Abu Hurairah, may God be pleased with him, reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "People will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection in three groups: riders, walkers, and on their faces." A man asked, "O Messenger of God, how can they walk on their faces?" He said, "The One who made them walk on their feet is capable of making them walk on their faces." It is in human nature to deny anything one is not accustomed to. Had a person not seen a snake slithering on its belly like a flash of lightning, they would deny the possibility of moving without legs. Even walking with legs seems improbable to one who has not witnessed it. Beware of denying any of the wonders of the Day of Resurrection simply because they contradict worldly analogies, for if you had not witnessed the wonders of this world and they were described to you beforehand, you would have denied them even more vehemently. So envision in your heart your own image: standing naked, exposed, humiliated, defeated, bewildered, stunned, awaiting the decree that will befall you—whether bliss or misery. Magnify this state in your mind, for it is immense.

(Description of the Sweat)

Then contemplate the crowding of creation and their assembly, until the inhabitants of the seven heavens and seven earths—angels, jinn, humans, devils, beasts, predators, and birds—are crammed into the gathering place. The sun will rise upon them, its heat multiplied and its nature transformed from its former mildness. It will be brought near to the heads of all beings, as close as the distance of two bow-lengths or nearer. No shadow will remain on earth except the shadow of the Lord of the Worlds, and none will be able to take shelter in it except those brought near. So among them will be those shaded by the Throne, and those exposed to the sun's heat, melted by its blaze, their distress and anguish intensified by its scorching. Then the creatures will jostle and push one another due to the severe crowding and differing paces, compounded by intense shame and modesty from exposure and the desire to hide when presented before the Compeller of the heavens. Thus, the scorching of the sun, the heat of breaths, and the burning of hearts with the fire of shame and fear will combine, causing sweat to gush from the root of every hair until it flows upon the plain of Resurrection. Then it will rise upon their bodies according to their ranks with God: for some, the sweat will reach their knees; for others, their waists; for others, to their earlobes; and for others, they will nearly be submerged in it. Ibn 'Umar reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "On the Day when people stand before the Lord of the Worlds, one of them will be submerged in his sweat up to half his ears." Abu Hurairah reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "People will sweat on the Day of Resurrection until their sweat goes seventy cubits into the earth, overwhelming them and reaching their ears." So it is narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim in the Sahih. In another hadith: "Standing, their eyes fixed on the sky for forty years, sweat will overwhelm them from the intensity of distress." 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "The sun will draw near to the earth on the Day of Resurrection, and people will sweat. Among them, some will have sweat reaching their ankles, some halfway up their shins, some their knees, some their thighs, some their waists, and some their mouths"—and he gestured with his hand to his mouth—"and some will be covered by sweat," and he struck his hand upon his head like this. So reflect, O wretched one, upon the sweat of the people of the gathering and the intensity of their distress, among whom will be those who cry out, "My Lord, relieve me from this distress and waiting, even if to the Fire!" And all this before they have even faced the reckoning or punishment. For you are one of them, and you do not know how high the sweat will reach you. Know that every sweat not expended through exertion in the path of God—in pilgrimage, jihad, fasting, night prayer, striving to fulfill a Muslim's need, or bearing hardship in enjoining good and forbidding evil—will be extracted by shame and fear on the plain of Resurrection, and the distress will be prolonged. If the son of Adam were saved from ignorance and delusion, he would know that the sweat of exertion in bearing the difficulties of obedience is a lighter matter and shorter in duration than the sweat of distress and waiting on the Day of Resurrection.

A day of immense gravity, its intensity prolonged, its duration lengthy.
                            (Description of the Length of the Day of Resurrection)
A day when the creatures will stand, their eyes staring, their hearts rent asunder. They will not speak, nor will any regard be given to their affairs. They will stand for three hundred years, not eating a single meal therein, nor drinking a single drink, nor finding therein the breath of a breeze. Ka'b and Qatadah said concerning, "The Day when mankind will stand before the Lord of the worlds" (83:6), that they will stand for the measure of three hundred years. Nay, Abdullah ibn 'Amr reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) recited this verse and then said: "How would it be with you if God gathered you as arrows are gathered in a quiver for fifty thousand years and did not look at you?" And al-Hasan said: "What is your thought concerning a day in which they stood upon their feet for the measure of fifty thousand years, not eating a single meal therein, nor drinking a single drink, until when their necks were severed from thirst and their bellies burned from hunger, they were turned to the Fire and given to drink from a boiling spring whose heat had reached its peak and whose scorching blaze had intensified. When their utmost exertion reached what they had no power to bear, some of them spoke to others, seeking one who would be honored by his Lord to intercede on their behalf. But they clung to no prophet except that he pushed them away and said, 'Leave me, myself, myself! My own affair preoccupies me from the affair of another.' And each one excused himself due to the severity of the wrath of God Almighty, saying, 'Our Lord has become wrathful today a wrath like which He has never been wrathful before, nor will He be wrathful after its like,' until our Prophet (peace be upon him) intercedes for those for whom permission is granted therein: 'None will possess the power of intercession except he to whom the Most Merciful gives permission and approves of his word' (20:109). So contemplate the length of this day and the severity of waiting therein, so that the waiting for patience from sins in your brief lifespan may become light upon you. And know that whoever's waiting in this world for death is prolonged due to the severity of his struggle for patience against desires, his waiting on that Day in particular will be shortened." The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said, when asked about the length of that day: "By the One in Whose Hand is my soul, it will indeed be lightened for the believer until it becomes easier for him than a prescribed prayer he prays in the world." So strive to be among those believers. As long as a breath of your life remains, the matter is up to you, and preparation is in your hands. So work in short days for long days, gaining a profit whose joy has no end. And deem insignificant your lifespan—nay, the lifespan of this world, which is seven thousand years—for if you were to be patient for, for example, seven thousand years to be delivered from a day whose measure is fifty thousand, your profit would be great and your toil slight.
                      (Description of the Day of Resurrection, its Calamities, and its Names)
So prepare, O wretched one, for this day of tremendous import, lengthy time, overpowering dominion, and imminent arrival. A day when you will see the sky split asunder, the stars scattered from its terror, the shining stars extinguished, the sun rolled up, the mountains set in motion, the pregnant camels neglected, the wild beasts gathered, the seas set ablaze, the souls paired with their bodies, Hellfire stoked, Paradise brought near, the mountains pulverized, the earth stretched forth. A day when you will see the earth quaking with its quake, and the earth will cast out its burdens. On that Day, mankind will proceed in diverse groups to be shown their deeds. A day when the earth and the mountains will be lifted and crushed with a single crushing. Then on that Day, the Inevitable Event will occur, and the sky will be cleft asunder, for it will be frail on that Day, and the angels will be at its edges. And the Throne of your Lord will be borne above them on that Day by eight. On that Day you will be presented, nothing of you hidden. A day when the mountains will move and you will see the earth laid bare. A day when the earth will be shaken with a shaking, and the mountains will be crumbled to powder, becoming scattered dust. A day when mankind will be like scattered moths, and the mountains will be like carded wool. A day when every nursing mother will be distracted from that which she nursed, and every pregnant female will deliver her burden, and you will see mankind intoxicated, yet they are not intoxicated, but the punishment of God is severe. A day when the earth will be changed to a different earth, and the heavens, and they will appear before God, the One, the Subduer. A day when the mountains will be blown away, leaving a level plain wherein you will see no crookedness nor curvature. A day when you will see the mountains, thinking them firmly fixed, yet they will pass like the passing of clouds. A day when the sky will be split open, becoming rose-colored like oil. Then on that Day, no human or jinn will be asked about his sin. A day when the disobedient will be prevented from speech, and no inquiry will be made therein about crimes; rather, they will be seized by the forelocks and the feet. A day when every soul will find what it did of good present, and what it did of evil—it will wish there were a vast distance between it and that. A day when every soul will know what it has brought forth, and will bear witness to what it sent ahead and left behind. A day when tongues will be silenced and limbs will speak. A day whose mention turned grey the Master of the Messengers when al-Siddiq (may God be pleased with him) said to him: "I see you have turned grey, O Messenger of God." He said: "Surah Hud and its sisters turned me grey"—and they are al-Waqi'ah, al-Mursalat, 'Amma yatasa'alun, and Idha al-shamsu kuwirat. So O incapable reader, your portion from your reading is merely that you mumble the Quran and move your tongue with it.

If you were truly contemplating what you recite, you would be worthy of having your gall bladder burst from the bitterness that tinged the hair of the Master of the Messengers. If you content yourself with the movement of the tongue, you have been deprived of the fruit of the Qur'an. The Resurrection is one of the matters mentioned therein, and Allah has described some of its calamities and multiplied its names, so that through the abundance of its names we may comprehend the abundance of its meanings. The purpose of the numerous names is not the mere repetition of names and titles; rather, the aim is to alert those of understanding. Beneath each name of the Resurrection lies a secret, and within every attribute ascribed to it is a meaning. Therefore, strive to know their meanings. We shall now gather its names for you. They are: The Day of Resurrection, the Day of Regret, the Day of Remorse, the Day of Reckoning, the Day of Questioning, the Day of Racing, the Day of Scrutiny, the Day of Competition, the Day of the Earthquake, the Day of the Great Convulsion, the Day of the Thunderbolt, the Day of the Inevitable, the Day of the Striking Calamity, the Day of the Quaking, the Day of the Successive Blow, the Day of the Overwhelming Event, the Day of the Disaster, the Day of the Approaching, the Day of the Inevitable Truth, the Day of the Overwhelming Catastrophe, the Day of the Deafening Blast, the Day of the Meeting, the Day of Separation, the Day of the Drive, the Day of Retribution, the Day of the Mutual Calling, the Day of Account, the Day of Return, the Day of Punishment, the Day of Flight, the Day of the Abode, the Day of the Meeting, the Day of Permanence, the Day of the Decree, the Day of Recompense, the Day of Trial, the Day of Weeping, the Day of Gathering, the Day of the Threat, the Day of the Presentation, the Day of the Weighing, the Day of Truth, the Day of Judgment, the Day of Decision, the Day of Assembly, the Day of Raising, the Day of Victory, the Day of Disgrace, a Great Day, a Barren Day, a Difficult Day, the Day of Recompense, the Day of Certainty, the Day of Emergence, the Day of Destination, the Day of the Blast, the Day of the Shout, the Day of the Tremor, the Day of the Great Quake, the Day of the Stern Command, the Day of Stupefaction, the Day of Terror, the Day of the End, the Day of Distress, the Day of the Abode, the Day of the Appointed Time, the Day of Refuge, the Day of the Watch, the Day of Anxiety, the Day of Sweat, the Day of Need, the Day of Denial, the Day of Dispersal, the Day of Splitting, the Day of Standing, the Day of Emergence, the Day of Eternity, the Day of Mutual Loss and Gain, a Frowning Day, a Known Day, the Hour, a Witnessed Day, a Day about which there is no doubt, a Day when secrets are tested, a Day when no soul will avail another in the least, a Day when gazes will be fixed, a Day when no protector will avail another in the least, a Day when no soul will have power for another, a Day when they will be called to the Fire of Hell, a Day when they will be dragged upon their faces into the Fire, a Day when their faces will be turned over in the Fire, a Day when no parent will avail his child, a Day when a man will flee from his brother, his mother, and his father, a Day when they will not speak nor be permitted to offer excuses, a Day from which there is no repelling from Allah, a Day when they will be exposed, a Day when they will be tried over the Fire, a Day when wealth and children will not avail, a Day when the wrongdoers' excuses will not avail them, and for them is the curse, and for them is the evil abode, a Day when excuses will be returned, secrets will be tested, consciences will be laid bare, and veils will be removed, a Day when gazes will be downcast, voices will be stilled, turning away will be scarce, hidden things will be exposed, and sins will be manifest, a Day when the servants will be driven, with their witnesses accompanying them, the young will turn grey, and the old will be stupefied. On that Day, the Scales will be set up, the Records will be spread open, Hellfire will be made manifest, the scalding water will boil, the Fire will roar, the disbelievers will despair, the Fires will be stoked, complexions will be changed, the tongue will be silenced, and the limbs of man will speak. O mankind, what has deluded you concerning your Generous Lord, when the doors are closed, the curtains are drawn, and you are concealed from creation, yet you commit immorality? What will you do when your own limbs bear witness against you? So woe, utter woe to us, the company of the heedless! Allah sends to us the Master of the Messengers and reveals to him the Clear Book, informing us of these attributes describing the Day of Recompense. Then He makes known our heedlessness, saying: "The reckoning of the people has drawn near, while they are in heedlessness, turning away. No mention comes to them from their Lord, newly revealed, but they listen to it while they are playing, their hearts distracted." Then He informs us of the nearness of the Hour, saying: "The Hour has drawn near, and the moon has split." "Indeed, they see it as distant, but We see it as near." "And what will make you perceive? Perhaps the Hour is near." Then the best of our states is that we take the study of this Qur'an as a practice, yet we do not ponder its meanings, nor do we reflect upon the multitude of descriptions and names of this Day, nor do we prepare to escape its calamities. So we seek refuge in Allah from this heedlessness, unless Allah encompasses us with His vast mercy.

(Description of the Questioning)

Then reflect, O wretched one, after these states, upon the questioning that will be directed to you verbally, without an interpreter. You will be asked about the little and the much, the speck on a date-stone and the thin membrane covering it. While you are in the distress of the Resurrection, its sweat, and the severity of its great terrors, angels descend from the highest heaven with massive bodies and enormous forms, harsh and severe, commanded to seize the forelocks of the criminals to the standing place of presentation before the Compeller.

The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Verily, God Almighty has an angel between the two edges of whose eyes is a distance of one hundred years' journey." So what do you think of yourself when you witness, for example, these angels sent to you to take you to the station of presentation, and you see them, despite the immensity of their forms, humbled by the severity of the Day, trembling from what has become apparent of the wrath of the Compeller upon His servants? At their descent, no prophet, no saint, nor any righteous person remains but that they fall upon their chins in fear that they might be the ones taken. This is the state of those brought near, so what do you think of the sinful transgressors?

At that time, groups of people, from the intensity of terror, will hasten to say to the angels: "Is our Lord among you?" due to the grandeur of their procession and the intensity of their awe. The angels will be alarmed by their question, venerating their Creator from being among them, and they will call out with their voices, declaring their Lord transcendent above what the people of the earth have imagined, saying: "Glory be to our Lord! He is not among us, but He is coming thereafter."

At that point, the angels will stand in rows, encircling the creatures from all sides, and upon all of them will be the marks of humility and submission, and the state of fear and awe due to the severity of the Day. Then God Almighty will fulfill His word: "And We shall certainly question those to whom messengers were sent, and We shall certainly question the messengers. Then We shall relate to them with knowledge, and We were not absent." And His word: "So by your Lord, We will surely question them all about what they used to do."

Then He, glorified be He, will begin with the prophets: "The Day when God will gather the messengers and say, 'What response were you given?' They will say, 'We have no knowledge. Indeed, it is You who is Knower of the unseen.'" Oh, the severity of a day when the minds of the prophets are bewildered and their knowledge is erased from the intensity of awe, when they are asked, 'What response were you given?'—when they had been sent to the creatures and they had known. Their minds are stunned, so they do not know how to answer, and they say from the intensity of awe, 'We have no knowledge. Indeed, it is You who is Knower of the unseen.' And they are truthful at that time, for their intellects have fled and their knowledge has been erased, until God Almighty strengthens them.

Then Noah, peace be upon him, will be called and it will be said to him: 'Did you convey?' He will say: 'Yes.' It will be said to his people: 'Did it reach you?' They will say: 'No warner came to us.' Jesus, peace be upon him, will be brought, and God Almighty will say to him: 'Did you say to the people, "Take me and my mother as gods besides God"?' He will remain convulsing under the awe of this question for years. Oh, the greatness of a day when accountability is established upon the prophets with a question like this!

Then the angels will come forward and call out one by one: 'O so-and-so, son of so-and-so, come forth to the station of presentation!' At that, limbs will tremble, joints will shake, minds will be confounded, and groups will wish they could be taken to the Fire rather than have the foulness of their deeds presented before the Compeller and their coverings unveiled before the gathering of all creatures.

Before the questioning begins, the light of the Throne will appear—"and the earth will shine with the light of its Lord"—and every servant will be certain of the Compeller's approach to question the servants. Each one will think that no one sees him but Him, and that he alone is the one taken for accountability and questioning, to the exclusion of all others. Then the Compeller, glorified and exalted be He, will say at that time: 'O Gabriel, bring the Fire.' Gabriel will come for it and say: 'O Hell, respond to your Creator and your Sovereign.' Gabriel will find it in its rage and wrath. No sooner is it called than it surges, boils, snorts towards the creatures, and gasps. The creatures will hear its rage and its snorting, and its keepers will rise up, springing towards the creatures in wrath against those who disobeyed God Almighty and opposed His command.

So let your mind consider and your heart envision the state of the servants' hearts when they are filled with terror and dread. They will fall down on their knees and turn their backs in flight—"the Day you will see every nation kneeling"—and some of them will fall upon their faces, prone. The sinners and wrongdoers will cry out, 'Woe! Ruin!' and the truthful will cry, 'Myself! Myself!'

While they are in that state, Hell will snort its second snort, doubling their fear and causing their strength to fail, and they will think they are being taken. Then it will snort its third snort, and the creatures will fall upon their faces, and they will stare with their eyes, looking from a hidden, humble corner. At that, the hearts of the wrongdoers will be crushed, reaching their throats, choking, and the minds of the blissful and the wretched alike will be bewildered.

Thereafter, God Almighty will turn to the messengers and say, 'What response were you given?' When they see what accountability has been established upon the prophets, terror will intensify upon the sinners. The parent will flee from their child, the brother from his brother, the husband from his wife, and each one will remain awaiting his own command.

Then they will be taken one by one, and God Almighty will question him directly about the little and the much of his deeds, about his secret and his public acts, and about all his limbs and organs. Abu Hurairah said: They asked, 'O Messenger of God, will we see our Lord on the Day of Resurrection?' He said, 'Do you have any difficulty in seeing the sun at midday when there is no cloud obscuring it?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'Do you have any difficulty in seeing the moon on a night when it is full and there is no cloud obscuring it?' They said, 'No.' He said, 'By the One in whose hand is my soul, you will have no difficulty in seeing your Lord.' Then the servant will be cast and he will say...

Did I not honor you, make you master, give you in marriage, and subjugate horses and camels for you, allowing you to lead and dwell in comfort? The servant will say, "Yes." He will say, "Did you suppose you would meet Me?" The servant will say, "No." He will then say, "I will forget you as you forgot Me." Imagine yourself, O wretched one, when the angels have taken you by your arms and you are standing before God, exalted is He, and He questions you directly, saying: "Did I not bestow youth upon you? In what did you expend it? Did I not grant you respite in life? In what did you waste it? Did I not provide you with wealth? From where did you earn it, and on what did you spend it? Did I not honor you with knowledge? What did you do with what you learned?" How then do you see your shame and disgrace as He enumerates His blessings upon you and your acts of disobedience, His favors and your misdeeds? If you deny, your own limbs will testify against you. Anas, may God be pleased with him, said: We were with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and he laughed, then said, "Do you know why I laughed?" We said, "God and His Messenger know best." He said, "From the servant's dialogue with his Lord. He will say, 'O Lord, did You not protect me from injustice?' He will say, 'Yes.' He will then say, 'I do not accept for Myself any witness except from Myself.' He will say, 'Your own soul is sufficient as a reckoner against you today, and the noble scribes as witnesses.'" He said, "Then his mouth will be sealed, and it will be said to his limbs, 'Speak.'" He said, "So they will speak with his deeds. Then he will be left to speak, and he will say to his limbs, 'Away with you, be gone! It was for your sake that I strayed.'" So we seek refuge in God from being exposed before the entire creation by the testimony of the limbs, except that God, exalted is He, has promised the believer that He will cover him and not expose him to others. A man asked Ibn 'Umar, saying to him, "How did you hear the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, speak concerning the private discourse?" He said, "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'One of you will be brought so near to his Lord that He places His veil over him and says, "Did you do such and such?" He will say, "Yes." He will say, "Did you do such and such?" He will say, "Yes." Then He will say, "I concealed it for you in the world, and I forgive it for you today."'" And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever conceals the fault of a believer, God will conceal his fault on the Day of Resurrection." This is only hoped for a believing servant who concealed people's faults, bore their shortcomings against himself, did not move his tongue to mention their misdeeds, and did not speak of them in their absence with what they would dislike if they heard it. Such a one is worthy of being recompensed with the same on the Day of Resurrection. Even if He has concealed it from others, has not the call to the presentation reached your hearing? Is not that terror sufficient recompense for your sins, when you are seized by your forelock and led forth, your heart agitated, your mind bewildered, your limbs trembling, your color changed, and the world dark upon you from the intensity of the terror? Imagine yourself in this state, stepping over necks, breaking through rows, being led as a worn-out horse is led, while all creation has raised their eyes to you. Imagine yourself in the hands of those entrusted with you in this state until they bring you to the Throne of the Merciful, then cast you from their hands, and God, glorious and exalted is He, calls you with His mighty word: "O son of Adam, draw near to Me." So you draw near to Him with a palpitating, sorrowful, fearful, and humble heart, a downcast gaze, and a broken heart, and you are given your record, which leaves nothing small or great but that it has accounted it. How many obscenities you had forgotten, then remembered! How many acts of obedience you were heedless of their faults, then their defects were unveiled to you! How much shame and cowardice is yours! How much constraint and incapacity is yours! I wonder, upon which foot will you stand before Him, with which tongue will you answer, with which heart will you comprehend what you say? Then reflect upon the magnitude of your life when He reminds you of your sins directly, saying: "O My servant, were you not ashamed of Me, yet you confronted Me with the ugly, and were ashamed of My creation, so you showed them the good?
