Was I more trivial to you than My other servants? You took lightly My observation of you and did not care, yet you deemed great the observation of others. Did I not bestow favors upon you? What made you heedless of Me? Did you suppose that I do not see you and that you would not meet Me?" The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "There is not one of you except that God, the Lord of the worlds, will question him, with no veil between them and no interpreter." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "One of you will surely stand before God, mighty and majestic, with no veil between them, and He will say to him, 'Did I not bestow favors upon you? Did I not give you what you have?' He will say, 'Yes.' He will say, 'Did I not send a messenger to you?' He will say, 'Yes.' Then he will look to his right and see nothing but Hellfire, then look to his left and see nothing but Hellfire. So let one of you protect himself from the Fire, even with half a date; if he does not find that, then with a good word.'" Ibn Mas'ud said it similarly: "There is not one of you except that God, mighty and majestic, will seclude Himself with him as one of you secludes himself with the moon on the night of the full moon, then He will say, 'O son of Adam, what made you heedless of Me? O son of Adam, what did you do with what you knew? O son of Adam, how did you answer the messengers? O son of Adam, was I not a watcher over your eye when you looked with it at what is not lawful for you? Was I not a watcher over your ears?'" And so on, enumerating all his other limbs. And Mujahid said: "The feet of a servant will not move from before God, mighty and majestic, on the Day of Resurrection until he is questioned about four matters: about his life, in what he spent it; about his knowledge, what he did with it; about his body..."

In what he has expended and from his wealth, from where he earned it and on what he spent it. So be awed, O wretched one, by your shame before that, and by your peril, for you are between being told, "I concealed it for you in the world, and I forgive it for you today," at which your joy and delight would be immense, and the former and later generations would envy you; or it being said to the angels, "Take this evil servant, bind him, then cast him into Hell," at which, if the heavens and the earth were to weep for you, it would be fitting for the enormity of your calamity and the intensity of your regret for what you neglected of obedience to God and for what you sold your Hereafter for—a base world that did not remain with you.

Then do not neglect to contemplate the Balance and the flying of the books to the right and the left. For after the questioning, people are of three groups: a group who have no good deed, so a black neck emerges from the Fire, gathering them as a bird gathers seeds, enfolds them, and casts them into the Fire, and the Fire swallows them, and a call is made upon them: "Misery, after which there is no happiness." Another group have no evil deed, so a caller calls out, "Let those who praise God in every circumstance rise," so they rise and are sent forth to Paradise. Then the same is done for the people who pray at night, then for those whom worldly trade and its sale did not distract from the remembrance of God Almighty, and a call is made upon them: "Happiness, after which there is no misery." A third group remains, and they are the majority, who mixed a righteous deed and another evil one. It may be hidden from them, but it is not hidden from God Almighty, whether their good deeds or their evil deeds predominate. But God refuses except to make them know that, to manifest His grace in pardon and His justice in punishment. So the scrolls and books fly, enfolded upon the good deeds and evil deeds, and the Balance is set up, and gazes are fixed upon the books—will they fall to the right or to the left?—then upon the tongue of the Balance—will it incline to the side of evil deeds or to the side of good deeds? This is a tremendous state in which the minds of creation are bewildered. Al-Hasan narrated: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, had his head in 'A'ishah's lap, may God be pleased with her, and he dozed. She remembered the Hereafter and wept until her tears flowed and dropped onto the cheek of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. He awoke and said, 'What makes you weep, O 'A'ishah?' She said, 'I remembered the Hereafter. Will you remember your families on the Day of Resurrection?' He said, 'By the One in Whose hand is my soul, in three places no one will remember except himself: when the scales are placed and the deeds are weighed, until a son of Adam sees whether his scale is light or heavy; and at the scrolls, until he sees whether he takes his book with his right hand or his left; and at the Bridge.'"

From Anas: "The son of Adam will be brought on the Day of Resurrection until he is made to stand between the two pans of the Balance, and an angel is entrusted with him. If his scale is heavy, the angel calls out with a voice heard by all creation, 'So-and-so is happy, a happiness after which he will never be miserable.' If his scale is light, he calls out with a voice heard by all creation, 'So-and-so is miserable, a misery after which he will never be happy.' And when the pan of good deeds is light, the Zabaniyah advance, with iron maces in their hands, wearing garments of fire, and they take the share of the Fire to the Fire." The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said regarding the Day of Resurrection: "It is a day when God Almighty calls Adam, peace be upon him, and says to him, 'Rise, O Adam, and send forth the contingent to the Fire.' He says, 'And how many is the contingent to the Fire?' He says, 'From every thousand, nine hundred and ninety-nine.' When the Companions heard that, they were dismayed until not one of them showed a smile. When the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, saw what was with his Companions, he said, 'Strive and receive glad tidings, for by the One in Whose hand is Muhammad's soul, with you are two creations that were never with anyone except they outnumbered those who perished from the Children of Adam and the Children of Iblis.' They said, 'And what are they, O Messenger of God?' He said, 'Gog and Magog.' So relief came to the people. Then he said, 'Strive and receive glad tidings, for by the One in Whose hand is Muhammad's soul, you among people on the Day of Resurrection are but like a mole on a camel's side or like a mark on a beast's foreleg.'"

You have known the terror of the Balance and its peril, and that eyes are fixed upon the tongue of the Balance: "Then as for him whose scales are heavy, he will be in a pleasant life. But as for him whose scales are light, his refuge will be an abyss. And what will convey to you what that is? A blazing Fire." And know that none is saved from the peril of the Balance except he who, in this world, held his soul to account and weighed therein with the scale of the Sacred Law his deeds, his words, his passing thoughts, and his glances, as 'Umar, may God be pleased with him, said: "Hold yourselves to account before you are held to account, and weigh yourselves before you are weighed." His holding his soul to account is that he repents from every sin before death with sincere repentance, makes up for what he neglected of his shortcoming in the obligations due to God Almighty, and restores wrongs, grain by grain, and seeks absolution from everyone his tongue, his hand, or the evil suspicion of his heart has wronged, with their hearts being content, until he dies and no wrong or obligation remains upon him. Such a one enters Paradise without reckoning. But if he dies before restoring wrongs, his adversaries surround him, this one taking him by the hand and that one...

He will seize him by his forelock, and this one will grab him by his collar. This one says, "You wronged me," and this one says, "You insulted me," and this one says, "You ridiculed me," and this one says, "You mentioned me in my absence with what displeases me," and this one says, "You were my neighbor and you violated my neighborly rights," and this one says, "You dealt with me and you cheated me," and this one says, "You sold to me and you defrauded me, concealing the defect of your merchandise from me," and this one says, "You lied about the price of your goods," and this one says, "You saw me in need while you were wealthy, yet you did not feed me," and this one says, "You found me wronged while you were capable of repelling the wrong from me, yet you appeased the wrongdoer and did not consider me."

While you are in that state, and the adversaries have sunk their claws into you and firmly grasped your collars with their hands, and you are bewildered and perplexed by their multitude—to the point that there remains no one in your lifetime with whom you transacted for a dirham or sat with in a gathering except that they have a rightful claim against you for a wrong through backbiting, betrayal, or a look of contempt—and you have weakened in resisting them, and you have stretched forth the neck of hope to your Master and Lord, hoping He might deliver you from their grasp, then the call of the Almighty, Glorious is His Majesty, strikes your hearing: "Today every soul will be recompensed for what it earned. No injustice today!" (Qur'an 40:17). At that moment, your heart is torn out from awe, and your soul becomes certain of ruin, and you remember what God, Exalted is He, warned you through the tongue of His Messenger, where He said: "And never think that Allah is unaware of what the wrongdoers do. He only delays them for a Day when eyes will stare [in horror]. Racing ahead, their heads raised up, their glance does not come back to them, and their hearts are void. And, warn the people..." (Qur'an 14:42-44) the verse.

How great was your joy today in savoring people's reputations and taking their wealth, and how severe will be your regrets on that Day when your Lord stands upon the carpet of justice and you are presented for the address of reckoning, while you are bankrupt, poor, helpless, and humiliated, unable to restore a right or present an excuse. At that time, your good deeds, for which you toiled your entire life, will be taken and transferred to your adversaries in lieu of their rights.

Abu Hurairah reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "Do you know who the bankrupt one is?" We said, "The bankrupt among us is one who has no dirham nor dinar nor property." He said, "The bankrupt from my nation is the one who comes on the Day of Resurrection with prayer, fasting, and zakah, but he comes having insulted this one, slandered that one, consumed the wealth of this one, shed the blood of that one, and struck this one. So, his good deeds are given to this one and that one. If his good deeds are exhausted before what is upon him is settled, then their sins are taken and cast upon him, then he is cast into the Fire." So, look at your calamity on such a Day, when not a single good deed of yours is safe from the afflictions of ostentation and the snares of Satan. If a single good deed remains safe over a long period, your adversaries will rush to it and take it. Perhaps if you were to hold yourself to account while being diligent in fasting the day and praying at night, you would know that not a day passes you by except that there flows from your tongue backbiting of the Muslims sufficient to consume all your good deeds. So how about the rest of the sins, such as consuming the unlawful and doubtful matters, and shortcomings in acts of obedience? And how can you hope for deliverance from wrongs on a Day when recompense will be taken for the hornless from the horned?

It has been narrated from Abu Dharr: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, saw two sheep butting each other and said, "O Abu Dharr, do you know why they are butting each other?" I said, "No." He said, "But Allah knows, and He will judge between them on the Day of Resurrection."

And Abu Hurairah said regarding the saying of God, Mighty and Majestic: "There is no creature on the earth or bird that flies with its wings except that they are communities like you." (Qur'an 6:38) that all creatures will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection—the beasts, the animals, the birds, and everything. The justice of God, Exalted is He, will reach such a degree that He will take recompense for the hornless from the horned. Then He will say, "Be dust." That is when the disbeliever will say, "I wish I were dust." So you, O wretched one, on a day when you see your record empty of the good deeds for which you long toiled, you will say, "Where are my good deeds?" It will be said, "They have been transferred to the records of your adversaries." And you will see your record laden with sins, for which you long endured fatigue and strove hard to abstain, and you will say, "O Lord, these are sins I never committed." It will be said, "These are the sins of the people whom you backbit, insulted, intended harm for, and wronged in transactions, neighborly relations, speech, debate, conversation, study, and all other types of dealings."

Ibn Mas'ud reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "Indeed, Satan has despaired of being worshipped through idols in the land of the Arabs, but he will be content with you through what is less than that: through the 'insignificant' sins, which are the destructive ones. So, guard against wrongdoing as much as you are able. For indeed, a servant will come on the Day of Resurrection with good deeds like mountains, thinking they will save him. Then one person after another will come and say, 'O Lord, so-and-so wronged me with a wrong.' So He will say, 'Take from his good deeds.' And it will continue like that until nothing of his good deeds remains. The likeness of that is a group of travelers who alight in a desert with no firewood. The people disperse and gather firewood. It is not long before they have made their fire great and cooked what they desired." Similarly, the sins... (And when the saying of God, Exalted is He, was revealed: "Indeed, you...")

Dead, and they are dead; then on the Day of Resurrection before your Lord you will dispute." Al-Zubayr said: "O Messenger of God, will what was between us in this world be repeated upon us, along with the specific sins?" He said: "Yes, it will indeed be repeated upon you until every right-holder is given his due right." Al-Zubayr said: "By God, the matter is severe." So he magnified the severity of a day in which no step is pardoned, and no slap nor word is overlooked, until the wronged is vindicated from the wrongdoer. Anas said: I heard the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, say: "God will resurrect the servants naked, barefoot, and uncircumcised." We said: "What does 'barefoot' mean?" He said: "They will have nothing with them. Then their Lord, the Exalted, will call them with a voice heard by those far away as it is heard by those near: 'I am the King, I am the Judge. It is not fitting for anyone from the people of Paradise to enter Paradise while anyone from the people of Hell has a grievance against him until I exact it from him, nor for anyone from the people of Hell to enter Hell while anyone from the people of Paradise has a grievance against him until I exact it from him—even for a slap.'" We said: "How can that be, when we come to God, the Mighty and Majestic, naked, barefoot, and uncircumcised?" He said: "Through good deeds and bad deeds."

So fear God, O servants of God, and the wrongs against servants: taking their wealth, violating their honor, constricting their hearts, and behaving poorly in companionship. For what is between a servant and God is private, and forgiveness from Him is swifter. But for one upon whom grievances have accumulated, and he has repented from them, yet finds it difficult to seek absolution from the claimants of those grievances, let him multiply his good deeds for the Day of Reckoning, and let him rejoice in some good deeds between him and God with perfect sincerity, such that none is aware of them except God. Perhaps that will bring him nearer to God, the Exalted, so that he attains by it His gentleness, which He has stored for His beloved believers in warding off the wrongs of servants from them.

As narrated from Anas from the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, that he said: "While the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was sitting, we saw him laugh until his front teeth showed. 'Umar said: 'What makes you laugh, O Messenger of God? May my father and mother be sacrificed for you!' He said: 'Two men from my nation knelt before the Lord of Might. One of them said: "O Lord, exact my grievance from my brother." God, the Exalted, said: "Give your brother his due." He said: "O Lord, none of his good deeds remain." God, the Exalted, said to the claimant: "What will you do, when none of his good deeds remain?" He said: "O Lord, let him bear some of my burdens."' And the eyes of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, overflowed with tears. Then he said: 'Indeed, that is a tremendous day, a day when people will need others to bear their burdens.' He said: 'Then God said to the claimant: "Raise your head and look into the Gardens." He raised his head and said: "O Lord, I see cities of elevated silver, and palaces of gold adorned with pearls. For which prophet is this, or for which truthful one, or for which martyr?" He said: "For whoever gives Me the price." He said: "O Lord, and who possesses its price?" He said: "You possess it." He said: "What is it?" He said: "Your pardoning your brother." He said: "O Lord, I have pardoned him." God, the Exalted, said: "Take your brother by the hand and admit him into Paradise."' Then the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said at that: 'Fear God and reconcile between yourselves, for God reconciles between the believers.'"

This is an alert that this is only attained by adorning oneself with the attributes of God, which is reconciling between people and all other noble traits. So reflect now upon yourself: if your record is free from wrongs, or gentleness has been shown to you until you were pardoned, and you are certain of eternal happiness—how will your joy be upon departing from the Plain of Gathering, when the garment of acceptance has been bestowed upon you, and you return with a happiness after which there is no misery, and a bliss at whose edges annihilation does not circle? At that, your heart will fly with joy and gladness, your face will become white, radiant, and shining like the full moon on its night. Imagine yourself proceeding among the creation, your head raised, your back free from burdens, the freshness of the breeze of bliss and the coolness of acceptance gleaming from your forehead, and the creation of the first and the last looking at you and your state, envying you for your beauty and comeliness, while angels walk before you and behind you, proclaiming atop all gatherings: "This is so-and-so, son of so-and-so; God is pleased with him and has made him pleased. He has attained a happiness after which he will never be miserable." Do you think this station is not greater than the position you attain in the hearts of creation in this world through your ostentation, hypocrisy, affectation, and adornment? If you know it is better than that—indeed, there is no comparison between them—then strive to reach this rank through pure sincerity and truthful intention in your dealings with God, for you will not attain it except by that.

But if it is the other—God forbid—that a sin you considered minor has emerged from your record, yet it is great with God, so He detested you because of it and said: "Upon you is My curse, O wicked servant! I do not accept your worship," then you will not hear this call except that your face turns black. Then the angels will become angry due to the anger of God, the Exalted, and they will say: "And upon you is our curse and the curse of all creation." At that, the Zabaniyah will descend upon you, having become angry due to the anger of their Creator, advancing upon you with their harshness, their terrifying cries, and their dreadful forms.

They seized your forelock, dragging you face-down before the entire creation as they gaze upon the blackening of your face and the exposure of your disgrace. You cry out in ruin and calamity, while they say to you, “Do not call today for a single calamity, but call for many calamities.” The angels proclaim, saying, “This is so-and-so, son of so-and-so; God has uncovered his scandals and his shameful deeds, and He has cursed him for his vile misdeeds.” Thus he is wretched with a wretchedness after which he will never know happiness. And perhaps that comes from a sin you committed secretly among God’s servants, or from seeking status in their hearts, or from fearing exposure before them. How immense is your ignorance when you guard against exposure before a small group of God’s servants in this perishing world, yet do not dread the tremendous exposure before that great assembly, along with facing God’s wrath and His painful punishment, and being dragged by the hands of the fierce guards to the midst of Hellfire. These are your states, while you remain unaware of the greatest peril—the peril of the Bridge.

Then, after these terrors, reflect on the words of God Almighty: “On the Day when We gather the righteous to the Most Merciful as a delegation, and drive the criminals to Hell as a thirsty herd,” and in His saying: “So guide them to the path of Hell. And stop them; indeed, they are to be questioned.” After these terrors, people are driven to the Bridge—a bridge stretched over the back of the Fire, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair. Whoever was upright in this world on the Straight Path will find the Bridge of the Hereafter light and will be saved; but whoever deviated from uprightness in this world, burdened his back with sins, and disobeyed will stumble at the first step on the Bridge and plummet. Consider now what terror would seize your heart when you see the Bridge and its fineness, then your sight falls upon the blackness of Hell beneath it, and your hearing is struck by the roaring and rage of the Fire—while you are obliged to walk on the Bridge in your weak state, with your heart agitated, your feet unsteady, and your back weighed down by sins that hinder you from walking even on the smooth earth, let alone on the sharpness of the Bridge. How will it be when you place one foot upon it and feel its sharpness, compelled to lift the second foot, while the creatures before you slip and stumble, and the guards of the Fire pull them down with hooks and grappling irons? You watch how they are overturned, their heads descending toward the Fire and their feet rising. What a dreadful sight, what a difficult ascent, and what a narrow passage! Look at your state as you crawl and climb upon it, burdened with your sins, glancing right and left at the creatures as they tumble into the Fire, while the Messenger, peace be upon him, says, “O Lord, grant safety, grant safety!” and the cries of ruin and calamity rise to you from the depths of Hell due to the multitude of creatures who slip from the Bridge. How would it be if your foot slipped and your regret availed you not, so you cry out in ruin and calamity, saying, “This is what I feared! Would that I had sent ahead for my life! Would that I had taken a way with the Messenger! Woe to me! Would that I had not taken so-and-so as a friend! Would that I were dust! Would that I were forgotten, utterly forgotten! Would that my mother had not borne me!” At that moment, the fires seize you—God forbid—and the caller calls out, “Be driven into it, and do not speak!” Then no recourse remains except screaming, groaning, panting, and pleading for help. How do you now regard your intellect, with these perils before you? If you do not believe in that, how long will your stay be with the disbelievers in the depths of Hell? And if you believe in it but are heedless of it and negligent in preparing for it, how great is your loss and transgression! What will your faith profit you if it does not spur you to strive in seeking the pleasure of God Almighty through obeying Him and abandoning disobedience? Even if nothing lay before you except the terror of the Bridge and the dread in your heart at the peril of crossing it—even if you are saved—that alone is sufficient as terror, fright, and horror. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: “The Bridge will be laid across the midst of Hellfire, and I will be the first of the messengers to cross with his community. On that day, none will speak except the messengers, and the supplication of the messengers that day will be: ‘O God, grant safety! O God, grant safety!’ In Hell are hooks like the thorns of the sa‘dan plant—have you seen the thorns of the sa‘dan?” They said, “Yes, O Messenger of God.” He said, “They are like the thorns of the sa‘dan, except that none knows the measure of their size except God Almighty. They snatch people according to their deeds: among them are those who are ruined by their deeds, and among them are those who are scratched but then saved.” And Abu Sa‘id al-Khudri reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: “People will pass over the bridge of Hell, upon which are thorns, hooks, and grappling irons that snatch people to the right and left. On its two sides are angels saying, ‘O God, grant safety! O God, grant safety!’ Among the people are those who pass like lightning, and those who pass like the wind, and those who pass like a galloping horse, and those who run, and those who walk, and those who crawl, and those who drag themselves. As for the people of the Fire who are its true inhabitants, they…”

They die and do not come to life, while others are seized for their sins and iniquities, then burned into embers, after which permission for intercession is granted." And he mentioned the rest of the hadith. And from Ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him, that he said: "God will gather the former and the latter for an appointed day, standing for forty years, their gazes fixed toward the sky, awaiting the decree." And he mentioned the hadith until he spoke of the time of the believers' prostration, saying: "Then He will say to the believers, 'Raise your heads,' so they raise their heads, and He gives them their light according to the measure of their deeds. Among them is he who is given light like a great mountain, moving before him; and among them is he whose light is smaller than that; and among them is he whose light is like a palm tree; and among them is he whose light is smaller than that, until the last of them is a man given light upon his big toe, illuminating at times and fading at others. When it illuminates, he places his foot and walks, and when it darkens, he stands still." Then he mentioned their crossing over the Bridge according to their light: among them are those who pass like the blink of an eye, and among them are those who pass like lightning, and among them are those who pass like clouds, and among them are those who pass like the shooting of stars, and among them are those who pass like the gallop of a horse, and among them are those who pass like the running of a man, until he who was given light upon his big toe passes, crawling on his face, his hands and feet dragging—one hand clinging, another dragging; one foot clinging, another dragging—his sides scorched by the Fire. He remains thus until he is delivered. When he is delivered, he stands upon it and says, 'Praise be to God, God has given me what He gave no one, for He saved me from it after I saw it.' Then he is taken to a pond at the gate of Paradise and washes." And Anas ibn Malik said: I heard the Messenger of God say: "The Bridge is like the edge of a sword or like the edge of a hair, and the angels rescue the believing men and women, and Gabriel, peace be upon him, is holding my waist, and I say, 'O Lord, safety, safety!' And many will slip and fall on that day." These are the terrors and enormities of the Bridge, so prolong your reflection upon it, for those who are saved from the terrors of the Day of Resurrection are those who prolonged their reflection upon it in this world. Indeed, God does not combine two fears upon a servant: whoever fears these terrors in this world will be secure from them in the Hereafter. And I do not mean by fear a tenderness like the tenderness of women, where your eye weeps and your heart softens upon hearing, then you soon forget and return to your diversion and play. What fear is there in that? Rather, whoever fears something flees from it, and whoever hopes for something seeks it. Nothing will save you except a fear that prevents you from the disobedience of God Almighty and urges you to His obedience. And far from the tenderness of women is the fear of the foolish: when they hear the terrors, seeking refuge springs to their tongues, so one of them says, 'I seek help from God, we seek refuge in God, O God, safety, safety!' while they persist in the disobedience that is the cause of their ruin. So Satan laughs at their seeking refuge, just as he laughs at one pursued by a predatory lion in a desert, behind whom is a fortress. When he sees the fangs of the lion and its ferocity from afar, he says with his tongue, 'I seek refuge in this impregnable fortress, and I seek help in the strength of its structure and the firmness of its pillars,' saying that with his tongue while sitting in his place. How can that avail him against the lion? Likewise, the terrors of the Hereafter have no fortress except the sincere saying of 'There is no god but God.' The meaning of its sincerity is that he has no object of desire besides God Almighty and no object of worship other than Him. And whoever takes his desire as his god is far from sincerity in his monotheism, and his affair is perilous within himself. If you are incapable of all that, then be a lover of the Messenger of God, eager to honor his traditions, yearning to heed the hearts of the righteous among his community, and seeking blessing through their supplications, so that perhaps you may attain from his intercession or their intercession, and be saved by intercession if your provision is scant.

(Description of Intercession)
Know that when entry into the Fire becomes due for groups among the believers, then God Almighty, by His grace, accepts intercession on their behalf from the prophets and the truthful, indeed from the scholars and the righteous, and everyone who has standing and good dealings with God Almighty—for he has intercession for his family, relatives, friends, and acquaintances. So be eager to acquire for yourself a rank of intercession with them, and that is by never despising any human being at all, for God Almighty has concealed His friendship within His servants—perhaps the one your eye belittles is a friend of God. And never deem any sin insignificant at all, for God Almighty has concealed His wrath within sins—perhaps God's displeasure lies therein. And never deem any obedience insignificant at all, for God Almighty has concealed His pleasure within obedience—perhaps His pleasure lies therein, even if it be a good word or a sincere intention or what resembles it. And evidences of intercession in the Qur'an and reports are many: God Almighty said: "And your Lord is going to give you, and you will be satisfied." It is narrated from 'Amr ibn al-'As: "That the Messenger of God recited the saying of Abraham, peace be upon him: 'My Lord, indeed they have led astray many of the people. So whoever follows me, then he is of me; and whoever disobeys me—indeed, You are Forgiving, Merciful,' and the saying of Jesus, peace be upon him: 'If

Then he raised his hands and said, "My community, my community," and wept. So Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said, "O Gabriel, go to Muhammad and ask him what makes him weep." Gabriel came to him and asked him, and he informed him—though Allah knows best—so He said, "O Gabriel, go to Muhammad and tell him: We shall please you concerning your community and not grieve you." And he (peace be upon him) said, "I have been given five things not given to anyone before me: I am aided by terror a month's journey away; spoils have been made lawful for me, though they were not lawful for anyone before me; the earth has been made a place of prostration and its soil pure for me, so wherever a man from my community is overtaken by prayer, let him pray; I have been granted intercession; and every prophet was sent to his own people specifically, but I have been sent to all people." And he (peace be upon him) said, "On the Day of Resurrection, I will be the leader of the prophets, their orator, and the possessor of their intercession—without boasting." And he (peace be upon him) said, "I am the master of the children of Adam, without boasting, and I am the first for whom the earth will split open, and the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted. In my hand will be the banner of praise, beneath which will be Adam and those after him." And he (peace be upon him) said, "Every prophet has a supplication that is answered, and I wish to reserve my supplication as intercession for my community on the Day of Resurrection." And Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, "Pulpits of gold will be set up for the prophets, and they will sit upon them, but my pulpit will remain—I will not sit on it, standing before my Lord, upright, fearing that I may be sent to Paradise while my community remains after me. So I will say, 'O Lord, my community!' And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, will say, 'O Muhammad, what do you wish Me to do with your community?' I will say, 'O Lord, hasten their reckoning.' Then I will continue to intercede until I am given writs for men who have been sent to the Fire, and until Malik, the keeper of Hell, says, 'O Muhammad, you have left no remnant for the Fire due to your Lord's anger toward your community.'" And he (peace be upon him) said, "Indeed, I will intercede on the Day of Resurrection for more than the stones and clay upon the face of the earth." And Abu Huraira said: Some meat was brought to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and the foreleg was raised to him—it used to please him—so he took a bite from it, then said, "I am the master of the messengers on the Day of Resurrection. And do you know why that is? Allah will gather the first and the last on a single plain; the caller will make them hear, and their sight will penetrate; the sun will draw near until the people are overcome with distress and anguish they cannot bear or endure. Then the people will say to one another, 'Do you not see what has befallen you? Will you not look for someone to intercede for you with your Lord?' Some will say to others, 'Go to Adam (peace be upon him).' So they will come to Adam and say, 'You are the father of mankind; Allah created you with His own hand, breathed into you of His spirit, and commanded the angels to prostrate to you. Intercede for us with your Lord. Do you not see our state? Do you not see what has befallen us?' Adam (peace be upon him) will say to them, 'My Lord is angry today with an anger like none before and none after. He forbade me the tree, and I disobeyed. Myself, myself! Go to another. Go to Noah.' So they will come to Noah (peace be upon him) and say, 'O Noah, you are the first messenger to the people of the earth, and Allah named you a grateful servant. Intercede for us with your Lord. Do you not see our state?' He will say, 'My Lord is angry today with an anger like none before and none after. I had a supplication which I invoked against my people. Myself, myself! Go to another. Go to Abraham, the friend of Allah.' So they will come to Abraham, the friend of Allah (peace be upon him), and say, 'You are the prophet of Allah and His friend from among the people of the earth. Intercede for us with your Lord. Do you not see our state?' He will say to them, 'My Lord is angry today with an anger like none before and none after. I told three lies'—and he mentioned them—'Myself, myself! Go to another. Go to Moses.' So they will come to Moses (peace be upon him) and say, 'O Moses, you are the messenger of Allah; He favored you with His message and His speech above the people. Intercede for us with your Lord. Do you not see our state?' He will say, 'My Lord is angry today with an anger like none before and none after. I killed a soul I was not commanded to kill. Myself, myself! Go to another. Go to Jesus (peace be upon him).' So they will come to Jesus and say, 'O Jesus, you are the messenger of Allah and His word which He cast to Mary, and a spirit from Him; you spoke to people in the cradle. Intercede for us with your Lord. Do you not see our state?' Jesus (peace be upon him) will say, 'My Lord is angry today with an anger like none before and none after'—and he did not mention a sin—'Myself, myself! Go to another. Go to Muhammad (peace be upon him).' So they will come and say, 'O Muhammad, you are the messenger of Allah and the seal of the prophets; Allah has forgiven you your past and future sins. Intercede for us with your Lord. Do you not see our state?' Then I will go and come beneath the Throne, falling prostrate before my Lord. Then Allah will open for me from His praises and beautiful glorification something He has not opened for anyone before me. Then it will be said, 'O Muhammad, raise your head. Ask, and you will be given; intercede, and your intercession will be granted.' So I will raise my head."

I say, "My community, my community, O Lord." He said, "O Muhammad, admit from your community those upon whom there is no reckoning through the right-hand gate of the gates of Paradise, and they are partners with the people in the other gates." Then He said, "By the One in whose hand is my soul, the distance between the two doorposts of the gates of Paradise is like the distance between Mecca and Himyar, or like the distance between Mecca and Busra." In another narration with this same context, the sins of Abraham are mentioned—his saying about the stars, "This is my Lord," his saying about their idols, "Rather, their chief did this," and his saying, "Indeed, I am ill." This is the intercession of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. And for individuals of his community from the scholars and the righteous, there is also intercession, to the extent that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "More people will enter Paradise by the intercession of a man from my community than the tribes of Rabi'ah and Mudar." And he, peace be upon him, said, "It will be said to a man, 'Arise, O so-and-so, and intercede.' So the man will arise and intercede for the tribe, for the household, and for one or two men, according to the measure of his deeds." And Anas said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "A man from the people of Paradise will look down on the Day of Resurrection upon the people of the Fire, and a man from the people of the Fire will call out to him and say, 'O so-and-so, do you recognize me?' He will say, 'No, by God, I do not recognize you. Who are you?' He will say, 'I am the one you passed by in the world and you asked me for a drink of water, and I gave you to drink.' He will say, 'Now I recognize you.' He will say, 'Then intercede for me with it before your Lord.' So he will ask God, may He be remembered and exalted, and say, 'I looked down upon the people of the Fire, and a man from its people called out to me and said, "Do you recognize me?" I said, "No, who are you?" He said, "I am the one who asked you for a drink in the world and you gave me to drink, so intercede for me before your Lord." So intercede for me concerning him.' So God will grant him intercession for him, and he will be commanded, and he will be brought out of the Fire." And from Anas, he said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "I am the first of the people to emerge when they are resurrected, and I am their speaker when they are presented, and I am their bearer of glad tidings when they despair. The banner of praise on that day will be in my hand, and I am the most honored of the children of Adam before my Lord, and I do not boast." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "I will stand before my Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, and I will be clothed in a garment from the garments of Paradise. Then I will stand at the right side of the Throne; no one from creation will stand in that station except me." And Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, said, "A group of the companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, were sitting waiting for him. He came out, and when he drew near to them, he heard them conversing and heard their talk. One of them said, 'It is amazing that God, may He be glorified and exalted, took from His creation a close friend—He took Abraham as a close friend.' Another said, 'What is more amazing than the speech of Moses—He spoke to him directly.' Another said, 'And Jesus—God is his word and His spirit.' Another said, 'Adam—God chose him.' Then he, peace be upon him, came out to them, greeted them, and said, 'I have heard your words and your amazement. Indeed, Abraham is the close friend of God, and that is so. And Moses is the one God spoke to, and that is so. And Jesus is the spirit of God and His word, and that is so. And Adam is the one God, may He be exalted, chose, and that is so. But know that I am the beloved of God, and I do not boast. And I am the bearer of the banner of praise on the Day of Resurrection, and I do not boast. And I am the first to intercede and the first whose intercession is accepted on the Day of Resurrection, and I do not boast. And I am the first to move the ring of Paradise, so God will open it for me, and I will enter it, and with me are the poor believers, and I do not boast. And I am the most honored of the first and the last, and I do not boast.'"

(The Description of the Basin)
Know that the Basin is a great honor with which God has specifically favored our Prophet, peace be upon him. The reports have encompassed its description, and we hope that God, may He be exalted, will grant us in this world knowledge of it and in the Hereafter the tasting of it. For among its attributes is that whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. Anas said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, dozed off, then raised his head smiling. They said to him, "O Messenger of God, why did you smile?" He said, "A verse was just revealed to me," and he recited, "In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful: 'Indeed, We have granted you al-Kawthar...'" until he finished it. Then he said, "Do you know what al-Kawthar is?" They said, "God and His Messenger know best." He said, "It is a river that my Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, has promised me in Paradise. Upon it is abundant good. Upon it is a basin to which my community will come on the Day of Resurrection. Its vessels are like the number of the stars in the sky." And Anas said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "While I was traveling in Paradise, I came upon a river whose banks were domes of hollow pearl. I said, 'What is this, O Gabriel?' He said, 'This is al-Kawthar which your Lord has given you.' Then the angel struck with his hand, and its mud was fragrant musk." And he used to say, peace be upon him, "The distance between the two sides of my basin is like the distance between Medina and Sana'a, or like the distance between Medina and Oman." And Ibn Umar reported that when the verse, "Indeed, We have granted you al-Kawthar," was revealed, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "It is a river in Paradise whose banks are of gold. Its drink is whiter than milk, sweeter than honey, and more fragrant than musk. It flows over pebbles of pearl and coral." And Thawban, the freed slave of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "Indeed, my basin extends from Aden to Oman al-Balqa'. Its water is whiter than milk, sweeter than honey, and its cups are like the number of the stars in the sky. Whoever drinks a single drink from it...

The first to arrive at it will be the poor emigrants, never to thirst thereafter. Umar ibn al-Khattab asked, "Who are they, O Messenger of God?" He replied, "They are those with dishevelled hair, soiled garments, who do not marry women of luxury, and for whom the gates of comfort are not opened." Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz then said, "By God, I have married a woman of luxury, Fatimah bint Abd al-Malik, and the gates of comfort have been opened for me, unless God has mercy on me. Assuredly, I will not oil my head until it becomes dishevelled, nor wash the garment upon my body until it becomes soiled."

And from Abu Dharr, who said: I asked, "O Messenger of God, what are the vessels of the Basin?" He said, "By Him in Whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, its vessels are more numerous than the stars and planets in a dark, clear night. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. At its farthest point, two spouts from Paradise pour into it. Its width is like its length, the distance between Oman and Aylah. Its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey."

And from Samurah, who said the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Every prophet has a basin, and they vie with one another as to who will have the most arrivals. I indeed hope to be the one with the most arrivals." This is the hope of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. So let every servant hope to be among the arrivals, and beware of being a mere wisher, deluded while thinking he is hopeful. For the one who hopes for the harvest is he who sows the seed, clears the land, and waters it, then sits hoping for God's bounty in bringing forth growth and warding off lightning until harvest time. As for one who abandons tilling, planting, clearing the land, and watering it, yet hopes from God's bounty that grain and fruit will grow for him—this is a deluded wisher and is not among the hopeful in any way. Such is the hope of most people, and it is the delusion of fools. We seek refuge in God from delusion and heedlessness. For delusion concerning God is greater than delusion concerning the world. God Almighty has said: "So let not the worldly life delude you, nor let the Deceiver delude you concerning God."

(The Discourse on the Description of Hell, Its Terrors and Punishments)

O you who are heedless of yourself, deluded by the preoccupations of this worldly life which is nearing its end and disappearance! Cease pondering what you are departing from, and turn your thought to your destination. For you have been informed that the Fire is the destination for all, as it is said: "There is none of you but will enter it. This is, for your Lord, a decree determined. Then We will save those who feared God and leave the wrongdoers within it, on their knees." So you are certain of the arrival, but in doubt about the salvation. Let the terror of that destination take hold of your heart, that you may perhaps prepare for salvation from it.

Contemplate the state of the creatures when they have endured the calamities of the Resurrection. While they are in its distress and terrors, standing, awaiting the reality of its tidings and the intercession of its intercessors, darknesses with many branches envelop the guilty, and a fire with flames overshadows them. They hear it roaring and rumbling, expressing intense wrath and anger. At that, the guilty become certain of destruction, and the nations fall upon their knees, until the innocent fear a terrible fate.

A caller from the guardians of Hell emerges, saying: "Where is so-and-so, son of so-and-so, who deceived himself in the world with prolonged hopes, wasting his life in evil deeds?" They hasten to him with iron maces, confront him with grave threats, and drive him to severe torment. They plunge him into the depths of Hell and say to him: "Taste! Indeed, you are the mighty, the noble!" They are settled in an abode narrow in expanse, dark in its paths, obscure in its perils, where the captive remains forever and the blaze is kindled. Their drink therein is scalding water, and their resting place is Hell. The guardians subdue them, and the abyss gathers them. Their hopes therein are for ruin, and they have no escape therefrom. Their feet are shackled to their foreheads, and their faces are blackened from the darkness of sins. They call out from its confines and cry in its corners and edges: "O Malik, the promise has come true for us! O Malik, the iron has burdened us! O Malik, our skins have been cooked! O Malik, take us out from it, for we will not return!" But the guardians say: "Far be it! Now is not the time for hope, nor is there any exit for you from the abode of disgrace. Be driven into it, and do not speak. Even if you were brought out, you would return to what you were forbidden." At that, they despair and grieve for what they neglected in God's cause. Regret does not save them, nor does grief avail them. Rather, they are thrown upon their faces, bound. The fire is above them, the fire beneath them, the fire to their right, and the fire to their left. They are drowned in the Fire; their food is fire, their drink is fire, their clothing is fire, and their bedding is fire. They are amidst fragments of fire and garments of pitch, struck with maces and weighed down by chains. They clamor in its narrow straits, are shattered in its depths, and are tossed amidst its billows. The Fire boils them as a cauldron boils. They cry out in woe and lamentation. Whenever they call for destruction, scalding water is poured over their heads, melting what is in their bellies and their skins. And for them are maces of...

Iron shall shatter their foreheads, causing pus to gush from their mouths, and their livers shall rupture from thirst. Their eyeballs shall stream down their cheeks, flesh shall fall from their jaws, and hair shall be torn from their limbs—indeed, their very skins. Whenever their skins are scorched, they will be replaced with new ones, until their bones are stripped bare of flesh, leaving souls tethered to veins and nerve fibers, writhing in the blaze of those fires. Yet, they will wish for death but not die. How would you fare if you beheld them with faces blackened darker than pitch, their sight blinded, tongues silenced, backs broken, bones shattered, ears severed, skins torn, hands shackled to their necks, their foreheads bound to their feet as they walk upon the fire with their faces, treading upon iron thorns with their eyes, while the flames course through their innards and the serpents and scorpions of the abyss cling to their limbs? This is but a glimpse of their state.

Now consider in detail their terrors, and reflect also upon the valleys and ravines of Hell. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "In Hell there are seventy thousand valleys, in each valley seventy thousand ravines, in each ravine seventy thousand serpents and seventy thousand scorpions, and the disbeliever and hypocrite will not cease until all of these are inflicted upon them." And Ali (may God honor his countenance) reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "Seek refuge in God from the Pit of Sorrow or the Valley of Sorrow." It was asked, "O Messenger of God, what is the Valley or Pit of Sorrow?" He replied, "It is a valley in Hell from which Hell itself seeks refuge seventy times a day, prepared by God Almighty for hypocritical reciters." Such is the vastness of Hell and the branching of its valleys, corresponding to the number of worldly desires and its gates, matching the seven limbs through which a servant disobeys, one above another: the uppermost is Jahannam, then Saqar, then Laza, then Hutamah, then Sa’ir, then Jahim, then Hawiyah. Now contemplate the depth of Hawiyah, for its depth is limitless, just as worldly desires are boundless. For as no worldly craving ends except in a greater craving, so no abyss in Hell ends except in a deeper abyss. Abu Hurairah said: "We were with the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) when we heard a crash. The Messenger said, 'Do you know what this is?' We said, 'God and His Messenger know best.' He said, 'This is a stone cast into Hell seventy years ago, and only now has it reached its bottom.'"

Then observe the disparity of levels, for the Hereafter has greater degrees and greater distinction. Just as people’s immersion in the world varies—some drowned in excess, others wading to a limited extent—so too their suffering in the Fire varies. For God wrongs not even an atom’s weight; thus, the types of torment do not converge upon every inhabitant of the Fire indiscriminately. Rather, each has a prescribed measure according to their disobedience and sin, though the least punished among them, if offered the entire world, would ransom himself from the severity of his plight. The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "The least punished of the people of the Fire on the Day of Resurrection will wear sandals of fire that cause his brain to boil from their heat." Now consider those for whom it is lightened, and take warning from those for whom it is intensified. If you doubt the severity of Hell’s punishment, bring your finger near a fire and measure by it, then know that you have erred in comparison, for the fire of this world does not equate to the Fire of Hell. Yet, since the severest worldly torment is that of this fire, the torment of Hell is understood through it. Far be it! If the people of the Blaze found such a fire, they would willingly plunge into it to escape their state. This is alluded to in some reports: "The fire of this world was washed seventy times with the waters of mercy so that the people of this world could bear it." Indeed, the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) explicitly described the Fire of Hell, saying: "God commanded that the Fire be kindled for a thousand years until it reddened, then for another thousand years until it whitened, then for another thousand years until it blackened, and so it is black and dark." And he (peace be upon him) said: "The Fire complained to its Lord, saying, 'O Lord, part of me consumes another.' So He permitted it two breaths: a breath in winter and a breath in summer. Thus, the most intense heat you experience in summer is from it, and the most intense cold you experience in winter is from its frost." Anas ibn Malik said: "The most comfortable disbeliever in the world will be brought and told, 'Dip him once into the Fire.' Then he will be asked, 'Have you ever experienced any comfort?' He will say, 'No.' Then the most afflicted person in the world will be brought and told, 'Dip him once into Paradise.' Then he will be asked, 'Have you ever experienced any affliction?' He will say, 'No.'" Abu Hurairah said: "If there were a hundred thousand or more in the mosque, and one inhabitant of the Fire exhaled, they would all perish." Some scholars said regarding His words, 'The Fire will scorch their faces,' that it scorches them once and leaves no flesh upon bone except that it casts it at their heels." Then, after this, consider the stench...

The pus that flows from their bodies until they drown in it—this is the ghasaq (foul fluid). Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "If a bucket of the ghasaq of Hell were poured onto the world, it would corrupt the people of the earth." This is their drink when they cry out from thirst; the most intensely thirsty among them is given water of pus to gulp down, scarcely able to swallow it, and death comes to him from every direction yet it does not kill him. And if they cry for relief, they are given water like molten brass that scalds their faces—how wretched a drink and how evil a resting place! Then consider their food: it is the Zaqqum tree, as God Almighty says: "Then indeed you, O misguided deniers, will surely eat from the tree of Zaqqum and fill your bellies with it, then drink on top of it boiling water, drinking like thirsty camels." And He says: "Indeed, it is a tree that emerges from the depths of Hellfire; its fruit is as if it were the heads of devils. So indeed they will eat from it and fill their bellies with it. Then indeed they will have upon it a mixture of scalding water. Then indeed their return will be to the Blaze." And He says: "He will enter a blazing Fire and be given to drink from a boiling spring." And He says: "Indeed, with Us are shackles and a Blaze, and food that chokes, and a painful punishment." Ibn 'Abbas reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "If a drop of Zaqqum were dripped into the seas of the world, it would spoil the livelihoods of the people of the world—so how about one whose food is that?" And Anas reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "Aspire to what God has made desirable for you, and beware and fear what God has warned you of—His punishment and His retribution, and Hellfire. For if a drop of Paradise were with you in your worldly life, its fragrance would delight you; and if a drop of the Fire were with you in your worldly life, its foulness would afflict you." And Abu al-Darda' reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "Hunger is cast upon the people of the Fire until it equals the torment they are in, so they cry out for food and are given food of dhari' (a bitter, thorny plant) that neither nourishes nor satisfies hunger. And they cry out for food and are given food that chokes, and they remember how they used to clear their throats in the world with a drink, so they cry out for a drink. Then boiling water is raised to them with hooks of iron, and when it draws near their faces, it scorches their faces. And when the drink enters their bellies, it cuts up what is in their bellies. So they say, 'Call the keepers of Hell!' They call them, and they say, 'Call upon your Lord to lighten for us a day of the torment.' They say, 'Did not your messengers come to you with clear proofs?' They say, 'Yes.' They say, 'Then call, but the call of the disbelievers is only in vain.' So they say, 'Call Malik.' They call him, and they say, 'O Malik, let our Lord decree an end for us!' He answers them, 'Indeed, you will remain.'" Al-A'mash reported: I was informed that between their call and Malik's answer to them is a thousand years. Then they say, 'Call upon your Lord, for none is better than your Lord.' They say, 'Our Lord, our wretchedness has overcome us, and we were a misguided people. Our Lord, bring us out of it; if we return [to evil], then indeed we are wrongdoers.' He answers them, 'Remain despised therein and do not speak to Me.' At that, they despair of all good, and at that they begin to groan and lament and woe. And Abu Umamah reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said concerning God's words, 'And he is given to drink of purulent water; he gulps it but can hardly swallow it': "It is brought near to him and he loathes it. When it is brought close to him, it scorches his face and the skin of his head falls off. And when he drinks it, it cuts his intestines until it exits from his anus. God Almighty says, 'And they are given scalding water to drink so that it cuts their intestines.' And He says, 'And if they cry for relief, they are given water like molten brass that scalds the faces.'" Such is their food and drink in their hunger and thirst. Now reflect upon the serpents of Hell and its scorpions, and upon the intensity of its poisonous winds, the enormity of its forms, and the horror of its appearance—set upon its inhabitants and incited against them, so that they do not cease from biting and stinging for a single moment. Abu Hurayrah reported that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever is given wealth by God and does not pay its zakah, it will be made for him on the Day of Resurrection into a venomous serpent with two fangs that will encircle him on the Day of Resurrection, then seize him by his jaws—meaning his cheeks—and say, 'I am your wealth, I am your treasure.' Then he recited God's words: 'And let not those who are stingy with what God has given them of His bounty think...' to the end of the verse." And the Messenger (peace be upon him) said: "Indeed, in the Fire are serpents like the necks of Bactrian camels; their sting is felt for forty autumns. And in it are scorpions like mules with loads; their sting is felt for forty autumns. These serpents and scorpions are only set upon those who were given to stinginess, bad character, and harming people in the world. Whoever is protected from that is protected from these serpents, so they are not made to appear to him." Then reflect after all this upon the magnification of the bodies of the people of the Fire, for God Almighty increases their bodies in length and width so that their torment is multiplied thereby, and they feel the scorching of the Fire and the stings of the scorpions and serpents from all their parts at once.

One after another, Abu Hurairah reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "A molar of the disbeliever in the Fire is like Mount Uhud, and the thickness of his skin is a journey of three." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "His lower lip will sag onto his chest, and the upper one will be raised, covering his face." And upon him be peace said: "Indeed, the disbeliever will drag his tongue in Sijjeen on the Day of Resurrection, and people will tread upon it." Despite the enormity of their bodies, the Fire will burn them repeatedly, renewing their skins and flesh. Al-Hasan said regarding God's statement, "Whenever their skins are roasted, We will replace them with other skins," that the Fire consumes them seventy thousand times each day; whenever it consumes them, they are told, 'Return,' and they return as they were. Then reflect now upon the weeping of the people of the Fire, their gasping, and their cries of 'Woe!' and 'Ruin!'—for that is unleashed upon them upon their initial casting into the Fire. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "On that Day, Hell will be brought forth with seventy thousand reins, and with each rein are seventy thousand angels." And Anas reported that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Weeping will be sent upon the people of the Fire, and they will weep until their tears are exhausted, then they will weep blood until trenches appear on their faces—if ships were sent into them, they would sail. And as long as they are permitted to weep, gasp, exhale, and cry 'Woe!' and 'Ruin!', they find some relief therein, but they are also prevented from that." Muhammad ibn Ka'b said: "The people of the Fire have five supplications; God Almighty answers them in four, but when it comes to the fifth, they will never speak again. They will say, 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice, and we confess our sins. Is there any way out?' God Almighty will answer them, 'That is because when God alone was invoked, you disbelieved; but if others are associated with Him, you believe. So the judgment belongs to God, the Most High, the Great.' Then they will say, 'Our Lord, delay us for a brief term that we may respond to Your call and follow the messengers.' God Almighty will answer, 'Did you not swear before that there would be no end for you?' They will say, 'Our Lord, take us out; we will do righteous deeds, other than what we used to do.' God Almighty will answer, 'Did We not give you long enough lives that whoever would remember could do so? And the warner came to you. So taste, for the wrongdoers have no helper.' Then they will say, 'Our Lord, our misfortune has overwhelmed us, and we were a people astray. Our Lord, remove us from it; if we return, then indeed we are wrongdoers.' God Almighty will answer them, 'Remain despised therein and do not speak to Me.' They will never speak after that, and that is the utmost severity of punishment." Malik ibn Anas, may God be pleased with him, said: "Zayd ibn Aslam said regarding God's statement, 'It is all the same for us whether we despair or are patient; there is for us no escape,' that they were patient for a hundred years, then they despaired for a hundred years, then they were patient for a hundred years, then they said, 'It is all the same for us whether we despair or are patient.'" And he, peace be upon him, said: "Death will be brought on the Day of Resurrection like a white ram and slaughtered between Paradise and the Fire, and it will be said, 'O people of Paradise, eternity without death! O people of the Fire, eternity without death!'" And from Al-Hasan, he said: "A man will emerge from the Fire after a thousand years. Would that I were that man!" And Al-Hasan, may God be pleased with him, was seen sitting in a corner weeping. He was asked, "Why are you weeping?" He said, "I fear that He will cast me into the Fire and not care." These are the categories of Hell's punishment in summary, and the detailing of its generality, its parts, its trials, and its regret has no end. The greatest matter for them, alongside what they encounter of severe punishment, is the regret of missing the bliss of Paradise, missing the meeting with God Almighty, and missing His pleasure—knowing that they sold all that for a paltry price, a few dirhams, for they sold it only for base desires in the world, for short days that were not pure but rather troubled and marred. They will say within themselves, "Alas for us! How we destroyed ourselves by disobeying our Lord! Why did we not compel ourselves to be patient for a few days? Had we been patient, those days would have passed, and we would now be in the company of the Lord of the worlds, enjoying pleasure and approval." Such is their regret, for they have missed it and are afflicted with what they are afflicted, and nothing of the world's pleasures and delights remains with them. Moreover, had they not witnessed the bliss of Paradise, their regret would not be so great, but it is displayed to them. Indeed, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "On the Day of Resurrection, some people will be brought from the Fire to Paradise until, when they draw near to it, inhale its fragrance, and look upon its palaces and what God has prepared for its people therein, they will be called, 'Turn them away; they have no share in it.' They will return with a regret that no one before or after has experienced. They will say, 'Our Lord, if You had entered us into the Fire before showing us what You showed us of Your reward and what You prepared therein for Your allies, it would have been easier for us.' God Almighty will say, 'That is what I intended for you. When you were alone, you would confront Me with grave sins, and when you met people, you met them humbly, showing people the opposite of what you concealed.'"

You give Me from your hearts when you have given to people, yet you do not revere Me. You honor people, yet you do not honor Me. You leave matters for people, yet you do not leave them for Me. So today I shall make you taste the painful punishment along with depriving you of the everlasting reward." (215) Ahmad ibn Harb said, "One of us prefers shade over the sun, yet he does not prefer Paradise over the Fire." Jesus, peace be upon him, said, "How many a healthy body, fair face, and eloquent tongue will tomorrow be screaming between the layers of the Fire." David said, "My God, I have no patience for the heat of Your sun, so how can I have patience for the heat of Your Fire? I have no patience for the sound of Your mercy, so how for the sound of Your punishment?" So look, O wretched one, at these terrors and know that God Almighty created the Fire with its terrors and created people for it who will neither increase nor decrease, and that this is a matter already decreed and concluded. God Almighty said: "And warn them of the Day of Regret, when the matter will be decided while they are in a state of heedlessness, and they do not believe." By my life, the allusion is to the Day of Resurrection, nay, in pre-eternity, but what the decree has preceded with becomes manifest on the Day of Resurrection. So the wonder is at you, how you laugh and play and busy yourself with the trifles of the world, while you do not know what the decree has preceded with concerning your fate. If you say, "Would that I knew what my destination is, and to what my end and return is, and what the decree has preceded with concerning me," then you have a sign to find solace in and to affirm your hope because of it. It is that you look at your states and your deeds, for everyone is facilitated towards what he was created for. If the path of good has been made easy for you, then give glad tidings, for you are kept far from the Fire. But if you do not intend any good except that obstacles surround you and repel it, and you do not intend any evil except that its causes are made easy for you, then know that a decree has been passed upon you. For the indication of this upon the outcome is like the indication of rain upon vegetation and the indication of smoke upon fire. God Almighty has said: "Indeed, the righteous will be in bliss, and indeed, the wicked will be in a Blazing Fire." So measure yourself against these two verses, and you will have known your abode in the two abodes. And God knows best.

(The Discourse on the Description of Paradise and the Varieties of Its Bliss)
Know that that abode, whose sorrows and griefs you have come to know, is faced by another abode. So contemplate its bliss and its joy, for whoever is distant from one of them will inevitably reside in the other. So extract fear from your heart through prolonged reflection on the terrors of Hellfire, and extract hope through prolonged reflection on the everlasting bliss promised to the people of the Gardens. Drive your soul with the whip of fear and guide it with the reins of hope to the Straight Path, for by that you attain the great dominion and are saved from the painful punishment. So reflect upon the people of Paradise, upon their faces the radiance of bliss, being given to drink of a pure, sealed wine, seated upon thrones of red ruby, in tents of moist white pearl, upon spreads of green brocade, reclining upon couches set along the banks of rivers flowing with wine and honey, attended by immortal youths and boys, adorned with wide-eyed maidens of beautiful virtues, as if they were ruby and coral, whom no man or jinn has touched before them, walking in the levels of the Gardens. When one of them sways in her walk, seventy thousand of the boys carry the hems of her garments, upon her are the finest of white silks at which eyes are dazzled, crowned with tiaras studded with pearl and coral, coquettish, alluring, fragrant, secure from aging and misery, secluded in the tents within palaces of ruby built amidst the meadows of the Gardens, with restrained glances, large-eyed. Then they are served, and upon them are served, with cups and ewers and a pure, white drink from a flowing spring, a delight to the drinkers. And there circulate upon them servants and boys like hidden pearls, as a reward for what they used to do, in a secure station, in Gardens and springs, in Gardens and a river, in a seat of honor near a Sovereign Perfect in Ability. They look therein upon the face of the Noble King, and the radiance of bliss has shone upon their faces. No fatigue shall touch them, nor any abasement; rather, they are honored servants, and with various gifts from their Lord they are attended. They are immortal therein in what their souls desire, they fear not therein, nor do they grieve, and they are secure from the doubt of death. They are therein in bliss, and they eat of its foods and drink from its rivers milk, wine, and honey, in rivers whose beds are of silver and whose gravel is coral, and upon a ground whose dust is fragrant musk and whose vegetation is saffron. And they are rained upon from clouds therein from the water of sweet basil upon dunes of camphor. And they are brought cups—and what cups!—cups of silver studded with pearls, ruby, and coral; a cup containing the sealed pure wine mixed with the sweet *Salsabeel*; a cup whose light shines from the clarity of its jewel, the drink appearing from behind it with its delicacy and redness. No human made it, falling short in perfecting its craftsmanship and beautifying its workmanship, in the hand of a servant whose face's radiance resembles the sun in its brightness. But from where would the sun have sweetness like the sweetness of his form, the beauty of his temples, and his loveliness?

His eyes, so how wondrous it is for one who believes in an abode of such description and is certain that its inhabitants do not die, nor do calamities befall those who dwell in its courtyards, nor do events cast the eye of change upon its people—how can he find comfort in an abode whose ruin God has decreed, and delight in a life beneath it? By God, if there were in it nothing but the soundness of bodies, with security from death, hunger, thirst, and all kinds of afflictions, it would be worthy of abandoning this world for its sake, and of not preferring over it that which is fleeting and tainted with hardship. How much more so when its inhabitants are secure kings, enjoying varieties of bliss, having therein all they desire, and who each day attend the court of the Throne, gazing upon the Noble Countenance of God, and attaining from that vision from God what makes them not look at any other bliss of Paradise, nor turn aside, while they perpetually move among these varieties of blessings, secure from their disappearance. Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "A caller will call out: 'O people of Paradise, you are granted health, so you shall never fall ill; you are granted life, so you shall never die; you are granted youth, so you shall never grow old; you are granted bliss, so you shall never grieve.' That is the meaning of His word, Exalted is He: 'And they will be called, "This is Paradise, which you have been made to inherit for what you used to do."'" And whenever you wish to know the description of Paradise, read the Qur'an, for there is no explanation beyond the explanation of God, the Exalted. Read from His saying, the Exalted: "For those who feared the standing before their Lord are two gardens" to the end of Surah Ar-Rahman, and read Surah Al-Waqi'ah and other surahs. And if you wish to know the detailed descriptions from the reports, then contemplate now my detailing of it after you have grasped its summary. And first, contemplate the number of the gardens. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said regarding His saying, the Exalted: "And for those who feared the standing before their Lord are two gardens": "Two gardens of silver, their vessels and all within them, and two gardens of gold, their vessels and all within them, and nothing lies between the people and their looking at their Lord except the veil of majesty upon His Countenance in the Garden of Eden." Then look to the gates of Paradise, for they are numerous according to the roots of acts of obedience, just as the gates of Hell are according to the roots of sins. Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever spends a pair from his wealth in the way of God will be called from all the gates of Paradise. Paradise has eight gates: whoever was among the people of prayer will be called from the gate of prayer; whoever was among the people of fasting will be called from the gate of fasting; whoever was among the people of charity will be called from the gate of charity; whoever was among the people of jihad will be called from the gate of jihad." Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, said: "By God, no one is in need of being called from all of them. Is anyone called from all of them?" He said: "Yes, and I hope you are among them." And from 'Asim bin Damrah, from 'Ali, may God honor his face, that he mentioned the Fire, magnifying its affair with a mention I do not recall, then he said: "And those who feared their Lord will be led to Paradise in groups," until when they reached a gate from its gates, they found near it a tree from beneath whose trunk two springs flowed. They turned to one of them as they were commanded and drank from it, and it removed whatever harm or ailment was in their bellies. Then they turned to the other and purified themselves with it, and the freshness of bliss flowed over them, so their hair never changed thereafter, nor did their heads become disheveled, as if they were anointed with oil. Then they reached Paradise, and its keepers said to them: 'Peace be upon you, you have done well, so enter it, abiding eternally.' Then the youths meet them, circulating among them as the youths of this world circulate around a beloved who returns to them from an absence, saying to him: 'Rejoice, God has prepared such and such honor for you.' Then a youth from those youths speaks to one of his wives from the wide-eyed maidens, saying: 'So-and-so has come,' by the name he was called in the world. She says: 'Have you seen him?' He says: 'I have seen him, and he is behind me.' Joy overwhelms her until she rises to the threshold of her door. When he reaches his dwelling, he looks at the foundation of its structure, and behold, it is a pearl boulder, above it a palace of red, green, and yellow, of every hue. Then he raises his head and looks at its ceiling, and behold, it is like lightning, and were it not that God, the Exalted, had decreed it, it would have taken his sight. Then he lowers his head, and behold, his wives, 'and cups set in place, cushions arrayed, and carpets spread.' Then he reclines and says: 'Praise be to God, who has guided us to this; we would not have been guided had God not guided us.' Then a caller calls out: 'You shall live and never die, you shall dwell and never depart, you shall be healthy and never fall ill.'" And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "I will come on the Day of Resurrection to the gate of Paradise and ask for it to be opened. The keeper will say: 'Who are you?' I will say: 'Muhammad.' He will say: 'For you I was commanded not to open for anyone before you.'" Then contemplate now the chambers of Paradise and the differing degrees of elevation within it, for the Hereafter has greater degrees and greater distinction. And just as among people in...

The outward acts of worship and the praiseworthy inward character traits differ manifestly, and likewise there is a manifest difference in what they are recompensed with. If you seek the highest degrees, then strive that none precede you in obedience to God, the Exalted, for God has commanded you to race and compete in it. He, the Exalted, said: "Race one another to forgiveness from your Lord" (Qur'an 57:21). And He, the Exalted, said: "For that let the competitors compete" (Qur'an 83:26). It is astonishing that if your peers or neighbors surpass you by an extra dirham or a taller building, that weighs heavily upon you and distresses your heart, and your life becomes bitter due to envy. Yet, in the best of your states, you would be settled in Paradise while not being safe therein from people who precede you with subtleties that the entire world cannot equal.
