Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, the people of Paradise see the people of the elevated chambers above them just as you see the setting star on the horizon from east to west, due to the superiority between them." They said, "O Messenger of God, those are the dwellings of the prophets which none but they can reach." He said, "Yes, by the One in Whose Hand is my soul, men who believed in God and were truthful to the messengers." He also said: "Indeed, the people of the highest degrees are seen by those below them just as you see the rising star on a horizon of the horizons of the sky. And Abu Bakr and 'Umar are among them and how excellent they are." Jabir reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said to us: "Shall I not inform you of the chambers of Paradise?" I said, "Yes, O Messenger of God, may my father and mother be sacrificed for you." He said, "In Paradise there are chambers made of every kind of jewel, their exterior seen from their interior and their interior from their exterior. In them is bliss, delights, and joy that no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to the heart of any human being." He said, "O Messenger of God, for whom are these chambers?" He said, "For the one who spreads peace, feeds food, persists in fasting, and prays at night while people are asleep." We said, "O Messenger of God, who can bear that?" He said, "My community can bear that, and I will inform you about it: Whoever meets his brother and greets him with peace or returns the greeting has spread peace. Whoever feeds his family and dependents food until they are full has fed food. Whoever fasts the month of Ramadan and three days from every month has persisted in fasting. Whoever prays the 'Isha' prayer and prays the dawn prayer in congregation has prayed at night while people are asleep," meaning the Jews, Christians, and Magians. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was asked about His saying: "And goodly dwellings in Gardens of Eden" (Qur'an 9:72). He said: "Palaces of pearl; in every palace are seventy houses of red ruby; in every house are seventy rooms of green emerald; in every room is a couch; on every couch are seventy beds of every color; on every bed is a wife from the wide-eyed maidens; in every house are seventy tables; on every table are seventy kinds of food; in every house are seventy attendants; and the believer is given every morning—meaning from the strength—what enables him to encompass all of that."

(Description of the Wall of Paradise, Its Lands, Trees, and Rivers)

Ponder the image of Paradise and reflect on the bliss of its inhabitants and the regret of those deprived of it due to being content with this world as a substitute for it. Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "The wall of Paradise is a brick of silver and a brick of gold; its soil is saffron and its clay is musk." He, peace be upon him, was asked about the soil of Paradise and said: "White musk, pure." Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever is pleased that God, the Mighty and Majestic, gives him wine to drink in the Hereafter, let him leave it in this world. And whoever is pleased that God clothes him in silk in the Hereafter, let him leave it in this world." He said: "The rivers of Paradise gush forth from beneath hills or beneath mountains of musk." "If the ornament of the lowest of the people of Paradise were to equal the ornament of all the people of this world, what God, the Mighty and Majestic, adorns him with in the Hereafter would be better than all the ornament of this world." Abu Huraira reported: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "In Paradise is a tree in whose shade a rider travels for a hundred years without traversing it. Recite if you wish: 'And an extended shade' (Qur'an 56:30)." Abu Umama reported: "The companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, used to say, 'God, the Mighty and Majestic, benefits us through the Bedouins and their questions.' A Bedouin came and said, 'O Messenger of God, God has mentioned in the Qur'an a harmful tree, and I did not know there was a tree in Paradise that harms its owner.' The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, 'What is it?' He said, 'The lote-tree, for it has thorns.' He said, 'God, the Exalted, has said: "Among lote-trees without thorns" (Qur'an 56:28). God removes its thorns and places in place of every thorn a fruit. Then the fruit splits open from it into seventy-two colors of food, none of which resembles another.'" Jarir ibn 'Abdullah reported: We alighted at al-Safah and there was a man sleeping beneath a tree; the sun had almost reached him. I said to the servant, "Go with this leather mat and shade him." So he went.

He shaded him, and when he awoke, it was Salman. I came to him and greeted him with peace. He said, "O Jarir, humble yourself before God, for whoever humbles himself before God in this world, God will elevate him on the Day of Resurrection. Do you know what the darknesses are on the Day of Resurrection?" I said, "I do not know." He said, "The injustices people commit against one another." Then he took a twig so small I could barely see it and said, "O Jarir, if you sought the like of this in Paradise, you would not find it." I said, "O Abu 'Abdullah, then where are the date palms and trees?" He said, "Their trunks are of pearl and gold, and their uppermost parts are fruit."

(Description of the Garments, Furnishings, Couches, Thrones, and Tents of the People of Paradise)
God Almighty said: "They will be adorned therein with bracelets of gold and pearl, and their garments therein will be silk." The verses concerning this are many, and its details are in the narrations. It has been narrated from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever enters Paradise will enjoy bliss and never grieve; his garments will not wear out, nor will his youth fade. In Paradise is that which no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has never occurred to the heart of man." A man said, "O Messenger of God, tell us about the garments of the people of Paradise: are they created or woven?" The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, remained silent, and some of the people laughed. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "Why do you laugh at an ignorant one asking a knowledgeable one?" Then the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, "Rather, they are split open from the fruit of Paradise, twice." And Abu Hurayrah said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, the first group to enter Paradise will be in the likeness of the moon on the night of the full moon. They will not spit therein, nor blow their noses, nor defecate. Their vessels and combs will be of gold and silver, their sweat will be musk, and each of them will have two wives, the marrow of whose shins will be seen from behind the flesh due to their beauty. There will be no discord among them nor hatred; their hearts will be as one heart, glorifying God morning and evening." (In a narration: "Each wife will have seventy garments.") And regarding His saying, Almighty is He: "They will be adorned therein with bracelets of gold," he, peace be upon him, said: "They will have crowns upon them; the smallest pearl among them will illuminate what is between the east and the west." And he, peace be upon him, said: "The tent is a hollow pearl, its height in the sky is sixty miles; in each corner of it are believers, family members whom the others do not see." Narrated by al-Bukhari in the Sahih. Ibn 'Abbas said: "The tent is a hollow pearl, a parasang by a parasang, with four thousand doors of gold." And Abu Sa'id al-Khudri said: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said regarding His saying, Almighty is He: 'And raised couches,' he said: 'The distance between two couches is like the distance between the heaven and the earth.'"

(Description of the Food of the People of Paradise)
The description of the food of the People of Paradise is mentioned in the Qur'an: from fruits, plump birds, manna, quail, honey, milk, and countless varieties. God Almighty said: "Whenever they are provided with a provision of fruit therefrom, they will say, 'This is what we were provided with before,' and they will be given it in resemblance." God Almighty mentioned the drink of the People of Paradise in many places. Thawban, the freed slave of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "I was standing with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, when a Jewish rabbi came to him and asked questions until he said, 'Who will be the first to cross, meaning over the Sirat?' He said, 'The poor emigrants.' The Jew said, 'Then what is their gift when they enter Paradise?' He said, 'The increase of the whale's liver.' He said, 'Then what is their meal after that?' He said, 'The bull of Paradise that used to graze at its edges will be slaughtered for them.' He said, 'Then what is their drink with it?' He said, 'From a spring therein called Salsabil.' He said, 'You have spoken the truth.'" And Zayd ibn Arqam said: "A man from the Jews came to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and said, 'O Abu al-Qasim, do you not claim that the people of Paradise will eat and drink therein?' And he said to his companions, 'If he affirms this to me, I will argue with him.' The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, 'Yes, by the One in whose hand is my soul, indeed one of them is given the strength of a hundred men in eating, drinking, and intercourse.' The Jew said, 'But whoever eats and drinks will have need (to relieve himself).' The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said, 'Their need is a sweat that flows from their skins like musk, and then the belly becomes flat.'" And Ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "You will see a bird in Paradise and desire it, and it will fall before you roasted." And Hudhayfah said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "In Paradise are birds like al-Bukhati (large camels)." Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, said, "They are indeed delicate, O Messenger of God." He said, "More delicate than them is the one who eats them, and you are among those who will eat them, O Abu Bakr." And 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said regarding His saying, Almighty is He: "There will be circulated among them plates," he said: "There will be circulated among them seventy plates of gold, each plate containing a color not found in another like it." And 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him, said regarding "And its mixture is of Tasnim," he said: "It is mixed for the companions of the right hand, and the near ones drink it pure." And Abu al-Darda', may God be pleased with him, said regarding His saying, Almighty is He: "Its seal is musk," he said: "It is a white drink like silver, with which they seal the last of their drink. If

That a man of worldly pursuits dipped his hand into it and withdrew it, leaving no living being but that it found the fragrance of its perfume.
                         (Description of the Wide-Eyed Maidens and Youths)
   Their description has been repeated in the Qur'an, and reports have come with additional clarification. Anas, may God be pleased with him, narrated that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "A morning or an evening spent in the path of God is better than the world and all it contains. And the space of a bow's length, or the place of one's foot, in Paradise is better than the world and all it contains. Were a woman from the women of the people of Paradise to look out towards the earth, she would illuminate it and fill what is between them with fragrance, and her head-covering upon her head is better than the world and all it contains," meaning the veil. And Abu Sa'id al-Khudri said: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said regarding His statement, the Exalted: 'As if they were rubies and coral' (Qur'an 55:58): 'You look at her face in her chamber, clearer than a mirror. Indeed, the lowest pearl upon her illuminates what is between the East and the West. And she will have upon her seventy garments, yet his sight penetrates them until he sees the marrow of her shin from behind that.'" And Anas said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "When I was taken on the Night Journey, I entered a place in Paradise called al-Baydakh, upon which were tents of pearl, green chrysolite, and red ruby. They said, 'Peace be upon you, O Messenger of God.' I said, 'O Gabriel, what is this call?' He said, 'These are the ones secluded in the tents; they sought permission from their Lord to greet you, and He permitted them.' Then they began to say, 'We are the contented ones, never displeased; we are the eternal ones, never departing.'" And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, recited the statement of the Exalted: "Maidens secluded in tents" (Qur'an 55:72). And Mujahid said regarding His statement, the Exalted: "And purified spouses" (Qur'an 2:25): "Purified from menstruation, feces, urine, spittle, phlegm, semen, and childbirth." And al-Awza'i said regarding "In occupation, enjoying" (Qur'an 36:55): "Their occupation is the deflowering of virgins." (And a man said: "O Messenger of God, do the people of Paradise have intercourse?" He said: "A man among them is given, in a single day, strength better than that of seventy of you.") And 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said: "The lowest in rank among the people of Paradise is he for whom a thousand servants are set to work, each servant upon a task not incumbent upon his master." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, a man from the people of Paradise will marry five hundred wide-eyed maidens, four thousand virgins, and eight thousand previously married women. He will embrace each one of them for the duration of his worldly life." And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, in Paradise there is a market wherein there is no buying or selling, except images of men and women. When a man desires an image, he enters into it. And in it is a gathering of the wide-eyed maidens, raising their voices with sounds the like of which creation has never heard, saying, 'We are the eternal ones, never perishing; we are the blissful ones, never grieved; we are the contented ones, never displeased. Blessed is he for whom we are, and we are for him.'" And Anas, may God be pleased with him, said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, the wide-eyed maidens in Paradise sing, 'We are the beautiful maidens, reserved for noble spouses.'" And Yahya ibn Kathir said regarding His statement, the Exalted: "In a garden, honored" (Qur'an 30:15): "Listening to singing in Paradise." And Abu Umamah al-Bahili said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "There is no servant who enters Paradise except that two of the wide-eyed maidens sit at his head and at his feet, singing to him with the most beautiful voice heard by mankind and jinn, and it is not with the flute of Satan, but with the praise of God and His glorification."
            (Explanation of various collective descriptions of the people of Paradise that have come in reports)
   Usamah ibn Zayd narrated that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said to his companions: "Is there not one who strives for Paradise? For Paradise has no equal, by the Lord of the Ka'bah! It is a gleaming light, a swaying sweet basil, a lofty palace, a flowing river, abundant ripe fruit, and a beautiful, lovely spouse in splendor, and bliss in an eternal abode, and freshness in a lofty, splendid, secure abode." They said: "We are the ones who strive for it, O Messenger of God." He said: "Say, 'If God wills.'" Then he mentioned jihad and urged towards it. (And a man came to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and said: "Are there horses in Paradise, for they amaze me?" He said: "If you desire that, you will be brought a horse of red ruby, and it will fly with you in Paradise wherever you wish." And a man said to him: "Camels amaze me, so are there camels in Paradise?" He said: "O servant of God, if you enter Paradise, you will have therein what your soul desires and what delights your eyes.") And from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, a man from the people of Paradise will have a child born to him as he desires, its pregnancy, weaning, and youth occurring in a single hour." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "When the people of Paradise are settled in Paradise, brothers will long for brothers. So the couch of this one will travel to the couch of that one, and they will meet and converse about what was between them in the abode of the world. One will say, 'O my brother, do you remember such-and-such a day in such-and-such a gathering when we called upon God, the Mighty and Majestic, and He forgave us?'" And the Messenger

God Almighty said: "Indeed, the inhabitants of Paradise are beardless, youthful, with kohl-rimmed eyes, appearing as thirty-three-year-olds, in the form of Adam, their height sixty cubits by a width of seven cubits." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "The lowest of the people of Paradise is he who has eighty thousand servants and seventy-two wives, and a pavilion of pearl, chrysolite, and ruby is erected for him, stretching from Jabiyah to Sana'a. Upon them are crowns, and the least of its pearls would illuminate what is between the east and the west." And he, peace be upon him, said: "I looked into Paradise and saw that a pomegranate from its pomegranates was like the hide of a fattened camel, and its birds were like Bactrian camels. And there was a maiden in it, so I said, 'O maiden, to whom do you belong?' She said, 'To Zayd ibn Harithah.' And in Paradise is that which no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to the heart of any human."

And Ka'b said: God the Exalted created Adam, peace be upon him, with His hand, wrote the Torah with His hand, and planted Paradise with His hand. Then He said to it, 'Speak,' and it said: 'Indeed, the believers have succeeded.' These are the attributes of Paradise we have mentioned in summary, then conveyed in detail. Al-Hasan al-Basri, may God have mercy on him, mentioned its entirety, saying: "Its pomegranates are like large water-skins, its rivers are of water unsullied, rivers of milk whose taste does not change, rivers of purified honey not clarified by men, and of wine delightful to the drinkers, which does not befuddle the mind nor cause headaches. And in it is that which no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to the heart of any human. They are kings in comfort, appearing as thirty-three-year-olds of one age, their height sixty cubits, in heaven, kohl-rimmed, beardless, youthful. They are secure from punishment and the abode is tranquil for them. Its rivers flow over gravel of ruby and chrysolite, and its roots, palm trees, and vines are of pearl, and its fruits—none knows their nature except God the Exalted. Its fragrance is found from a distance of five hundred years' journey. They have therein horses and swift camels, their saddles, bridles, and saddles of ruby, visiting therein. Their spouses are the wide-eyed maidens, as if they were hidden pearls. A woman takes seventy garments between her two fingers and wears them, and the marrow of her shin is seen from behind those seventy garments. God has purified the characters from evil and the bodies from death. They do not blow their noses therein, nor urinate, nor defecate; it is only a fragrant perspiration of musk. Their provision therein is morning and evening. But know, there is no night; morning succeeds evening and evening succeeds morning. The last to enter Paradise and the lowest in rank—his sight and his dominion are extended for a journey of a hundred years in palaces of gold and silver and tents of pearl, and his sight is expanded so he sees its farthest as he sees its nearest. They are served in the morning with seventy thousand trays of gold and in the evening with the like, on each tray a flavor not matched by the other, and he finds the taste of the last as he finds the taste of the first. In Paradise is a ruby containing seventy thousand dwellings, in each dwelling seventy thousand houses, without crack or hole."

And Mujahid said: "The lowest of the people of Paradise in rank is he whose dominion extends for a thousand years' journey, seeing its farthest as he sees its nearest, and the highest of them is he who looks upon his Lord in the morning and the evening." And Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib said: "There is no one from the people of Paradise except that in his hand are three bracelets: a bracelet of gold, a bracelet of pearl, and a bracelet of silver." And Abu Hurayrah, may God be pleased with him, said: "In Paradise is a maiden called al-'Ayna'; when she walks, seventy thousand handmaidens walk to her right and left, and she says, 'Where are those who enjoin good and forbid evil?'" And Yahya ibn Mu'adh said: "Abandoning the world is difficult, but missing Paradise is more difficult. Abandoning the world is the dowry for the Hereafter." He also said regarding seeking the world: "It is humiliation for the souls," and regarding seeking the Hereafter: "It is honor for the souls. So how strange is he who chooses humiliation in seeking what perishes and leaves honor in seeking what endures."

(The Attribute of Vision and Looking upon the Face of God, Blessed and Exalted)
God the Exalted said: "For those who do good is the best reward and extra." This extra is the vision of the face of God the Exalted, and it is the greatest delight in which the bliss of the people of Paradise is forgotten. We have mentioned its reality in the Book of Love. The Book and the Sunnah testify to it, contrary to what the people of innovation believe. Jarir ibn 'Abdullah al-Bajali said: "We were sitting with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, when he saw the moon on the night of the full moon. He said, 'You will see your Lord as you see this moon; you will have no difficulty in seeing Him. So if you are able not to be overcome in prayer before sunrise and before sunset, then do so.' Then he recited: 'And exalt [God] with praise of your Lord before the rising of the sun and before its setting.'" This is recorded in the two Sahih collections. Muslim recorded in his Sahih from Suhayb that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, recited God's saying: "For those who do good is the best reward and extra," and said: "When the people of Paradise enter Paradise and the people of the Fire enter the Fire, a caller will call out..."

O dwellers of Paradise, you have a promise with God that He wishes to fulfill for you. They said, "What is this promise? Has He not already made our scales heavy, whitened our faces, admitted us into Paradise, and delivered us from the Fire?" He said: Then the veil is lifted, and they gaze upon the Countenance of God, Mighty and Majestic is He, and they are given nothing more beloved to them than gazing upon Him. This tradition of the Vision has been narrated by a group of the Companions, and this is the ultimate beauty and the final bounty. All the delights we have detailed pale in comparison to this blessing; they are forgotten. Indeed, the joy of the people of Paradise upon the bliss of the Meeting has no end; rather, no pleasure of Paradise bears any proportion to the pleasure of the Meeting. We have been brief here due to our detailed exposition in the Book of Love, Longing, and Contentment. Thus, the servant's aspiration regarding Paradise should be for nothing other than meeting the Master. As for the other delights of Paradise, even the grazing beast released in the pasture shares in them.

                           [Chapter on the Vastness of God's Mercy]
        We conclude the book with a chapter on the vastness of God's mercy, as an optimistic omen.
   Indeed, the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) loved good omens. We have no deeds by which we may hope for forgiveness, so we follow the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) in optimism and hope that our end is sealed with goodness in this world and the next, just as we have concluded the book by mentioning God's mercy. For God Almighty has said: "Indeed, God does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills." And He Almighty has said: "Say, 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of God. Indeed, God forgives all sins. Indeed, it is He who is the Forgiving, the Merciful.'" And He Almighty has said: "And whoever does evil or wrongs himself then seeks forgiveness of God will find God Forgiving and Merciful." And we seek forgiveness from God Almighty for every slip of the foot or excess of the pen in this book of ours and in all our books. We seek His forgiveness for our words that our deeds do not match. We seek His forgiveness for what we claimed and displayed of knowledge and insight into God's religion while being deficient in it. We seek His forgiveness for every knowledge and action we intended for His Noble Countenance, then mixed it with other than Him. We seek His forgiveness for every promise we made to ourselves, then fell short in fulfilling. We seek His forgiveness for every blessing He bestowed upon us, which we then used in disobedience to Him. We seek His forgiveness for every explicit or implicit mention of the deficiency of the deficient or the shortcoming of the falling short, with which we were characterized. We seek His forgiveness for every fleeting thought that prompted us to affectation, pretense, and showing off to people in a book we penned, a speech we composed, or knowledge we imparted or acquired. And after seeking forgiveness for all of that—for ourselves and for whoever peruses this book of ours, writes it, or hears it—we hope to be honored with forgiveness, mercy, and pardon for all sins, outward and inward. For generosity is abundant, mercy is vast, and bounty upon all kinds of creation is overflowing. We are but a creation from among the creations of God, Mighty and Majestic is He, and we have no means to Him except His grace and generosity. For the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "Indeed, God Almighty has one hundred mercies. He sent down one mercy among the jinn, mankind, birds, beasts, and insects; through it they show affection and mercy to one another. And He withheld ninety-nine mercies with which He will show mercy to His servants on the Day of Resurrection." And it is narrated that "When the Day of Resurrection comes, God Almighty will bring out a book from beneath the Throne, in which is written: 'My mercy has preceded My wrath, and I am the Most Merciful of the merciful.' Then He will bring out of the Fire a number like the people of Paradise." And the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "God, Mighty and Majestic is He, will appear to us on the Day of Resurrection smiling and will say: 'Rejoice, O community of Muslims, for there is not one of you except that I have placed a Jew or a Christian in his place in the Fire.'" And the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "God Almighty will grant Adam intercession on the Day of Resurrection for all his progeny, for one hundred thousand thousand and ten thousand thousand." And he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "Indeed, God, Mighty and Majestic is He, will say on the Day of Resurrection to the believers: 'Did you love to meet Me?' They will say: 'Yes, O our Lord.' He will say: 'Why?' They will say: 'We hoped for Your pardon and forgiveness.' He will say: 'I have made My forgiveness obligatory for you.'" And he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "God, Mighty and Majestic is He, will say on the Day of Resurrection: 'Bring out of the Fire whoever remembered Me one day or feared Me in a situation.'" And the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "When the people of the Fire are gathered in the Fire, and with them, whomever God wills from the people of the Qiblah, the disbelievers will say to the Muslims: 'Were you not Muslims?' They will say: 'Yes.' They will say: 'What did your Islam avail you, since you are with us in the Fire?' They will say: 'We had sins, and we were taken for them.' Then God, Mighty and Majestic is He, hears what they said and orders those from the people of the Qiblah who are in the Fire to be brought out, and they are brought out. When the disbelievers see that, they will say: 'If only we had been Muslims, we would have been brought out as they were brought out.' Then the Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) recited: 'Often those who disbelieve wish that they had been Muslims.'"

The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "God is more merciful to His believing servant than a compassionate mother is to her child." And Jabir ibn Abd Allah said: "On the Day of Resurrection, whoever's good deeds outweigh his evil deeds, he is the one who will enter Paradise without reckoning. And whoever's good deeds and evil deeds are equal, he is the one who will be given an easy reckoning, then will enter Paradise. Indeed, the intercession of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, is for the one who has doomed himself and burdened his back." It is narrated that God, Mighty and Majestic, said to Moses, peace be upon him: "O Moses, Qarun sought your aid and you did not aid him. By My Might and Majesty, had he sought My aid, I would have aided him and forgiven him." And Sa'd ibn Bilal said: "On the Day of Resurrection, two men will be commanded to be brought out of the Fire. Then God, Blessed and Exalted, will say: 'This is for what your hands have sent forth, and I am not unjust to the servants.' Then He will command them to be returned to the Fire. One of them will rush in his chains until he plunges into it, while the other will hesitate. Then He will command them to be brought back and will ask them about their action. The one who rushed to the Fire will say: 'I was warned of the consequence of disobedience, so I would not expose myself to Your wrath a second time.' And the one who hesitated will say: 'My good opinion of You made me feel that You would not return me to it after You had brought me out of it.' Then He will command them both to Paradise." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "A caller will call from beneath the Throne on the Day of Resurrection: 'O community of Muhammad! As for what was due to Me from you, I have forgiven it for you. What remains are the mutual claims among you, so forgive one another and enter Paradise by My mercy.'" It is narrated that a Bedouin heard Ibn Abbas reciting: '...and you were on the brink of a pit of the Fire, and He saved you from it...' The Bedouin said: "By God, He did not save you from it if He intends to cast you into it!" Ibn Abbas said: "Take it from one who is not a jurist." And al-Sanabihi said: "I entered upon Ubadah ibn al-Samit while he was in his death illness, and I wept. He said: 'Gently, why do you weep? By God, there is no beneficial tradition I heard from the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, except that I have related it to you, except for one tradition, and I will relate it to you today, for my soul is about to depart. I heard the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, say: "Whoever testifies that there is no god but God and that Muhammad is the Messenger of God, God has forbidden the Fire to him."'" And Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, God will single out a man from my community before all creation on the Day of Resurrection. Ninety-nine scrolls will be unfurled for him, each scroll as far as the eye can see. Then He will say: 'Do you deny anything of this? Have My recording scribes wronged you?' He will say: 'No, my Lord.' He will say: 'Do you have any excuse?' He will say: 'No, my Lord.' He will say: 'Rather, you have with Us a good deed, and there is no injustice upon you today.' Then a card will be brought out on which is written: 'I bear witness that there is no god but God, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of God.' He will say: 'My Lord, what is this card alongside these scrolls?' He will say: 'You will not be wronged.' He said: Then the scrolls will be placed in one scale and the card in the other scale. He said: The scrolls will be light and the card will be heavy, for nothing is weightier than the name of God." And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said in the latter part of a long tradition in which he describes the Resurrection and the Bridge: "Indeed, God will say to the angels: 'Whoever you find in his heart a dinar's weight of good, bring him out of the Fire.' They will bring out a great multitude. Then they will say: 'Our Lord, we have left none in it of those You commanded us.' Then He will say: 'Go back. Whoever you find in his heart half a dinar's weight of good, bring him out.' They will bring out a great multitude. Then they will say: 'Our Lord, we have left none in it of those You commanded us.' He will say: 'Go back. Whoever you find in his heart an atom's weight of good, bring him out.' They will bring out a great multitude. Then they will say: 'Our Lord, we have left none in it of those You commanded us.'" Abu Sa'id used to say: "If you do not believe me regarding this tradition, then read if you wish: 'Indeed, God does not wrong [anyone] by an atom's weight; and if it is a good deed, He multiplies it and gives from Himself a great reward.'" He said: Then God, Exalted is He, will say: "The angels have interceded, and the prophets have interceded, and the believers have interceded, and none remains but the Most Merciful of the merciful." Then He will take a handful and bring out from it people who never did any good at all; they had become cinders. He will cast them into a river at the entrances of Paradise called the River of Life. They will emerge from it as a seed emerges in the silt of a flood. Do you not see it—what is towards the stone and the tree, what faces the sun is yellow and green, and what is in the shade is white? They said: "O Messenger of God, it is as if you used to tend livestock in the desert." He said: They will emerge like pearls, with seals on their necks. The people of Paradise will recognize them, saying: "These are the freed ones of the Merciful, whom He admitted to Paradise without any deed they did or good they sent forth." Then He will say: "Enter Paradise. Whatever you see is for you." They will say: "Our Lord, You have given us what You have not given anyone in the worlds." God, Exalted is He, will say: "I have for you with Me what is better than this." They will say: "Our Lord, what thing is better than this?" He will say: "My pleasure with you, for I shall never be angry with you after it." Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim in their Sahih collections.

Al-Bukhari also narrates from Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, who said: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, came out to us one day and said: 'The nations were presented to me. A prophet would pass by with one man, a prophet with two men, and a prophet with no one. A prophet would pass by with a small group. Then I saw a great multitude and I hoped it would be my nation. It was said to me: "This is Moses and his people." Then it was said to me: "Look." I saw a great multitude filling the horizon. It was said to me: "Look this way and that." I saw a great multitude. It was said to me: "These are your nation, and with these are seventy thousand who will enter Paradise without reckoning."' The people dispersed without the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, clarifying for them. The Companions discussed this, saying: 'As for us, we were born in polytheism, but we have believed in God and His Messenger. Perhaps these are our children?' This reached the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and he said: 'They are those who do not practice cauterization, do not seek omens, do not believe in bad omens, and upon their Lord they rely.' Ukashah stood up and said: 'Pray to God to make me among them, O Messenger of God.' He said: 'You are among them.' Then another man stood and said the same as Ukashah. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Ukashah has preceded you in it.'"

And from 'Umar ibn Hazm al-Ansari, who said: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was absent from us for three days, only coming out for the obligatory prayer and then returning. On the fourth day, he came out to us and we said: 'O Messenger of God, you were detained from us until we thought something had happened.' He said: 'Nothing has happened except good. My Lord, Mighty and Majestic, promised me that He would admit seventy thousand from my nation into Paradise without reckoning, and I asked my Lord for an increase during these three days. I found my Lord to be Glorious, Self-Sufficient, and Generous, so He gave me, with each one of the seventy thousand, seventy thousand more.' I said: 'O Lord, will my nation reach this number?' He said: 'I will complete the number for you from the Bedouins.'"

And Abu Dharr said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "Gabriel appeared to me at the side of al-Harrah and said: 'Give glad tidings to your nation that whoever dies not associating anything with God will enter Paradise.' I said: 'O Gabriel, even if he steals and commits adultery?' He said: 'Yes, even if he steals and commits adultery.' I said: 'Even if he steals and commits adultery?' He said: 'Even if he steals, commits adultery, and drinks wine.'"

And Abu al-Darda' said: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, recited: 'But for him who fears the standing before his Lord are two Gardens' (Quran 55:46). I said: 'Even if he steals and commits adultery, O Messenger of God?' He recited: 'But for him who fears the standing before his Lord are two Gardens.' I said: 'Even if he steals and commits adultery?' He recited: 'But for him who fears the standing before his Lord are two Gardens.' I said: 'Even if he steals and commits adultery, O Messenger of God?' He said: 'Even if, to the dismay of Abu al-Darda's nose.'"

And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "On the Day of Resurrection, a man from the People of the Book will be given to every believer, and it will be said to him: 'This is your ransom from the Fire.'"

Muslim narrates in his Sahih from Abu Burdah that he related to 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz from his father, Abu Musa, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said: "No Muslim man dies but that God, Exalted is He, puts a Jew or a Christian in his place in the Fire." 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz made him swear by God, besides whom there is no deity, three times that his father had narrated it to him from the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and he swore to him.

And it is narrated: "A young boy stood in one of the military expeditions, being offered for sale on an extremely hot summer day. A woman in the people's tent saw him. She rushed forward, and her people followed behind her, until she took the boy, pressed him to her chest, then lay on her back on the ground and placed him on her stomach to shield him from the heat, saying: 'My son, my son!' The people wept and abandoned what they were doing. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, approached and stood before them. They informed him of the story. He was pleased with their mercy, then gave them glad tidings, saying: 'Are you amazed at this woman's mercy for her son?' They said: 'Yes.' He, peace be upon him, said: 'God, Blessed and Exalted, is more merciful to all of you than this woman is to her son.'"

Thus, the Muslims dispersed with the best joy and the greatest glad tidings. These hadiths, and what we have cited in the Book of Hope, give us glad tidings of the vastness of God's mercy, Exalted is He. So we hope from God, Exalted is He, that He will not deal with us as we deserve, but will bestow upon us from what is worthy of Him, by His grace, His abundant generosity, and His mercy.

[6] The hadith "Death is a gift for the believer" was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in his book "Al-Mawt" (Death), and by al-Tabarani and al-Hakim from the narration of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar as a *mursal* report with a *hasan* chain.

[7] The hadith "Death is an expiation for every Muslim" was transmitted by Abu Nu'aym in "Al-Hilyah", al-Bayhaqi in "Al-Shu'ab", and al-Khatib in "Al-Tarikh" from the narration of Anas. Ibn al-'Arabi said in "Siraj al-Muridin" that it is *hasan sahih*, but Ibn al-Jawzi deemed it weak. I have compiled its chains in a separate treatise.

[8] The hadith of 'Ata' al-Khurasani: The Prophet (peace be upon him) passed by a gathering where laughter was prevalent and said, "Mix your gathering with the remembrance of that which spoils pleasures..." This hadith was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" in this manner as a *mursal* report. We also narrated it in the dictations of al-Jalal from the narration of Anas, but it is not authentic.

[9] The hadith of Anas: "Increase your remembrance of death, for it purifies sins and induces asceticism in the worldly life." This was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" with a very weak chain.

[10] The hadith "Sufficient is death as a separator" was transmitted by al-Harith ibn Abi Usamah in his *Musnad* from the narration of Anas and 'Irak ibn Malik with a weak chain. Ibn Abi al-Dunya also narrated it in "Al-Birr wa al-Silah" from the narration of Abu 'Abd al-Rahman al-Hubli as a *mursal* report.

[11] The hadith "Sufficient is death as an admonisher" was transmitted by al-Tabarani and al-Bayhaqi in "Al-Shu'ab" from the narration of 'Ammar ibn Yasir with a weak chain. It is well-known as a saying of al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad, which al-Bayhaqi transmitted in "Al-Zuhd".

[12] The hadith: "The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) went out to the mosque and found some people conversing and laughing. He said, 'Remember death...'" This was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" from the narration of Ibn 'Umar with a weak chain.

[13] The hadith: "A man was mentioned in the presence of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) and they praised him well. He said, 'How was your companion's remembrance of death?...'" This was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" from the narration of Anas with a weak chain, and by Ibn al-Mubarak in "Al-Zuhd". He said: Malik ibn Mighwal informed us, and he mentioned it as a *balaghah* report with an addition.

[14] The hadith of Ibn 'Umar: "I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) as the tenth among ten men. A man from the Ansar said, 'Who are the most prudent of people?...'" This was transmitted by Ibn Majah in an abridged form and by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in its complete form with a sound (*jayyid*) chain.

[15] The hadith: He said to 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, "When you reach the morning, do not expect the evening..." This was transmitted by Ibn Hibban. Al-Bukhari narrated it as a saying of Ibn 'Umar at the end of the hadith, "Be in the world as if you are a stranger."

[16] The hadith of 'Ali: "Verily, the things I fear most for you are two traits: following desires and having long hopes..." in its full length, was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in his book "Shortening Hopes". He also narrated it from the narration of Jabir in a similar manner, and both are weak.

[17] The hadith of Umm al-Mundhir: "O people, do you not feel shame before God, the Exalted?" They said, "And what is that, O Messenger of God?" He said, "You amass wealth you do not eat..." This was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya, and through his chain in "Al-Shu'ab" with a weak chain, and it has been mentioned previously.

[18] The hadith of Abu Sa'id: "Usamah ibn Zid purchased from Zaid ibn Thabit a slave-girl for one hundred dinars to be paid in a month. I heard the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) say, 'Are you not astonished at Usamah?...'" This was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes", al-Tabarani in "Musnad al-Shamiyyin", Abu Nu'aym in "Al-Hilyah", and al-Bayhaqi in "Al-Shu'ab" with a weak chain.

[19] The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: "He would go out to pour water and would wipe [his hands] with dust. I would say, 'The water is close to you.' He would say, 'How do I know? Perhaps I will not reach it.'" This was transmitted by Ibn al-Mubarak in "Al-Zuhd", Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes", and al-Bazzar with a weak chain.

[20] The hadith: "He took three sticks and planted one in front of him..." This was transmitted by Ahmad and Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes", and the wording is his.

[21] The hadith: "The parable of the son of Adam, and beside him are ninety-nine appointed times of death..." This was transmitted by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of 'Abdullah ibn al-Shikhkhir, and he said it is *hasan*.

[22] The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: "The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) drew a square line for us, and drew a line in its middle..." This was narrated by al-Bukhari.

[23] The hadith of Anas: "The son of Adam grows old, yet two things remain with him: greed and hope." In another narration: "And they grow strong with him..."

Two are greed for wealth and greed for life, and Muslim narrated it with the wording "the second," while Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes" narrated it with the first wording through a sound chain.

[24] The hadith: The first of this community was saved by certainty and asceticism, and the last of this community will be ruined by stinginess and hope. Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it from the narration of Ibn Lahi'ah from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather.

[25] The hadith of al-Hasan: "All of you love to enter Paradise." They said, "Yes, O Messenger of God." He said, "Shorten your hopes..." The hadith was transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in this manner from the hadith of al-Hasan as mursal.

[26] The hadith: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, used to say in his supplication: "O God, I seek refuge in You from a hope that prevents the good of the Hereafter, and I seek refuge in You from a life that prevents the good of death, and I seek refuge in You from a hope that prevents the good of deeds." Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it from the narration of Hawshab from the Prophet, peace be upon him, and in its chain there is weakness and obscurity, and I do not know who Hawshab is.

[27] The hadith: "Love whom you love, for you will part from them." The hadith has preceded multiple times.

[28] The hadith: "An old man is youthful in love of the world, and even if his collarbones tremble from old age, except for those who are God-fearing, and few they are." I did not find it with this wording. In the two Sahihs, from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "The heart of an old man remains youthful with love for two things: long life and love of wealth."

[29] The hadith of his asking Mu'adh about the reality of his faith, and he said: "I did not take a step except that I thought I would not take another after it." Abu Nu'aym transmitted it in "Al-Hilyah" from the hadith of Anas, and it is weak.

[30] The hadith: "What does any of you expect from the world except wealth that leads to transgression or poverty that causes forgetfulness?" Al-Tirmidhi transmitted it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah with the wording: "Do they expect except affluence?" and he said it is hasan. Ibn al-Mubarak narrated it in "Al-Zuhd," and through his route Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes" with the wording of the author, and in it is an unnamed narrator.

[31] The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: "Take advantage of five before five: your youth before your old age..." Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it with a hasan chain, and Ibn al-Mubarak narrated it in "Al-Zuhd" from the narration of 'Amr ibn Maymun al-Azdi as mursal.

[32] The hadith: "Two blessings are taken for granted by many people: health and free time." Al-Bukhari transmitted it from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas, and it has preceded.

[33] The hadith: "Whoever fears sets out at night, and whoever sets out at night reaches the destination." Al-Tirmidhi transmitted it from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas, and it has preceded. And he said: "The hadith 'Whoever fears sets out at night, and whoever sets out at night reaches the destination' was transmitted by al-Tirmidhi from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and he said it is hasan."

[34] The hadith: "The quake came, followed by the aftershock..." Al-Tirmidhi transmitted it and graded it hasan from the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b.

[35] The hadith: "When he noticed heedlessness or negligence among his companions, he would call out to them in a loud voice: 'Death has come to you...'" Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it in "Shortening Hopes" from the hadith of Zayd al-Sulami as mursal.

[36] The hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "I am the warner, and death is the raider, and the Hour is the appointment." Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it in "Shortening Hopes," and Abu al-Qasim al-Baghawi with a chain containing leniency.

[37] The hadith of Ibn 'Umar: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, went out while the sun was on the tips of the palm branches, and he said: 'What remains of the world is only like what remains of this day compared to what has passed of it.'" Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it with a hasan chain, and al-Tirmidhi transmitted something similar from the hadith of Abu Sa'id and graded it hasan.

[38] The hadith: "The likeness of the world is like a garment torn from its beginning to its end..." Ibn Abi al-Dunya transmitted it from the hadith of Anas, and it is not authentic.

[39] The hadith of Jabir: "When he delivered a sermon and mentioned the Hour, his voice would rise and his cheeks would redden..." Muslim transmitted it, and Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes," and the wording is his.

[40] The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, recited: {'So whoever God wills to guide, He expands his breast to Islam'} and said: "When light enters the breast, it expands." It was said: "O Messenger of God, is there a sign for that which is recognized?" He said: "Yes, turning away from the abode of deception and turning to the abode of eternity."

Eternal Life and Preparation for Death Before Its Arrival" – narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes" and al-Hakim in "al-Mustadrak," as previously mentioned.

[41] The narration of Abu 'Ubaydah al-Baji: We visited al-Hasan during the illness from which he died, and he said: "Welcome to you, and greetings. May God grant you life in peace and settle us and you in the Abode of Permanence. This is a good public admonition if you are patient, truthful, and God-fearing. So, may God have mercy on you, let not your portion of this news be merely hearing it with this ear and letting it out from this ear. For whoever saw Muhammad, peace be upon him, saw him coming and going, not laying brick upon brick nor reed upon reed, but a banner was raised for him, so he hastened toward it: 'Hasten, hasten! Salvation, salvation! Why do you delay? You have come, by the Lord of the Ka'bah, as if you and the matter are together.' May God have mercy on a servant who made life a single life, so he ate a morsel, wore worn garments, clung to the earth, strove in worship, wept over sin, fled from punishment, and sought mercy until his term comes to him while he is upon that." – Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Shortening Hopes," Ibn Hibban in "al-Thiqat," and Abu Nu'aym in "al-Hilyah" from this chain.

[42] The narration that God accepts the repentance of a servant as long as the death rattle has not reached the throat – narrated by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah from the narration of Ibn 'Umar, and Ibn Majah graded it as good.

[43] The narration that he used to say: "O God, make easy for Muhammad the agonies of death" – previously mentioned.

[44] The narration that he used to say: "O God, take the soul from between the nerves, the marrow, and the fingertips" – the full narration. Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "The Book of Death" from the narration of Sa'idah ibn Ghaylan al-Ju'fi, and it is interrupted (mu'dal), the Companion being omitted from its chain, though it reaches a Follower.

[45] The narration of al-Hasan that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, mentioned death, its choking, and its pain, and said: "It is equivalent to three hundred strikes with a sword." – Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya therein thus, as a mursal narration, and its narrators are trustworthy.

[46] The narration that he was asked about death and its severity, and he said: "Indeed, the easiest death is like a thorn" – the full narration. Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya therein from the narration of Shahr ibn Hawshab, as a mursal narration.

[47] The narration that he visited a sick person and said: "Indeed, I do not know what he is experiencing; there is not a vein in him except that it aches for death due to its severity." – Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya therein from the narration of Salman with a weak chain, and he also narrated it in "Sickness and Expiation" from the narration of 'Ubayd ibn 'Umayr as a mursal narration with some variation, and its narrators are trustworthy.

[48] The narration: "Sudden death is a mercy for the believer and a cause of regret for the wicked." – Narrated by Ahmad from the narration of 'A'ishah with a sound chain, and he said: "and its taking is regret." And by Abu Dawud from the narration of Khalid al-Sulami: "Sudden death is a taking of regret."

[49] The narration of Makhul: "If a single hair from the hair of the deceased were to be placed upon the inhabitants of the heavens and the earth, they would die" – the full narration. Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Death" from the narration of Abu Maysarah, raised to the Prophet, and in it: "If the pain of a single hair..." and he added: "And indeed, on the Day of Resurrection there are ninety terrors, the least of which is a terror multiplied over death seventy thousand times." And Abu Maysarah is 'Amr ibn Shurahbil, and the narration is mursal with a good chain.

[50] The narration: "If a drop of death were placed upon all the mountains of the world, they would melt." I did not find a basis for it, and perhaps the author did not cite it as a hadith, for he said: "And it is narrated."

[51] The narration that there was a cup of water with him at the time of death, and he would put his hand in the water, then wipe his face with it and say: "O God, make easy for me the agonies of death." – Agreed upon from the narration of 'A'ishah.

[52] The narration that Fatimah said: "O, the grief for your grief, O my father!" – the full narration. Narrated by al-Bukhari from the narration of Anas with the wording: "O, the grief, O my father!" and in the narration of Ibn Khuzaymah: "O, my grief!"

[53] The narration: "Indeed, the servant struggles with the distress of death and the agonies of death, and they exchange greetings with one another" – the full narration. We narrated it in "The Forty" of Abu Haddabah Ibrahim ibn Haddabah from Anas, and Abu Haddabah is Malik.

[54] The narration of Abu Hurayrah that Dawud was a jealous man – the full narration. Narrated by Ahmad with a good chain similarly, and by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "The Book of Death" with the wording.

[55] The narration: "None of you will leave the world until he knows where his destination is and until he sees his place in Paradise or the Fire." – Narrated by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Death" from the narration of an unnamed man from 'Ali, as a mawquf narration.

No soul of a son of Adam departs from this world until it knows where its destination lies—to Paradise or to the Fire. In another narration: It is forbidden for a soul to depart from the world until it knows whether it is among the people of Paradise or the people of the Fire. In the two Sahih collections, from ‘Ubādah ibn al-Ṣāmit, there is evidence for this: When death approaches the believer, he is given glad tidings of God’s pleasure and honor; and when death approaches the disbeliever, he is given tidings of God’s punishment and chastisement. [Hadith]

[56] Hadith: Whoever loves to meet God, God loves to meet him; and whoever hates to meet God, God hates to meet him. The hadith is agreed upon, narrated from ‘Ubādah ibn al-Ṣāmit.

[57] Hadith: When God is pleased with His servant, He says: “O Angel of Death, go to so-and-so and bring me his soul, that I may show him mercy.” The hadith was reported by Ibn Abī al-Dunyā in the Book of Death, from Tamīm al-Dārī with a weak chain, containing many additions. It is not explicitly stated at the beginning of the hadith that it is raised [to the Prophet], though its end indicates it is raised. Al-Nasā’ī reports from Abū Hurayrah with a sound chain: When the deceased is present, the angels of mercy come to him with a white silk cloth and say: “Come forth pleased and pleasing, to God’s spirit and fragrance, and to a Lord who is pleased, not angry.” [Hadith]

[58] Hadith: Observe the deceased at three signs: when his forehead perspires, his eyes shed tears… The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhī al-Ḥakīm in Nawādir al-Uṣūl from Salmān, but it is not authentic.

[59] Hadith: Prompt your dying ones with “There is no god but God”—mentioned earlier.

[60] Hadith: Ḥudhayfah—for it demolishes what came before it—mentioned earlier.

[61] Hadith: Whoever dies while knowing that there is no god but God enters Paradise—mentioned earlier.

[62] Hadith: Abū Hurayrah—The Angel of Death came to a man who was dying, looked into his heart, and found nothing in it… The hadith was reported by Ibn Abī al-Dunyā in the Book of the Dying, al-Ṭabarānī, and al-Bayhaqī in al-Shu‘ab. Its chain is good, except that in al-Bayhaqī’s version the man is unnamed, while in al-Ṭabarānī’s version he is named Isḥāq ibn Yaḥyā ibn Ṭalḥah, who is weak.

[63] Hadith: Wāthilah ibn al-Asqa‘ visited a sick man and said: “Tell me, what is your expectation of God?” In it, God says: “I am as My servant expects of Me, so let him expect of Me what he will.” Reported by Ibn Ḥibbān as raised [to the Prophet], and previously mentioned; also by Aḥmad and al-Bayhaqī in al-Shu‘ab together.

[64] Hadith: He visited a youth who was dying and said: “How do you find yourself?” He replied: “I hope in God and fear my sins.” The hadith is previously mentioned.

[65] Hadith: Ibn Mas‘ūd—We entered upon the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) in the house of our mother ‘Ā’ishah when departure was near… The hadith was narrated by al-Bazzār, who said: “This speech has been reported from Murrah from ‘Abd Allāh from various channels, and their chains are close.” He said: “And ‘Abd al-Raḥmān al-Aṣbahānī did not hear this from Murrah; rather, it is from someone who informed him from Murrah.” He said: “I do not know anyone who reported it from ‘Abd Allāh except Murrah.” I say: It has been reported from other channels: Ibn Sa‘d reported it in al-Ṭabaqāt from the narration of Ibn ‘Awf from Ibn Mas‘ūd, and we reported it in the shaykh-list of Judge Abū Bakr al-Anṣārī from the narration of al-Ḥasan al-‘Arabī from Ibn Mas‘ūd, but both are interrupted and weak. Al-Ḥasan al-‘Arabī only reports it from Murrah, as reported by Ibn Abī al-Dunyā and al-Ṭabarānī in al-Awsaṭ.

[66] Hadith: He (peace be upon him) said to Gabriel at his death: “Who will take care of my community after me?” So God Almighty revealed to Gabriel: “Give My beloved the glad tidings that I will not abandon him regarding his community.” The hadith was reported by al-Ṭabarānī from Jābir and Ibn ‘Abbās in a long hadith in which he said: “Who will take care of my chosen community after me?” [Gabriel] said: “Rejoice, O beloved of God, for God Almighty says: ‘I have forbidden Paradise to all the prophets and communities until you and your community enter it.’” He said: “Now my soul is at peace.” Its chain is weak.

[67] Hadith: ‘Ā’ishah—We were commanded to wash him with seven waterskins from seven wells, so we did that, and he found relief. Then he went out and prayed with the people and sought forgiveness for the people of Uḥud. The hadith was reported by al-Dārimī in his Musnad, and in it is Ibrāhīm ibn al-Mukhtār, who is disputed, from Muḥammad ibn Isḥāq, and he was a mudallis, having reported it with ‘an‘anah.

[68] Hadith: ‘Ā’ishah—He was taken in my house, on my day, between my chest and my throat, and God joined my saliva with his at death. The hadith is agreed upon.

[69] A narration from Sa'id ibn 'Abdullah from his father who said: When the Ansar saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ growing increasingly weak, they gathered around the mosque. Al-'Abbas entered and informed him of their presence and their concern. The lengthy narration mentions his ﷺ coming out, leaning [on support], with his head bandaged, dragging his feet until he sat on the lowest step of the pulpit, and then mentions his sermon in full. This is a *mursal*, weak narration containing oddities, and I found no basis for it. His father, 'Abdullah ibn Darar ibn al-Azwar, is a *Tabi'i* who narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. Abu Hatim said about him and his son Sa'id: "They are not strong."

[70] A narration from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet ﷺ said to Abu Bakr, "Ask, O Abu Bakr." He said, "O Messenger of Allah, the appointed time has drawn near." He ﷺ said, "The appointed time has indeed drawn near." The narration concerns their asking him about who should wash him, in what he should be shrouded, and the manner of praying over him. Ibn Sa'd narrated it in *al-Tabaqat* from Muhammad ibn 'Umar—who is al-Waqidi—with a weak chain to Ibn 'Awf from Ibn Mas'ud. It is *mursal* and weak, as previously mentioned.

[71] A narration from 'Abdullah ibn Zam'ah: Bilal came at the beginning of Rabi' al-Awwal and gave the call to prayer. The Prophet ﷺ said, "Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer." I went out and saw no one at the door except 'Umar and some men, Abu Bakr not being among them... Abu Dawud transmitted it with a good chain, similarly but abbreviated, without the statement, "Then 'A'ishah said, 'Abu Bakr is a tender-hearted man...'" and he did not say "at the beginning of Rabi' al-Awwal." He said, "Tell someone to lead the people in prayer," and [the Prophet] said, "Allah refuses that, and so do the believers," twice. In another narration of his, he said, "No, no, no! Let the son of Abu Quhafah lead the people in prayer," saying that angrily. As for what is at its end from the statement of 'A'ishah, it is in the two *Sahih* collections from her narration: She said, "O Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr is a tender-hearted man; if he stands in your place, the people will not hear him due to his weeping." He said, "You are like the companions of Yusuf. Tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer."

[72] A narration from 'A'ishah: On the day the Messenger of Allah ﷺ passed away, they noticed some lightness [in his condition] in the early part of the day. The men dispersed to their homes and their affairs, rejoicing, and they left the Messenger of Allah ﷺ with the women. While we were in that state—we had never been in such a state of hope and joy before—the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "Make way for me; this is an angel seeking permission..." The lengthy narration concerns the coming of the Angel of Death, then his departure, then the coming of Jibril, then the coming of the Angel of Death and his ﷺ passing. Al-Tabarani transmitted it in *al-Kabir* from the narration of Jabir and Ibn 'Abbas, with differences, in a long narration containing: When Monday came, the matter intensified, and Allah revealed to the Angel of Death: "Descend to My beloved and chosen one, Muhammad ﷺ, in the most beautiful form, and be gentle with him in taking his soul." It contains the Angel of Death entering and seeking permission to take it. He ﷺ said, "O Angel of Death, where did you leave my beloved Jibril?" He said, "I left him in the lowest heaven, with the angels consoling him over you." It was not long before Jibril came to him and sat at his head, and mentioned Jibril giving him glad tidings of what Allah had prepared for him. It contains: "Come closer, O Angel of Death, and proceed with what you have been commanded." The Angel of Death drew near, struggling to take the soul of the Prophet ﷺ, and mentioned distress over that, until he said: "Then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ passed away." It is a long narration spanning two large pages, and it is rejected. In it is 'Abd al-Mun'im ibn Idris ibn Sinan from his father from Wahb ibn Munabbih. Ahmad said he used to fabricate from Wahb ibn Munabbih, and Abu Idris is also abandoned, as al-Daraqutni said. Al-Tabarani also narrated it from the narration of al-Husayn ibn 'Ali that Jibril came to him first and said to him from his Lord, "How do you find yourself?" Then Jibril came to him on the third day with the Angel of Death and the Angel of the Air, Isma'il, and that Jibril entered first and asked him, then the Angel of Death sought permission and his statement, "Proceed with what you have been commanded." It is also rejected; in it is 'Abdullah ibn Maymun al-Qaddah. Al-Bukhari said, "His narrations are discarded." He also narrated it from the narration of Ibn 'Abbas concerning the Angel of Death coming first, seeking permission, and his statement, "Your Lord sends you greetings of peace." He ﷺ said, "Where is Jibril?" He said, "He is close to me now; he will come." So the Angel of Death went out until Jibril descended upon him... The narration contains al-Mukhtar ibn Nafi', whose narrations are rejected.

[73] A narration from 'A'ishah: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ passed away between the rising of the forenoon sun and midday on Monday. Narrated by Ibn 'Abd al-Barr.

[74] A narration from 'A'ishah: When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ passed away, the people were overcome when the wailing rose, and the angels shrouded the Messenger of Allah ﷺ with his garment. They differed: some denied his death, others were struck dumb and did not speak for a long time afterwards, others became confused though they had their senses, and others were made to sit down. 'Umar ibn al-Khattab was among those who denied his death.

And concerning those who remained seated and those who were silenced, Umar came out to the people and said, "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, has not died..." the narration continues until his statement, "with your Lord you are being shortened," I found no basis for it, and it is rejected.

[75] A narration reached Abu Bakr while he was among the Banu al-Harith ibn al-Khazraj, so he came and entered upon the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. He looked at him, then leaned over him, kissed him, and wept. Then he said, "May my father and mother be sacrificed for you, God would not make you taste death twice..." the narration continues to the end of his statement, "and it was as if the people had not heard this verse until that day." Al-Bukhari and Muslim reported it from the narration of Aisha that Abu Bakr came on a horse from his dwelling at al-Sunh until he dismounted and entered the mosque. He did not speak to the people until he entered upon Aisha, then he turned toward the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, who was covered with a striped garment. He uncovered his face, then leaned over him, kissed him, and wept. Then he said, "May my father and mother be sacrificed for you, by God, God will not combine two deaths upon you. As for the death that was decreed for you, you have already died it." Both of them reported from the narration of Ibn Abbas that Abu Bakr came out while Umar was speaking to the people... the narration includes, "by God, and it was as if the people did not know that God had revealed this verse until Abu Bakr recited it." Al-Bukhari's wording is in both.

[76] A narration that when the news reached Abu Bakr, he entered the house of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, while he was praying over the Prophet, peace be upon him, his eyes overflowing and his sobs rising like the crackling of a fire, yet he remained firm in action and speech. He leaned over him and uncovered the garment from his face... the narration continues to his statement, "and preserve him among us." Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in the Book of Consolation from the narration of Ibn Umar with a weak chain. Abu Bakr came while the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was shrouded, so he uncovered the garment from his face... the narration to its end.

[77] The narration of Ibn Umar regarding hearing consolation for him, peace be upon him: "Indeed, in God is a replacement for everyone, attainment for every desire, and salvation from every fear. So in God place your hope and in Him trust." Then they heard another after it: "Indeed, in God is solace from every calamity and compensation for every loss. So obey God and act by His command." Abu Bakr said, "This is al-Khidr and al-Yasa'." I did not find mention of al-Yasa' in it, but as for the mention of al-Khidr in consolation, al-Nawawi rejected it in the books of Hadith and said, "The companions only mentioned it." I say, rather, al-Hakim reported it in al-Mustadrak in the narration of Anas, but he did not authenticate it, and it is not authentic. Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in the Book of Consolation from the narration of Anas as well, saying: When the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was taken, his companions gathered around him weeping. A man entered upon them, tall with shoulder-length hair, wearing a waist-wrapper and cloak, stepping over the companions of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, until he took hold of the doorposts. He wept over the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, then turned to the companions and said, "Indeed, in God is solace from every calamity, compensation for every loss, and a replacement for every perished one. So turn in repentance to God Almighty, and look to Him in tribulation, so observe, for the afflicted is he who is not compensated by reward." Then the man left. Abu Bakr said, "Follow the man." They looked right and left but saw no one. Abu Bakr said, "Perhaps this is al-Khidr, the brother of our Prophet, upon him be peace, who came to console us." Al-Tabarani reported it in al-Awsat with a very weak chain. Ibn Abi al-Dunya also reported it from the narration of Ali ibn Abi Talib: When the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was taken, a visitor came whose sound we heard but whose person we did not see. He said, "Peace, mercy, and blessings of God be upon you. Indeed, in God is compensation for every calamity, a replacement for every perished one, and attainment for every loss. So trust in God and hope in Him, for the deprived is he who is deprived of reward. And peace be upon you." Ali said, "Do you know who this is? He is al-Khidr." In it is Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Sadiq, who has been criticized, and there is a break between Ali ibn al-Husayn and the grandfather of Ali. What is known from Ali ibn al-Husayn is transmitted as mursal without mention of Ali, as al-Shafi'i reported in al-Umm, and it contains no mention of al-Khidr.

[78] The narration of Abu Ja'far: "His grave was spread with his own spread and his quilt." In it: "He left behind no wealth after his death, nor did he build in his lifetime brick upon brick, nor place reed upon reed." As for placing the spread and his quilt, the one who placed the quilt was Shuqran, the freed slave of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. Mention of that is not a condition of our book. As for him not leaving wealth, that has preceded from the narration of Aisha and others. As for him not building in his lifetime, that has also preceded.

[79] A narration: Gabriel, peace be upon him, said to me, "At your service, Islam, upon the death of Umar." Abu Bakr al-Ajurri reported it in the Book of the Law from the narration of Ubayy ibn Ka'b with a very weak chain, and Ibn al-Jawzi mentioned it in al-Mawdu'at.

[80] The narration of Ibn Abbas: "Umar was placed on his bed, and the people surrounded him supplicating and praying..." he mentioned.

Ali ibn Abi Talib said: I often heard the Prophet, peace be upon him, say, "I, Abu Bakr, and Umar went..." The hadith is agreed upon.

[81] The hadith of Thumamah ibn Hazn al-Fushairi: "I witnessed the people of the house, and Uthman looked down upon them..." Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is hasan, and by al-Nasa'i.

[82] The hadith: When Salman was near death, he wept, and in it is: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, made a covenant with us that the portion of any of us from this world should be like the provision of a rider." Reported by Ahmad and al-Hakim, who authenticated it, and it has preceded.

[83] The hadith of al-Dahhak: A man said, "O Messenger of God, who are the most ascetic of people?" He said, "He who does not forget the graves and the..." The hadith has preceded.

[84] The hadith: "I have not seen a sight except that the grave is more dreadful than it." Preceded in the third chapter on the Etiquette of Companionship.

[85] The hadith of Umar: "We went out with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, to the graveyards, and he sat by a grave, and I was the closest of the people..." In it is: "This is the grave of Aminah bint Wahb. I sought permission from my Lord to visit her, and He permitted me." Preceded in the Etiquette of Companionship as well. Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in the Book of Graves from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, in which there is mention of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Its end in Ibn Majah is abbreviated, and in it is Ayyub ibn Hani', whom Ibn Ma'in weakened, while Abu Hatim said he is salih.

[86] The hadith of Uthman: He would, when he stood by a grave, weep until his beard became wet. In it is: "The grave is the first of the abodes of the Hereafter." Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who graded it hasan, and by Ibn Majah and al-Hakim, who authenticated it. Preceded in the Etiquette of Companionship.

[87] The hadith: "That I advance a miscarried fetus is more beloved to me than leaving behind a hundred horsemen, all of whom fight in the way of God." I did not find in it mention of a hundred horsemen. Ibn Majah reported from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "A miscarried fetus I advance before me is more beloved to me than a horseman I leave behind me."

[88] The hadith: "No one of the Muslims loses three children and they are withheld..." Preceded in the chapter on Marriage.

[89] The hadith of his prohibition against visiting graves, then his permission for that. Reported by Muslim from the hadith of Buraydah, and it has preceded.

[90] The hadith of Ali: "I had forbidden you from visiting graves, but visit them, for they remind you of the Hereafter, but do not speak foolishly." Reported by Ahmad and Abu Ya'la in his Musnad, and Ibn Abi al-Dunya in the Book of Graves, and the wording is his. Ahmad and Abu Ya'la did not say, "but do not speak foolishly." In it is Ali ibn Zayd ibn Jad'an from Rabi'ah ibn al-Nabighah. Al-Bukhari did not authenticate it, and Rabi'ah was mentioned by Ibn Hibban among the reliable narrators.

[91] The hadith: "The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, visited the grave of his mother with a thousand cloaked ones, and no day was seen with more weeping than that day." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in the Book of Graves from the hadith of Buraydah, and his shaykh, Ahmad ibn Imran al-Akhnas, is abandoned. It is reported similarly from another route: "We were with him, nearly a thousand riders." In it is that he was not given permission to seek forgiveness for her.

[92] The hadith: And he said on that day, "I was given permission for the visit, but not for seeking forgiveness." Preceded in the hadith before it from the hadith of Buraydah, that he was not given permission to seek forgiveness for her. Muslim reported it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "I sought permission from my Lord to seek forgiveness for my mother, but He did not permit me, and I sought permission to visit her grave, and He permitted me."

[93] The hadith of Ibn Abi Mulaikah: Aisha came one day from the graveyards, so I said, "O Mother of the Believers, from where have you come?" She said, "From the grave of my brother Abd al-Rahman." I said, "Did not the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, forbid it?" She said, "Yes, then he commanded it." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in the Graves with a good chain.

[94] The hadith of Abu Dharr: "Visit the graves, for they remind you of the Hereafter, and wash the dead, for handling an empty body is an eloquent admonition." The hadith of Ibn Abi al-Dunya in the Graves and al-Hakim with a good chain.

[95] The hadith of Ibn Abi Mulaikah: "Visit your dead, greet them, and pray for them." The hadith of Ibn Abi al-Dunya in it is like this, mursal, and its chain is hasan.

[96] Hadith: Whoever visits the grave of his parents or one of them every Friday, he will be forgiven and recorded as dutiful. Reported by al-Tabarani in al-Saghir and al-Awsat from the narration of Abu Hurayrah, and by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in al-Qubur from the narration of Muhammad ibn al-Nu'man, who attributed it to the Prophet (marfu'), but it is problematic (mu'dal) and Muhammad ibn al-Nu'man is unknown, and his shaykh in al-Tabarani's chain, Yahya ibn al-'Ala' al-Bajali, is abandoned (matruk).

[97] Hadith of Ibn Sirin: A man may die while his parents are alive and he is undutiful to them, then he supplicates to Allah for them after their death, so Allah records him among the dutiful. Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in his book, and it is a sound chain but interrupted (mursal). It was also narrated by Ibn 'Adi from the narration of Yahya ibn 'Uqbah Abu al-Ghayzaran from Muhammad ibn Jahadah from Anas. He said: And it was narrated by al-Salt ibn al-Hajjaj from Ibn Jahadah from Qatadah from Anas. Both Yahya ibn 'Uqbah and al-Salt ibn al-Hajjaj are weak.

[98] Hadith: Whoever visits my grave, my intercession becomes incumbent for him. Previously mentioned in the chapter on the secrets of Hajj.

[99] Hadith: Whoever visits me in Madinah seeking reward, I will be an intercessor and a witness for him on the Day of Resurrection. Previously mentioned there.

[100] Hadith of 'A'ishah: No man visits the grave of his brother and sits by it except that he finds solace with him and receives a response until he departs. Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in al-Qubur, and in its chain is 'Abdullah ibn Sam'an, whose condition I have not ascertained. It was narrated by Ibn 'Abd al-Barr in al-Tamhid from a hadith of Ibn 'Abbas with similar meaning, and 'Abd al-Haqq al-Ishbili authenticated it.

[101] Hadith: The deceased in his grave is but like a drowning man calling for help, awaiting a supplication that reaches him from his father, or his brother, or a friend of his... The hadith. Reported by Abu Mansur al-Daylami in Musnad al-Firdaws from a hadith of Ibn 'Abbas. In its chain is al-Hasan ibn 'Ali ibn 'Abd al-Wahid. Al-Dhahabi said: He narrated from Hisham ibn 'Ammar a baseless hadith.

[102] Hadith of Sa'id ibn 'Abdullah al-Azdi: I was present with Abu Umamah al-Bahili while he was in the throes of death, and he said: O Sa'id, when I die, do with me as the Messenger of Allah commanded us. He said: When one of you dies and you have leveled the earth over him, let one of you stand at the head of his grave and say: O so-and-so, son of so-and-so... The hadith concerning prompting the deceased in his grave. Al-Tabarani reported it thus with a weak chain.

[103] Hadith: When your companion dies, leave him and do not disturb him. Reported by Abu Dawud from a hadith of 'A'ishah with a sound (jayyid) chain.

[104] Hadith: Do not revile the dead, for they have gone forward to what they have sent forth. Reported by al-Bukhari also from a hadith of 'A'ishah.
