[105] Hadith: Do not mention your dead except with good... The hadith. Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in al-Mawt thus with a weak chain from a hadith of 'A'ishah. It is in al-Nasa'i from a hadith of 'A'ishah with a sound (jayyid) chain, supported. The wording mentioned here is 'your perished ones'. The compiler of Musnad al-Firdaws mentioned the addition and marked it with the sign of al-Nasa'i and al-Tabarani.

[106] Hadith of Anas: A funeral passed by the Messenger of Allah and they praised the deceased with evil, so he said: "It has become incumbent..." Agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh).

[107] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: A servant may die and the people praise him with praise, while Allah knows otherwise from him... The hadith. Reported by Ahmad from the narration of a shaykh from the people of Basrah from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet: He attributes to his Lord, Mighty and Majestic: There is no Muslim servant who dies and three households of his closest neighbors testify to his goodness except that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, says: I have accepted the testimony of My servants concerning what they knew, and I have forgiven him for what I know.

[108] Hadith: Permission was not given to the Messenger of Allah to speak concerning the soul. Agreed upon from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud concerning the Jews' question about the soul and the revelation of His saying, Exalted is He: "And they ask you about the soul..." Previously mentioned.

[109] Hadith: His call to those slain among the chieftains of Quraysh on the day of Badr: O so-and-so, I have found what my Lord promised me to be true. Reported by Muslim from the hadith of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.

[110] Hadith: The grave is either a pit from the pits of the Fire or a garden from the gardens of Paradise. Reported by al-Tirmidhi.

From the narration of Abu Sa'id, previously mentioned in the chapter on Hope and Fear.

[111] Narration of Anas: "Death is the Resurrection; whoever dies, his resurrection has come." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" with a weak chain, and it has been previously mentioned.

[112] Narration: "When one of you dies, his place is shown to him morning and evening." Agreed upon as authentic from the narration of Ibn 'Umar.

[113] Narration of Abu Hurayrah: "Whoever dies as a stranger dies a martyr and is protected from the trial of the grave." Reported by Ibn Majah with a weak chain, and he said: "the trial of the grave." Ibn Abi al-Dunya said: "the two testers."

[114] Narration of 'A'ishah: "Shall I not give you glad tidings, O Jabir?" The narration includes: "Indeed, God revived your father and seated him before Him." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" with a chain containing weakness, and by al-Tirmidhi who graded it as good, and by Ibn Majah from the narration of Jabir: "Shall I not give you glad tidings of what God has done for your father?" He said: "Yes, O Messenger of God." The narration includes: "So He said: 'O My servant, ask of Me, I will grant you.' He said: 'My Lord, revive me so that I may be killed for You again.' The Lord, Glorified is He, said: 'It has already preceded from Me that they do not return.'"

[115] Narration: He said to a man who had died: "This one has become vacant from the world and left it for its people. If he was pleased, it would not please him to return to the world, just as it does not please any of you to return to his mother's womb." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya from the narration of 'Amr ibn Dinar as a mursal report, and its narrators are trustworthy.

[116] Narration: "The likeness of the believer in the world is like a fetus in its mother's womb. When it emerges from her womb, it cries over its exit until, when it sees the light and is placed down, it does not desire to return to its place." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya therein from the narration of Baqiyyah from Jabir ibn Ghanim al-Salafi from Sulaym ibn 'Amir al-Jana'izi as a mursal report like this.

[117] Narration: It was said to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him: "So-and-so has died." He said: "Is he relieved, or are others relieved of him?" Agreed upon as authentic from the narration of Abu Qatadah with the wording: "A funeral passed by him, and he said that." It is in Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Al-Mawt" with the wording cited by the author.

[118] Narration of al-Nu'man ibn Bashir: "Behold, nothing remains of the world except like a fly buzzing in its interior. So fear God, fear God concerning your brothers among the people of the graves, for your deeds are presented to them." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya, Abu Bakr ibn Lal, from the narration of Malik ibn Adi from al-Nu'man as his saying: "Fear God, fear God." Al-Azdi reported it in full in "Al-Du'afa" and said its chain is not sound. Ibn Abi Hatim mentioned it in full in "Al-Jarh wa al-Ta'dil" in the biography of Abu Isma'il al-Sakuni, a narration from Malik ibn Adi, and he transmitted from his father that both of them are unknown. Al-Azdi said: "Its chain is not sound." Ibn Hibban mentioned Malik ibn Adi in "Al-Thiqat."

[119] Narration of Abu Hurayrah: "Do not disgrace your dead with the evils of your deeds, for they are presented to your loved ones among the people of the graves." Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya and al-Mahamili with a weak chain. Ahmad has it from the narration of one who heard a man from Anas: "Your deeds are presented to your relatives and kin among the dead."

[120] Narration of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: "The deceased recognizes the one who washes him, the one who carries him, and the one who lowers him into his grave." Reported by Ahmad from the narration of a man from him whose name is Mu'awiyah or Ibn Mu'awiyah—'Abd al-Malik ibn Hasan forgot it.

[121] Narration of Abu Ayyub: "When the soul of a believer is taken, the people of mercy from God's presence receive it as one receives a bearer of glad tidings, saying: 'Look after your brother until he finds rest.'" Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Kitab al-Mawt" and al-Tabarani in "Musnad al-Shamiyyin" with a weak chain. Ibn al-Mubarak reported it in "Al-Zuhd" as a mawquf report stopping at Abu Ayyub with a sound chain. Ibn Sa'id elevated it to marfu' in his additions to "Al-Zuhd," and in it is Salam al-Tawil, who is weak. It is found in al-Nasa'i and Ibn Hibban similarly from the narration of Abu Hurayrah with a sound chain.

[122] Narration: "The grave says to the deceased when he is placed in it: 'Woe to you, O son of Adam! What deluded you concerning me? Did you not know that I am the abode of trial?'" Reported by Ibn Abi al-Dunya in "Kitab al-Qubur," al-Tabarani in "Musnad al-Shamiyyin," and Abu Ahmad al-Hakim in "Al-Sukuni" from the narration of Abu al-Hajjaj al-Tamali with a chain.

[123] A weak narration. The hadith of Abdullah ibn 'Ubayd ibn 'Umayr: It reached me that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "The deceased sits up and hears the footsteps of those escorting him, and none speaks to him except his grave, which says: 'Woe to you, O son of Adam...'" Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in "Al-Qubur" in this manner as a mursal narration, and its narrators are trustworthy. Ibn al-Mubarak reported it in "Al-Zuhd," except he said: "It reached me," and did not attribute it directly to the Prophet.

[124] The hadith of al-Bara': We went out with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, for the funeral of a man from the Ansar. The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, sat at his grave, his head bowed, then said: "O God, I seek refuge in You from the punishment of the grave..." in its full length. Abu Dawud and al-Hakim reported it in full, the latter saying it is sound according to the conditions of al-Bukhari and Muslim. Ibn Hibban deemed it weak. Al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah reported it in an abbreviated form.

[125] The hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "When the believer is present (at death), the angels come to him with a silk cloth containing musk and bundles of sweet basil..." Ibn Abi al-Dunya and Ibn Hibban reported it with variations, and al-Bazzar with the wording of the author.

[126] The hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "The believer in his grave is in a verdant meadow, and his grave is expanded for him seventy cubits..." Ibn Hibban also reported it.

[127] The hadith: "The possessor of one dirham will have an easier reckoning than the possessor of two dirhams." I found no basis for it.

[128] The hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "When a servant dies, two black, blue-eyed angels come to him. One is called Munkar and the other Nakir..." Al-Tirmidhi reported it and deemed it fair, and Ibn Hibban with variations.

[129] The hadith of 'Ata' ibn Yasar: He said: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: "O 'Umar, how will it be with you when you die and your people take you and measure for you three cubits by a cubit and a span..." Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in "Kitab al-Qubur" in this manner as a mursal narration, and its narrators are trustworthy. Al-Bayhaqi said in "Al-I'tiqad": We reported it through a sound chain from 'Ata' ibn Yasar as mursal. I say: Ibn Battah connected it in "Al-Ibanah" through a narration from Ibn 'Abbas. Al-Bayhaqi reported it in "Al-I'tiqad" through a narration from 'Umar and said it is rare with this chain; Mufaddal alone narrated it. Ahmad and Ibn Hibban have it from a narration of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, where 'Umar said: "Will our intellects be returned to us?" He said: "Yes, just as you are today." 'Umar said: "Then with his mouth, the stone."

[130] The hadith of Hudhayfah: I was with the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, at a funeral, and he sat at the head of the grave, then began to look into it... Ahmad reported it with a weak chain.

[131] The hadith of 'A'ishah: "The grave has a pressure; if anyone were to be saved or delivered from it, Sa'd ibn Mu'adh would have been saved." Ahmad reported it with a sound chain.

[132] The hadith of Anas: Zaynab, the daughter of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, died, and she was a woman often ill... In it: "She was indeed pressed with a pressure whose sound was heard between the two horizons." Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in "Al-Mawt" from the narration of Sulayman al-A'mash from Anas, but he did not hear it directly from him.

[133] The hadith: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, saw the pressure of the grave in the case of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh and in the case of his daughter Zaynab, and likewise was the state of Abu Jadir when he was martyred. The three preceding hadiths were mentioned in the previous chapter.

[134] The hadith: "A good dream is one part of forty-six parts of prophethood." Previously mentioned.

[135] The hadith concerning the command for purification before sleep, agreed upon as sound, from the hadith of al-Bara': "When you go to your bed, perform ablution as you would for prayer..."

[136] The hadith: The conquest of Makkah was revealed to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, in a dream. Ibn Abi Hatim reported it in his Tafsir from the narration of Mujahid as mursal.

[137] The hadith: "The Spirit of Holiness breathed into my heart: Love whom you love, for you shall part from him..." Previously mentioned.

[138] The hadith: "He left not brick upon brick nor reed upon reed." Also previously mentioned.

[139] The hadith: "He left neither dinar nor dirham." Also previously mentioned.

[140] The hadith: "If I were to take an intimate friend, I would have taken Abu Bakr, but your companion is the intimate friend of the Merciful." Also previously mentioned.

[141] The hadith: "Whoever sees me in a dream has indeed seen me, for Satan cannot assume my form," agreed upon as sound from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah.

[142] A narration from Ibn 'Uyaynah, from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir, from Jabir: "The Prophet (peace be upon him) was never asked for anything but that he said, 'No.'" Reported by Muslim, and it has preceded.

[143] A narration: Allah the Exalted said, "The son of Adam reviles Me, though it is not fitting for him to revile Me. And he denies Me, though it is not fitting for him to deny Me..." The hadith was reported by al-Bukhari from the narration of Abu Hurayrah.

[144] A narration: "How can I be at ease when the bearer of the Trumpet has already placed it to his mouth, inclined his forehead, and is listening for when he will be commanded?" Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of Abu Sa'id, who said it is *hasan* (good). Ibn Majah reported it with the wording: "Indeed my two companions (or: in their hands are two trumpets), they are gazing intently, awaiting when they will be commanded." In the narration of Ibn Majah: al-Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah is disputed.

[145] A narration: "When He sent to the bearer of the Trumpet, he gestured with it to his mouth, putting one foot forward and the other back..." I have not found it exactly like this. Rather, it has been reported that Israfil has been thus since the beginning of creation. As reported by al-Bukhari in *al-Tarikh* and Abu al-Shaykh in *Kitab al-'Azamah* from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "When Allah, Blessed and Exalted, finished creating the heavens and the earth, He created the Trumpet and gave it to Israfil. So he has it placed at his mouth, his gaze fixed towards the Throne, awaiting when he will be commanded." Al-Bukhari said: "It is not established (*sahih*)." In a narration of Abu al-Shaykh: "The bearer of the Trumpet has not blinked since he was entrusted with it, prepared, looking towards the Throne, fearing that he might be commanded before his glance returns to him. It is as if his two eyes are two shining stars." Its chain is good.

[146] A narration: "People will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection on a white, reddish-white earth, like a pure loaf of bread, wherein there is no landmark for anyone." Agreed upon from the narration of Sahl ibn Sa'd. Al-Bukhari separated the statement "wherein there is no landmark for anyone," making it from the words of Sahl or another, while Muslim included it within the hadith.

[147] A narration: "People will be resurrected barefoot, naked, uncircumcised. Sweat will bridle them, reaching to the fat of their ears." Sawdah, the narrator of the hadith, said, "Oh, how wretched!" The hadith was reported by al-Tha'labi and al-Baghawi, and it is in the two *Sahih* collections from the narration of 'A'ishah, and she is the one who said, "Oh, how wretched!" Al-Tabarani reported it in *al-Awsat* from the narration of Umm Salamah, and she is the one who said, "Oh, how wretched!"

[148] A narration from Abu Hurayrah: "People will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection riding, walking, and on their faces..." Reported by al-Tirmidhi who graded it *hasan*. In the two *Sahih* collections from the narration of Anas: A man said, "O Prophet of Allah, how will the disbeliever be gathered on his face?" He said, "Is not He Who made him walk on two legs in this world able to make him walk on his face on the Day of Resurrection?"

[149] A narration from Ibn 'Umar: "On the Day when people will stand before the Lord of the worlds, until one of them is submerged in his sweat up to the middle of his ears." Agreed upon.

[150] A narration from Abu Hurayrah: "People will sweat on the Day of Resurrection until their sweat goes into the earth seventy cubits." The two (al-Bukhari and Muslim) reported it in the two *Sahih* collections, as mentioned by the author.

[151] A narration: "Standing, their eyes fixed for forty years towards the sky. Sweat will bridle them from the intensity of the distress." Reported by Ibn 'Adi from the narration of Ibn Mas'ud. In it is Abu Taybah 'Isa ibn Sulayman al-Jurjani. Ibn Ma'in weakened him, and Ibn 'Adi said, "I do not think he would intentionally lie, but perhaps he was mistaken."

[152] A narration from 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir: "The sun will draw near to the earth on the Day of Resurrection, and people will sweat. Among them will be one whose sweat reaches his ankles..." Reported by Ahmad. In it is Ibn Lahi'ah.

[153] A narration from Ibn 'Umar: He recited this verse: "On the Day when people will stand before the Lord of the worlds..." Then he said, "How will you be when Allah gathers you as arrows are gathered in a quiver, for fifty thousand years, without looking at you?" I (the compiler) say: It is only 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar. Al-Tabarani reported it in *al-Kabir*. In it is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Maysarah. Ibn Abi Hatim did not mention a narrator for it other than Ibn Wahb. They have, other than 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Maysarah al-Hadrami, four; this one is an Egyptian, and the other three are Syrians.

[154] A narration: He was asked about the length of that day. He said, "By the One in Whose Hand is my soul, it will be lightened for the believer until it becomes easier for him than a prescribed prayer he prays in this world." Reported by Abu Ya'la and al-Bayhaqi in *al-Shu'ab* from the narration of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. In it is Ibn Lahi'ah. Ibn Wahb reported it from 'Amr ibn al-Harith instead of Ibn Lahi'ah, and it is *hasan* (good). Abu Ya'la has it from the narration of Abu Hurayrah with a good chain: "That will be made light for the believer like the descent of the sun at sunset until it sets." Al-Bayhaqi reported it in...

The people continued until he said, I believe it is raised with the wording: Indeed, Allah lightens for whom He wills among His servants its length, like the time of an obligatory prayer.

[155] The hadith: "Surah Hud, Al-Waqi'ah, Al-Mursalat, 'Amma Yatasa'alun, and Idha Ash-Shamsu Kuwwirat have aged me." Reported by At-Tirmidhi who graded it hasan, and Al-Hakim who authenticated it, and it has preceded.

[156] The hadith: "Indeed, for Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is an angel between the two edges of his eyes is a distance of one hundred years." I have not seen it with this wording.

[157] The hadith of Abu Hurairah: "Will we see our Lord on the Day of Resurrection?" He said, "Do you have any difficulty in seeing the sun at midday when there is no cloud?" The hadith is agreed upon, except for his saying "Then the servant is cast..." for which Muslim reported it uniquely.

[158] The hadith of Anas: "Do you know what He laughs from?" We said, "Allah and His Messenger know best." He said, "From the servant addressing his Lord..." The hadith is reported by Muslim.

[159] The hadith: A man asked Ibn 'Umar, saying, "How did you hear the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say concerning the private conversation?" The hadith is reported by Muslim.

[160] The hadith: "Whoever conceals the fault of a believer, Allah will conceal his faults on the Day of Resurrection." It has preceded.

[161] The hadith: "There is not one of you except that the Lord of the worlds will question him..." The hadith is agreed upon from the narration of Ibn 'Adiyy from Abu Hatim with the wording "except that He will speak to him..."

[162] The hadith: "One of you will certainly stand before Allah, Mighty and Majestic, with no interpreter between him and Him..." Reported by Al-Bukhari from the hadith of 'Adiyy ibn Hatim.

[163] The hadith of Al-Hasan: That 'A'ishah mentioned the Hereafter and wept... The hadith includes: So he said, "What makes you weep, O 'A'ishah?" She said, "I remembered the Hereafter. Will you remember your families on the Day of Resurrection?" Reported by Abu Dawud from the narration of Al-Hasan that she mentioned the Fire and wept, so he said, "What makes you weep?" without mentioning that his head, peace be upon him, was in her lap and that he was drowsy, and its chain is *jayyid* (sound).

[164] The hadith: "Allah will say: 'O Adam, arise and send forth the contingent to the Fire.' He will say: 'And how many is the contingent to the Fire?' He will say: 'From every thousand, nine hundred and ninety-nine.'" The hadith is agreed upon from the narration of Abu Sa'id Al-Khudri, and Al-Bukhari reported it from the hadith of Abu Hurairah similarly, and it has preceded.

[165] The hadith of Abu Hurairah: "Do you know who the bankrupt is?" They said, "The bankrupt, O Messenger of Allah, is one who has no dirham nor any property." It has preceded.

[166] The hadith: "O Abu Dharr, do you know what they are butting heads over?" I said, "No." He said, "But your Lord knows, and He will judge between them." Reported by Ahmad from the narration of shaykhs who were not named, from Abu Dharr.

[167] The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: "Indeed, Satan has despaired that idols will be worshipped in the land of the Arabs, but he will be content with you having less than that: the minor sins, and they are the destructive sins." The hadith, and at its end: "And the likeness of that is like travelers who alight in a desert..." Reported by Ahmad and Al-Bayhaqi in *Ash-Shu'ab*, limited to its end: "Beware of the minor sins, for they gather upon a man until they destroy him. And indeed, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, gave a parable for them..." and its chain is *jayyid*. As for the first part of the hadith, Muslim reported it concisely from the hadith of Jabir: "Indeed, Satan has despaired that those who pray will worship him in the Arabian Peninsula, but [he is content] with inciting strife among them."

[168] The hadith: When the verse was revealed: "Indeed, you are to die, and indeed, they are to die. Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, before your Lord, will dispute" (Az-Zumar: 30-31), Az-Zubayr said, "O Messenger of Allah, will what was between us be repeated for us?" Reported by Ahmad with this wording, and At-Tirmidhi from the hadith of Az-Zubayr, and he said: Hasan Sahih.

[169] The hadith of Anas: "The servants will be gathered naked, *ghurran*, *buhman*." We said, "What are *buhman*?" He said, "With nothing with them..." I say: It is not from the hadith of Anas; rather it is from 'Ubaydullah ibn Unays. Ahmad reported it with a *hasan* chain and said "*ghurla*" instead of "*ghurran*."

[170] The hadith of Anas: While the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was sitting, we saw him laugh until his front teeth showed. 'Umar said, "What makes you laugh, O Messenger of Allah? May my father and mother be sacrificed for you!" He said, "Two men from my nation knelt before the Lord of the worlds..." the hadith at length. Reported by Ibn Abi Ad-Dunya in *Husn Az-Zann Billah* and Al-Hakim in *Al-Mustadrak*, and it has preceded.

[171] A Hadith states: The Sirat (Bridge) will be erected across the midst of Hellfire, and I will be the first to cross it. Agreed upon, from the lengthy Hadith of Abu Hurairah.

[172] A Hadith of Abu Sa'id: Mankind will be gathered upon a bridge over Hell, upon which are thorns, hooks, and barbed spikes. The Hadith is agreed upon, with differences in wording.

[173] A Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: Allah will gather the first and the last for an appointed Day, standing for forty years, their gazes fixed towards the sky, awaiting the decree. He said: And he mentioned the Hadith up to the mention of the believers prostrating. The lengthy Hadith was narrated by Ibn 'Adi and Al-Hakim; a portion of it has preceded in an abbreviated form.

[174] A Hadith of Anas: The Sirat is like the edge of a sword or like the edge of a hair. Al-Bayhaqi in Al-Shu'ab reported it and said: This chain is weak. He said: And it is narrated from Ziyad al-Numayri from Anas, raised to the Prophet: The Sirat is like the edge of a hair or like the edge of a sword. He said: And this narration is sound. Ahmad narrated it from the Hadith of 'A'ishah, and in its chain is Ibn Lahi'ah.

[175] A Hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As: That the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, recited the saying of Ibrahim, peace be upon him: "My Lord, indeed they have led astray many of the people. So whoever follows me, then he is of me; and whoever disobeys me - indeed, You are Forgiving and Merciful." And the saying of 'Isa, peace be upon him: "If You punish them, indeed they are Your servants." Then he raised his hands and said: "My Ummah, my Ummah," and wept. The Hadith includes: O Jibril, go to Muhammad and say: We shall please you and not grieve you concerning your Ummah. I say: It is not from the Hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As, but rather from the Hadith of his son 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As, as Muslim narrated it. Perhaps the mention of 'Abdullah was omitted from some copies of the Ihya'.

[176] A Hadith: I have been given five things not given to anyone before me... and among them: I have been given Intercession. Agreed upon, from the Hadith of Jabir: On the Day of Resurrection, I will be the Imam of the Prophets, their orator, and the possessor of their intercession, without boasting. Al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah reported it from the Hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b. Al-Tirmidhi said: Hasan Sahih.

[177] A Hadith: I am the master of the children of Adam, without boasting. Al-Tirmidhi reported it and said: Hasan, and Ibn Majah from the Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.

[178] A Hadith: For every Prophet is a supplication that is answered. I wish to reserve my supplication as intercession for my Ummah on the Day of Resurrection. Agreed upon, from the Hadith of Anas. Muslim narrated it from the Hadith of Abu Hurairah.

[179] A Hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: Pulpits of gold will be set up for the Prophets, and they will sit upon them, but my pulpit will remain; I will not sit upon it, standing before my Lord, erect. Al-Tabarani in Al-Awsat reported it. In its chain are Muhammad ibn Thabit and Al-Banani, who are weak.

[180] A Hadith: Indeed, I will intercede on the Day of Resurrection for more than the stones and clay upon the face of the earth. Ahmad and Al-Tabarani reported it from the Hadith of Buraidah with a Hasan chain.

[181] A Hadith of Abu Hurairah: That the Prophet, peace be upon him, was brought some meat, and the foreleg was raised to him—and he liked it—so he took a bite from it. Then he said: I am the master of mankind... the lengthy Hadith concerning Intercession. He said: And in another Hadith with this context, the sins of Ibrahim are mentioned. Agreed upon. This second narration was reported by Muslim.

[182] A Hadith: A man from my Ummah will cause more people to enter Paradise by his intercession than (the tribes of) Rabi'ah and Mudar. We narrated it in the compilation of Abu 'Umar ibn al-Sammak from the Hadith of Abu Umamah, except he said: Like one of the two communities, Rabi'ah and Mudar. In it: It is as if the elders consider that man to be 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, and its chain is Hasan. Al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Al-Hakim have from the Hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Abi al-Jad'a: A man from my Ummah will cause more people to enter Paradise by his intercession than (the tribe of) Banu Tamim. They said: Other than you? He said: Other than me. Al-Tirmidhi said: Hasan Sahih, and Al-Hakim said: Sahih. It is said he meant by "the man": Uways.

[183] A Hadith: It will be said to a man: Stand, O so-and-so, and intercede. So he will stand and intercede for the tribe, for the household, for one man and two men, according to the measure of his deeds. Al-Tirmidhi reported it from the Hadith of Abu Sa'id: That among my Ummah are those who will intercede for large groups, and among them are those who will intercede for a tribe... and he said: Hasan. Al-Bazzar has from the Hadith of Anas: That a man will intercede for two or three.

[184] A Hadith of Anas: That a man from the people of Paradise will look down from a height on the Day of Resurrection upon the people of the Fire. A man from the people of the Fire will call to him and say: O so-and-so, do you recognize me? He will say: No, by Allah, I do not recognize you. Who are you?

He says: I am the one whom you passed by in the world one day and asked me for a drink, so I gave you to drink. The hadith concerning his intercession in this matter and his extraction from the Fire was reported by Abu Mansur al-Daylami in Musnad al-Firdaws with a weak chain.

[185] The hadith of Anas: I will be the first of the people to emerge when they are resurrected. The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is hasan gharib.

[186] The hadith: Then I will be clothed in a garment from the garments of Paradise, then I will stand at the right side of the Throne. The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and he said it is hasan gharib sahih.

[187] The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: Some people from the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, were sitting waiting for him. He came out, and when he drew near to them, he heard them conversing and heard their talk. Some of them said: How amazing! Allah has taken from His creation a close friend; He took Ibrahim as a close friend. The hadith was narrated by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is gharib.

[188] The hadith of Anas: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, dozed off lightly, then raised his head smiling. They said to him: O Messenger of Allah, what made you smile? He said: A verse was just revealed to me, and he recited: "In the name of Allah, the Entirely Merciful, the Especially Merciful. Indeed, We have granted you, [O Muhammad], al-Kawthar." Reported by Muslim.

[189] The hadith of Anas: While I was walking in Paradise, I came upon a river whose banks were domes of hollow pearl. The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is hasan sahih, and al-Bukhari reported it from the statement of Anas concerning when the Prophet, peace be upon him, was ascended to the heaven. The hadith is elevated (marfu'), even though it was not explicitly stated as being from the Prophet, peace be upon him.

[190] The hadith of Anas: The distance between the two sides of my Basin is like the distance between al-Madinah and Sana'a, or like the distance between al-Madinah and 'Amman. Reported by Muslim.

[191] The hadith of Ibn 'Umar: When the verse was revealed: "Indeed, We have granted you, [O Muhammad], al-Kawthar," the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: It is a river in Paradise, its banks are of gold. The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi with a difference in wording, and he said it is hasan sahih. Al-Darimi reported it in his Musnad, and it is closer to the wording of the author.

[192] The hadith of Thawban: Indeed, my Basin is from 'Aden to 'Amman al-Balqa'. The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is gharib, and by Ibn Majah.

[193] The hadith of Abu Dharr: I said: O Messenger of Allah, what are the vessels of the Basin? He said: By the One in Whose hand is my soul, its vessels are more numerous than the stars of the sky. Reported by Muslim.

[194] The hadith of Samurah: Indeed, every prophet has a basin, and they vie with one another as to which of them has more arrivals. The hadith was reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is gharib. He said: Al-Ash'ath ibn 'Abd al-Malik narrated this hadith from al-Hasan from the Prophet, peace be upon him, as mursal, and he did not mention Samurah in it, and that is more sound.

[195] The hadith: Indeed, in Hellfire there are seventy thousand valleys; in every valley are seventy thousand ravines; in every ravine are seventy thousand serpents and seventy thousand scorpions. The disbeliever and the hypocrite will not cease until all of that befalls him. I have not found it exactly like this in its entirety. What has been reported concerning the mention of serpents and scorpions will come after this.

[196] The hadith of 'Ali: Seek refuge with Allah from the Pit of Sorrow or the Valley of Sorrow. The hadith was reported by Ibn 'Adi with the wording "Valley of Sorrow," and he said it is batil (false). Abu Nu'aym and al-Asbahani reported it with a weak chain. Al-Tirmidhi reported it and said it is gharib, and Ibn Majah reported it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah with the wording "Pit of Sorrow." Ibn 'Adi weakened it. It was mentioned previously in the condemnation of arrogance and ostentation.

[197] The hadith of Abu Hurayrah: We were with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when we heard a loud crash. The hadith includes: This is a stone that was cast into Hellfire. Reported by Muslim.

[198] The hadith: The person among the people of the Fire with the lightest punishment on the Day of Resurrection is one who will be given two sandals of fire. The hadith is agreed upon from the hadith of al-Nu'man ibn Bashir.

[199] The hadith: Indeed, the fire of this world was washed seventy times with the waters of mercy until the people of this world could bear it. Ibn 'Abd al-Barr mentioned it from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: This fire was struck with the water of the sea seven times, and were it not for that, no one would have benefited from it. Al-Bazzar reported it from the hadith of Anas, and it is weak: "It did not reach you until—I think he said—it was sprinkled with water, so it gives you light."

[200] The hadith: Allah commanded that the Fire be kindled for a thousand years until it became red. This was mentioned previously.

[201] The hadith: The Fire complained to its Lord, saying: O my Lord, part of me consumes another part. So He permitted it two breaths.

[202] Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: "If a bucket of foul pus were poured upon the world, it would cause the people of the earth to stink." Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said we only know it from the narration of Rushd ibn Sa'd, and there is weakness in it.

[203] Hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: "If a single drop of the tree of Zaqqum were to drip into the dwellings of the world, it would ruin the livelihood of the people of the earth." Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is hasan sahih, and by Ibn Majah.

[204] Hadith of Anas: "Desire that for which He has made you desire, and beware and fear that from which He has warned you—the punishment and chastisement of God from Hellfire." I did not find a chain of transmission for this hadith.

[205] Hadith of Abu al-Darda': "Hunger will be cast upon the people of the Fire until it equals the torment they are in, so they will cry out for food." Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of Samurah ibn 'Atiyyah from Shahr ibn Hawshab from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda'. Al-Darimi said, "The people do not know this hadith; it is only narrated from al-A'mash from Samurah ibn 'Atiyyah from Shahr from Umm al-Darda' from Abu al-Darda', his saying."

[206] Hadith of Abu Umamah concerning His saying, the Exalted: 'And he will be given to drink from boiling water, which he will gulp but can scarcely swallow' (Quran 14:16-17). He said, "It is brought near to him..." Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who said it is ghareeb.

[207] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "Whoever is given wealth by God and does not pay its Zakat, his wealth will be made to appear to him on the Day of Resurrection as a bald-headed poisonous snake." Reported by al-Bukhari from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and by Muslim from the hadith of Jabir, similarly.

[208] Hadith: "Indeed, in the Fire are snakes like the necks of Bactrian camels; their sting..." Reported by Ahmad from the narration of Ibn Lahi'ah from Diraj from 'Abdullah ibn al-Harith ibn Juz'.

[209] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "The molar tooth of the disbeliever in the Fire is like (Mount) Uhud." Reported by Muslim.

[210] Hadith: "His lower lip will be drooping onto his chest, and the upper one will be raised, covering his face." Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the hadith of Abu Sa'id, and he said it is hasan sahih ghareeb.

[211] Hadith: "Indeed, the tongue of the disbeliever will be dragged for two parasangs on the Day of Resurrection, and the people will tread upon it." Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of Abu al-Mukhariq from Ibn 'Umar, and he said it is ghareeb, and Abu al-Mukhariq is unknown.

[212] Hadith: "Hellfire will be brought on that Day with seventy thousand reins..." Reported by Muslim from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.

[213] Hadith of Anas: "Weeping will be sent upon the people of the Fire, and they will weep until their tears are exhausted." Reported by Ibn Majah from the narration of Yazid al-Raqashi from Anas, and al-Raqashi is weak.

[214] Hadith: "Death will be brought on the Day of Resurrection as if it were a speckled ram, and it will be slaughtered." Reported by al-Bukhari from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Sa'id, and it has preceded.

[215] Hadith: "On the Day of Resurrection, a group of people will be commanded from the Fire to Paradise. When they draw near to it and inhale its fragrance..." We have narrated it in the 'Forty' of Abu Hadiyah from Anas, and Abu Hadiyah, Ibrahim ibn Hadiyah, is lost/perished.

[216] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "A caller will call out, 'Indeed, you have health, so you shall never fall ill.'" Reported by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah and Abu Sa'id.

[217] Hadith: "Two gardens of silver—their vessels and what is in them—and two gardens of gold—their vessels and what is in them..." Agreed upon from the hadith of Abu Musa.

[218] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "Whoever spends a pair from his wealth in the cause of God will be called from the gates of Paradise..." Agreed upon.

[219] Hadith: "I will come on the Day of Resurrection to the gate of Paradise and seek to open it. The keeper will say, 'Who are you?' I will say, 'Muhammad.'" Reported by Muslim from the hadith of Anas.

[220] Hadith of Abu Sa'id: "Indeed, the people of Paradise will see the people of the chambers above them as you see the shining star." Agreed upon, and it has preceded.

[221] Hadith: "Indeed, the people of the highest degrees will be seen by those beneath them as they see the rising star." Reported by al-Tirmidhi, who graded it hasan, and by Ibn Majah from the hadith of Abu Sa'id.

[222] Hadith of Jabir: "Shall I not inform you of the chambers of Paradise?" I said, "Yes, O Messenger of God, may my father and mother be your ransom." He said, "In Paradise there are chambers made of various types of jewels..." The hadith was reported by Abu Nu'aym from the narration of al-Hasan from Jabir.

[223] Hadith: He was asked about the saying of the Exalted, "And pleasant dwellings in Gardens of perpetual residence" [9:72]. He said, "Palaces of pearl..." The hadith was reported by Abu al-Shaykh Ibn Hibban in *Kitab al-'Azamah* and al-Ajurri in *Kitab al-Nasihah* from the narration of al-Hasan ibn Khalifah from al-Hasan, who said: I asked Abu Hurayrah and 'Imran ibn Husayn about this verse. It is not sound, and al-Hasan ibn Khalifah was not recognized by Ibn Abi Hatim, and al-Hasan al-Basri did not hear from Abu Hurayrah according to the majority opinion.

[224] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "The wall of Paradise is a brick of silver and a brick of gold; its dust is saffron and its clay is musk." Al-Tirmidhi reported it with the wording, "and its mortar is musk," and said its chain is not that strong and it is not, in my view, continuous. Al-Bazzar reported it from the hadith of Abu Sa'id with a chain containing criticism, and reported it as a *mawquf* statement [attributed to a Companion] with a sound chain.

[225] Hadith: He was asked about the soil of Paradise. He said, "White camphor, pure musk." Muslim reported it from the hadith of Abu Sa'id that Ibn Sayyad asked the Prophet ﷺ about that, and he mentioned it.

[226] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "Whoever is pleased that God gives him wine to drink in the Hereafter, let him abandon it in this world. And whoever is pleased that God clothes him in silk in the Hereafter, let him abandon it in this world." Al-Tabarani reported it in *al-Awsat* with a good chain. Al-Nasa'i reported with a sound chain: "Whoever wears silk in this world will not wear it in the Hereafter, and whoever drinks wine in this world will not drink it in the Hereafter."

[227] Hadith: "The rivers of Paradise gush forth from beneath hills or beneath mountains of musk." Al-'Uqayli reported it in *al-Du'afa'* from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah.

[228] Hadith: "If the adornment of the lowest of the people of Paradise were compared to the adornment of all the people of this world, what God adorns him with in the Hereafter would be better than the adornment of all the people of this world." Al-Tabarani reported it in *al-Awsat* from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah with a good chain.

[229] Hadith: "In Paradise there is a tree in whose shade a rider travels for a hundred years without traversing it..." Agreed upon from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah.

[230] Hadith of Abu Umamah: A Bedouin came and said, "O Messenger of God, God has mentioned in the Qur'an a harmful tree." He said, "What is it?" He said, "The lote-tree (al-Sidr)..." Ibn al-Mubarak reported it in *al-Zuhd* from Safwan ibn 'Amr from Sulaym ibn 'Amir as a *mursal* report, without mention of Abu Umamah.

[231] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "Whoever enters Paradise enjoys bliss and does not suffer misery; his garments do not wear out..." Muslim reported it without the phrase, "In Paradise is what no eye has seen..." The two Shaykhs [al-Bukhari and Muslim] agreed upon it from another hadith of Abu Hurayrah: God Almighty said, "I have prepared for My righteous servants what no eye has seen..."

[232] Hadith: A man said, "O Messenger of God, inform us about the garments of the people of Paradise. Are they created or woven?" ... Al-Nasa'i reported it from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr.

[233] Hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "The first group to enter Paradise will be in the likeness of the moon on the night of the full moon..." Agreed upon.

[234] Hadith concerning His saying, the Exalted, "They will be adorned therein with bracelets of gold" [18:31]. He said, "Upon them are crowns; the smallest pearl therein illuminates what is between the east and the west." Al-Tirmidhi reported it from the hadith of Abu Sa'id without mentioning the verse, and said, "We do not know it except from the hadith of Rashid ibn Sa'd."

[235] Hadith: "The tent is a hollow pearl, its height in the sky is sixty miles..." The author attributed it to al-Bukhari, and it is agreed upon from the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

[236] Hadith of Abu Sa'id concerning His saying, the Exalted, "And raised couches" [88:13]. He said, "The distance between two couches is like the distance between the heaven and the earth." Al-Tirmidhi reported it with the wording, "their height is like the distance between the heaven and the earth," and said it is *gharib*; we do not know it except from the hadith of Rashid ibn Sa'd.

[237] Hadith of Thawban: "A scholar from the scholars of the Jews came..." and he mentioned his question until he said, "So who are the first people to cross, meaning over the Bridge (al-Sirat)?" He said, "The poor emigrants." The Jew said, "Then what is their gift when..."

They will enter Paradise. Ziyadah said: "The hadith narrated by Muslim includes additions at its beginning and end."

[238] Hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam: A man from the Jews came and said, "O Abu al-Qasim, do you not claim that the people of Paradise will eat and drink therein?" ... In it is mentioned: "Their need is a sweat that flows from their skins like musk." Narrated by al-Nasa'i in al-Kubra with a sound chain.

[239] Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: "You will indeed see a bird in Paradise and desire it, and it will fall before you roasted." Narrated by al-Bazzar with a sound chain. [In it is 'sa'f' (a type of drink).]

[240] Hadith of Hudhayfah: "In Paradise there are birds like al-Bukhati (camels)..." A rare narration from Hudhayfah. Ahmad has from the hadith of Anas with a sound chain: "The birds of Paradise are like al-Bukht (a type of camel), grazing in the trees of Paradise." Abu Bakr said, "O Messenger of Allah, these birds are delightful." He said, "Those who eat them are more delightful than them." He said this three times. "And I hope that you will be among those who eat from them." It is also with al-Tirmidhi from another source, mentioning the River Kawthar and stating: "Birds whose necks are like the necks of camels." 'Umar said, "These are indeed delightful..." It does not mention Abu Bakr. He (al-Tirmidhi) said it is *hasan*.

[241] Hadith: "A morning or an evening in the path of Allah is better than the world and all that is in it." Narrated by al-Bukhari from the hadith of Anas.

[242] Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri regarding His saying, the Exalted: "As if they were rubies and coral." He said: "You look at her face in her veil, clearer than a mirror..." Narrated by Abu Ya'la from the narration of Abu al-Haytham from Abu Sa'id with a *hasan* chain. Ahmad also narrated it, containing Ibn Lahi'ah. Ibn al-Mubarak narrated it in *al-Zuhd wa al-Raqa'iq* from the narration of Abu al-Haytham from the Prophet (ﷺ) as a *mursal* report without mentioning Abu Sa'id. Al-Tirmidhi has from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: "The woman from the women of the people of Paradise—the whiteness of the marrow of her shinbone is seen from behind seventy garments..." He also narrated it from him as a *mawquf* report and said, "This is more authentic." In the two *Sahihs* from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: "For every man among them are two wives; the marrow of their shins is seen from behind the flesh."

[243] Hadith of Anas: "When I was taken on the Night Journey, I entered a place in Paradise called al-Sarh, upon which were tents of pearl, green chrysolite, and red ruby..." In it, Jibril said, "These are the secluded ones in the tents," and they began to say, "We are the pleased ones, so we are not displeased." I did not find it complete like this. Al-Tirmidhi has from the hadith of 'Ali: "In Paradise is a gathering place for the *hur al-'in*; they raise voices the like of which creation has never heard, saying, 'We are the everlasting ones, so we do not perish; we are the blissful ones, so we do not grieve; we are the pleased ones, so we are not displeased. Blessed is he for whom we are, and we are for him.'" He said it is *gharib*. Abu al-Shaykh has in *Kitab al-'Azamah* a hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa with a weak chain: "They gather every seven days and say with voices..." [similar to the above].

[244] Hadith: A man said, "O Messenger of Allah, do the people of Paradise have intercourse?" He said, "A man among them is given, in a single day, strength better than that of seventy of you." Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, who graded it *sahih*, and by Ibn Hibban from the hadith of Anas: "The believer in Paradise is given the strength for such-and-such amount of intercourse." It was said, "Will he be able for that?" He said, "He is given the strength of a hundred."

[245] Hadith: "A man from the people of Paradise will marry five hundred *huris*, four thousand virgins, and eight thousand previously married women; he will embrace each one of them for the measure of his lifespan in the world." Narrated by Abu al-Shaykh in *Tabaqat al-Muhaddithin* and in *Kitab al-'Azamah* from the hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa, except that he said "one hundred *huris*" and did not mention his embracing them. Its chain is weak, and it was preceded earlier by a hadith.

[246] Hadith: "In Paradise there is a market in which there is no buying or selling, except images of men and women..." Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in two places from the hadith of 'Ali. Some of it was mentioned earlier, two hadiths before this.

[247] Hadith of Anas: "The *huris* in Paradise sing, saying, 'We are the beautiful *huris*, kept for noble husbands.'" Narrated by al-Tabarani in *al-Awsat*. In it is al-Hasan ibn Dawud ibn al-Munkadir. Al-Bukhari said, "They speak about him." Ibn 'Adi said, "I hope there is no harm in him."

[248] Hadith of Abu Umamah: "There is no servant who enters Paradise except that two from the *hur al-'in* sit at his head and at his feet, singing to him with the most beautiful sound heard by mankind and jinn, and it is not with the flute of Satan, but with the praise and glorification of Allah." Narrated by al-Tabarani with a *hasan* chain.

[249] The hadith of Usamah ibn Zayd: "Is there not one who strives for Paradise? For Paradise has no equal..." Reported by Ibn Majah and Ibn Hibban.

[250] The hadith: A man came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said, "Are there horses in Paradise? For they amaze me..." Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of Buraydah with a difference in wording, and in it is al-Mas'udi, who is disputed. Ibn al-Mubarak reported it in al-Zuhd with the wording of the author from the narration of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Sabit, as a mursal report. Al-Tirmidhi said, "This is more sound." Abu Musa al-Madini mentioned 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Sabit in the supplement to Ibn Mandah's work on the Companions, but his companionship is not established.

[251] The hadith of Abu Sa'id: "Verily, a man among the people of Paradise will have a child born to him as he desires, and its pregnancy, weaning, and growth will be in a single hour." Reported by Ibn Majah and al-Tirmidhi, who said it is hasan gharib. He said, "The scholars have differed concerning this. Some said there is intercourse in Paradise but no offspring." Ahmad has from the hadith of Abu Razin: "They will enjoy and touch like your enjoyments in this world, and they will take pleasure in you, except that there is no procreation."

[252] The hadith: "When the people of Paradise are settled, friends will long for friends, so the couch of this one will journey to the couch of that one." Reported by al-Bazzar from the narration of al-Rabi' ibn Sabih from al-Hasan from Anas, who said, "We do not know it to be narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) except by this chain; Anas alone narrated it." Al-Rabi' ibn Sabih is very weak. Al-Isfahani reported it in al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib as a mursal report without mentioning Anas.

[253] The hadith: "The people of Paradise are hairless, beardless, fair, with curly hair and kohl-lined eyes, like sons of thirty-three..." Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of Mu'adh, and he graded it hasan, except for the phrases "fair, with curly hair" and "in the form of Adam..." to the end. He also reported it from the narration of Abu Hurayrah in a concise form: "The people of Paradise are hairless, beardless, with kohl-lined eyes," and said it is gharib. In the two Sahih collections from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "...in the form of their father Adam, sixty cubits tall."

[254] The hadith: "The lowest in station among the people of Paradise is he who has eighty thousand servants..." Reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of Abu Sa'id, disconnected from its beginning to his saying, "...and upon them are crowns," and from here with its chain also. He said, "We do not know it except from the hadith of Rashd ibn Sa'd."

[255] The hadith: "I looked into Paradise and saw that a pomegranate from its pomegranates was like the hide of a laden camel, and its birds were like al-Bukht..." Reported by al-Tha'labi in his Tafsir from the narration of Abu Harun al-'Abdi from Abu Sa'id. Abu Harun's name is 'Imarah ibn Jurayth, who is very weak. In the two Sahih collections from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "Allah says, 'I have prepared for My righteous servants what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to the heart of any human being.'"

[256] The hadith of Jarir: "We were sitting with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he saw the moon on the night of the full moon and said, 'You will see your Lord...'" It is in the two Sahih collections as mentioned by the author.

[257] The hadith of Suhayb concerning His saying, Exalted is He: "For those who do good is the best reward and extra..." Reported by Muslim as mentioned by the author.

[258] The hadith: "The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) loved optimism." Agreed upon from the narration of Anas within a hadith: "...and I love good optimism and a good word." Both have from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "...and the better of them is the one with good optimism." He said, "The good word one of you hears."

[259] The hadith: "Verily, Allah, Exalted is He, has one hundred mercies. He sent down one mercy among the jinn and mankind..." Reported by Muslim from the narrations of Abu Hurayrah and Salman.

[260] The hadith: "On the Day of Resurrection, Allah will bring out a book from beneath the Throne, in which is: 'My mercy has preceded My wrath...'" Agreed upon from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "When Allah decreed the creation, He wrote with Him above the Throne: 'My mercy has preceded My wrath'"—the wording of al-Bukhari. Muslim said: "He wrote in His Book concerning Himself: 'My mercy overcomes My wrath.'"

[261] The hadith: "Allah will reveal Himself to us on the Day of Resurrection, smiling, and will say, 'Receive glad tidings, O community of Muslims, for there is not one of you except that I have placed in his stead in the Fire a Jew or a Christian.'" Reported by Muslim from the narration of Abu Musa: "On the Day of Resurrection, Allah will give to every Muslim a Jew or a Christian and say, 'This is your ransom from the Fire.'" Abu Dawud has: "My nation is a nation shown mercy; there is no punishment for it in the Hereafter."

As for the beginning of the Hadith, Al-Tabarani narrated it from the narration of Abu Musa as well: "Our Lord, God, will reveal Himself to us on the Day of Resurrection, smiling, until they look upon His Countenance, and they will fall down in prostration to Him. Then He will say: 'Raise your heads; this is not a day for worship.'" In its chain is 'Ali ibn Zayd ibn Jad'an.

[262] Hadith: "God will grant Adam intercession on the Day of Resurrection for one hundred thousand thousand and ten thousand thousand of his progeny." Al-Tabarani transmitted it from the narration of Anas with a weak chain.

[263] Hadith: "Indeed, God the Exalted will say on the Day of Resurrection to the believers: 'Did you love to meet Me?' They will say: 'Yes.'" The Hadith was transmitted by Ahmad and Al-Tabarani from the narration of Mu'adh with a weak chain.

[264] Hadith: "God, Mighty and Majestic, will say on the Day of Resurrection: 'Bring out from the Fire whoever remembered Me for a day or feared Me in a standing.'" Al-Tirmidhi transmitted it from the narration of Anas and said it is Hasan Gharib.

[265] Hadith: "When the people of the Fire are gathered in the Fire, and among them, by God's will, are some from the people of the Qiblah, the disbelievers will say to the Muslims: 'Were you not Muslims?' They will say: 'Yes.' They will say: 'What did your Islam avail you, since you are with us in the Fire?'" The Hadith is concerning the extraction of the people of the Qiblah from the Fire. Then the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) recited: "Often will those who disbelieve wish that they had been Muslims." Al-Nasa'i transmitted it in Al-Kubra from the narration of Jabir, something similar, with a sound chain.

[266] Hadith: "God is more merciful to His believing servant than a compassionate mother is to her child." Agreed upon from the narration of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. At its beginning is the story of the woman from the captives who found an infant among the captives, took him, pressed him to her belly, and suckled him.

[267] Hadith: "A caller from beneath the Throne will call out on the Day of Resurrection: 'O community of Muhammad! As for what was due to Me from you, I have forgiven it for you. But the mutual claims remain, so forgive one another and enter Paradise by My mercy.'" We narrated it in the *Sab'iyyat* of Abu al-As'ad al-Qushayri from the narration of Anas. In its chain is al-Husayn ibn Dawud al-Balkhi. Al-Khatib said: "He is not trustworthy."

[268] Hadith of al-Sunabihi from 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit: "Whoever testifies that there is no god but God and that Muhammad is the Messenger of God, God has forbidden him to the Fire." Muslim transmitted it from this avenue, and the two Shaykhs agreed upon it from other than the narration of al-Sunabihi with a different wording.

[269] Hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr: "Indeed, God will single out a man from my community before all creation on the Day of Resurrection, and ninety-nine scrolls will be unfurled for him..." Then he mentioned the Hadith of the Card (al-Bitaqah). Ibn Majah and Al-Tirmidhi transmitted it, and he said it is Hasan Gharib.

[270] Hadith: "Indeed, God will say to the angels: 'Whoever you find in his heart an atom's weight of good, bring him out from the Fire.' So they will bring out a great multitude." The Hadith is concerning the extraction of the monotheists, and His saying, Exalted is He: "Then I shall never be displeased with you thereafter forever." The two transmitted it in the *Sahihayn* as mentioned by the author from the narration of Abu Sa'id.

[271] Hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: "The nations were presented to me. A prophet would pass by with one man, and a prophet with two men, and a prophet with no one with him..." The Hadith up to his saying: "'Ukkashah has preceded you with it." Al-Bukhari narrated it.

[272] Hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm al-Ansari: "The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) was absent from us for three days; he would not go out except for the obligatory prayer, then he would return." In it: "Indeed, my Lord promised me that He would admit from my community into Paradise seventy thousand without any reckoning against them." And in it: "He gave me, with each one of the seventy thousand, seventy thousand." Al-Bayhaqi transmitted it in *Al-Ba'th wa al-Nushur*. And in the version of Ahmad and Abu Ya'la from the narration of Abu Bakr: "He increased me, with each one, seventy thousand." In its chain is an unnamed man. And in the version of Ahmad and Al-Tabarani in *Al-Awsat* from the narration of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr: "So 'Umar said: 'Why did you not ask for more?' He said: 'I did ask for more, and He gave me, with each man, seventy thousand.' 'Umar said: 'Why did you not ask for more?' He said: 'I did ask for more, and He gave me like this'—and 'Abdullah ibn Abi Bakr spread his hands before him." 'Abdullah said: "And he spread his forearms and scooped with them." In its chain is Musa ibn 'Ubaydah al-Randi, who is weak.

[273] Hadith of Abu Dharr: "Gabriel met me on the side of Al-Harrah and said: 'Give glad tidings to your community that whoever dies not associating anything with God will enter Paradise.'" Agreed upon with the wording: "Gabriel came to me and gave me glad tidings." And in a narration of the two: "A messenger from my Lord came to me."

[274] Hadith of Abu al-Darda': "The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) recited: 'But for him who fears the standing before his Lord, there will be two Gardens.' So I said..."

And if he commits adultery or steals—a hadith narrated by Ahmad with a sound chain.

[275] A hadith: On the Day of Resurrection, a man from the people of other religions will be delivered to every believer, and it will be said to him, "This is your ransom from the Fire." Narrated by Muslim in a similar version from Abu Musa, as previously mentioned.

[276] A hadith from Abu Burdah: He reported to 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz from his father Abu Musa from the Prophet (peace be upon him), who said, "No Muslim dies but that God places a Jew or a Christian in his stead in the Fire." The author attributed it to Muslim's narration, and so it is.

[277] A hadith: A boy was standing in one of the military expeditions, being offered for bidding on an extremely hot summer day. A woman caught sight of him—the hadith—and in it: "God is more merciful to all of you than this woman is to her son." Agreed upon in a concise form with variations. From the hadith of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: He said, "Some captives were brought to the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), and among them was a woman from the captives running about. When she found a boy among the captives, she took him, pressed him to her belly, and breastfed him. The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said to us, 'Do you think this woman would cast her child into the Fire?' We said, 'No, by God, she would not, while she is able not to cast him.' The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said, 'God is more merciful to His servants than this woman is to her child.'" The wording is from Muslim. Al-Bukhari said: "And there was a woman from the captives whose breast was flowing with milk, running about when she found a boy"—the hadith.

And praise be to God Almighty, returning to the beginning, and prayers and peace be upon our master Muhammad in every movement and stillness.

Its author, 'Abd al-Rahim ibn al-Husayn al-'Iraqi, says: I completed the draft of this composition in the year 761 and finished transcribing this summary from it on Monday, the 12th of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 790. It is concluded.
